## 2026-05-15 — Elder Gods Council ingest (largest single ingest in wiki history)

Eight-pass ingest of the 2026-05-15 raw drop from Elder Gods chat 1.txt — seven triples + a chronology single + a meta voice reference. Plus the previously-dropped Imma quad with A1 corrections applied at ingest. **20 new pages created**, multiple existing pages substantially updated. User decisions A1, A2, B1, B2 and questions 1–6 all applied at ingest time. 0 ERRORs throughout.

### User-locked corrections applied at ingest

- **A1 — Ascension mechanism**: Elder Gods do not elevate Ascended Mortal Deities. Ascension is mortal threshold-crossing + divine acknowledgement. Applied at `imma.md` (Sylph acknowledged, did not elevate; Imma may have misread acknowledgement as elevation) and at `velveth.md` (Kathira's Ascension came through crossing the love/betrayal/duty threshold + divine acknowledgement). Will land prominently on `gods-of-eadras.md` Ascended Mortal section in next-pass cleanup.
- **A1 — Velveth = Kathira Spellsinger of House Valtharion**, fiancée to Emperor Thoramis Firethorn. *Spellsinger* is earned cognomen; *Valtharion* is the actual house. Replaces the Meleth-Vaethari claim. Named both figures for first time in canon at `velveth.md`, `great-betrayal.md` (Summary, Necessary Hand section, How She Is Remembered, Emperor's name preservation), and cross-references throughout.
- **B1 — Cycle period**: 10,000 years final. `night-sky-cosmology.md` continues to use 10k figure; cosmology-stars-mythoi's 26k figure not adopted.
- **B2 — Hypothetical-Sixth-Wielder principles**: Kept "Deception Remains the Primary Tool Against Gods" only. Dropped "Perfection as Ultimate Form of Destruction" and "Mobility Changes Threat-Nature."
- **#2 — Truncated `05_faedanarr_*.txt`**: moved to `raw/deprecated/`; not deleted.
- **#3 — `ivine-council-*` filename typo**: renamed to `divine-council-*`.
- **#4 — Voice Reference**: saved as memory at `reference-elder-gods-voices.md` for future dialogue generation.
- **#5 — First Rebrightening / FR dating**: semi-formal (Sharanel/Tome/Lirran clergy register). Documented at `first-rebrightening.md`.
- **#6 — Open Palm + Unheld Hand**: coexist as reform + original. Documented at `doctrine-of-open-palm.md`.

### Pass 1 — Framing layer

Created **`first-rebrightening.md`** (the current era; FR dating semi-formal; five characteristic features of the era) and **`baldaranic-council-cycle.md`** (the divine deliberation framework — Convocation of the Reopened Ledger — with three phases: Open Palm Council, Arathi Council, Demon War Council). Established the conceptual scaffolding all subsequent passes plug into.

### Pass 2 — Demon War triple

Substantial surgical update to **`demon-war.md`**: survived-not-won framing, demon-vs-devil distinction (devils are infernal bureaucracy; demons are alien-Mythos energivores from Nethar/Vorath); Demon Prince of the Open Wound as adaptive sovereign appetite; Xar'vion under tiered disclosure (Public Doctrine / Vowed Scholarship / Sealed Judgment); imprisonment as not-clean compromise; corrected Anti-Magic Crusade causal chain; addition of the Unreceived section. Created **`unreceived.md`** (souls consumed wholly by demons + 5 rituals: Empty Cot Vigil, Unreceived Ledger, Black Banner Roll, Laugh With No Echo, Ashless Shrines; "May theft be remembered" as anchoring phrase) and **`woundwatch.md`** (proposed institutional patrol for Demonfall Marches; *The Wound That Must Not Be Fed* doctrine; Beast-Folk laughter-houses as defensive infrastructure). Corrected `magic-in-eadras.md` Netharim-prevalence error: Netharim are *distant third* (Wizards > Priests > Netharim > Lexanari), not most prominent. Added magic-user population hierarchy section.

### Pass 3 — Open Palm + Divine Bureaucracy

Created four new pages: **`doctrine-of-open-palm.md`** (reformist correction to Unheld Hand — *the Hand remains unheld; it shall not be absent*; primordial warning *do not fill the space we opened*; five mortal theologies: Orthodox Unheld / Empty Palm Lament / Stewardship Compact / Wild Refusal / Bold Revision); **`three-bells-of-intervention.md`** (mortals act → institutions fail → continuity threatened; *permitted does not mean guaranteed*); **`hearth-witness-mandate.md`** (mortal/recently-mortal auditors empowered to observe consequence not procedure; controversy over recently-dead-souls service); **`petition-of-abandoned-circumstance.md`** (formal afterlife procedure for souls to accuse divine offices of negligence; high denial rate by design preserves doctrinal tension).

### Pass 4 — Arathi Geo-Substrate (deep retcon)

Created five new pages: **`arathi-geo-substrate.md`** (Arathi "crystals" reframed as bio-engineered living/semi-living earth-matter — five clades: Saelith Choir, Veyruun Bone, Ishkara Vein, Thamrite Mirror, Oru-Sha War; pre-Cataclysm Eadras had **no active plate tectonics** — modern tectonics post-Cataclysm; Context-Bound Relics; revised Deep Vault Classification with substrate condition; 8 common mortal errors); **`vault-concordat.md`** (international framework for vault exploration); **`fallback-doctrine.md`** (*no life-supporting system without mortal-scale fallback*; six derived institutions including Entropy Taboo and Festival of Broken Certainties); **`unsealing-oath.md`** (three witnesses: knowledge, consequence, the unborn); **`absence-traditions.md`** (formal Absence Theology refuses invented continuity: *we do not remember, and this too is true*; four-stage development).

### Pass 5 — Unicorns retcon

Substantial rewrite of **`unicorns.md`**: individuality is temporary, herd is permanent; original hive mind; stallion = guardian of departure, alpha mare = guardian of return; Great Exchange taught individuality (*selfhood was the dragon-gift and the dragon-wound*); First Strays brought personal testimony into herd-deep memory; five memory layers (Herd-Deep, Returned Self, Held-Apart, Dragon-Touched, Wound-Kept); herd as trauma-healer (*they do not return to forget; they return so memory can stop bleeding*); three life patterns (Herd-Bound, Seasonal Strayers, Long Strayers — Long Strayer as **tragedy not perfection**). Sources line cleaned up (was corrupted with massive duplication of "user direction 2026-05-13" entry; now clean). Created three companion pages: **`herd-listeners.md`** (rare mortals permitted by herds to translate wound-memory into mortal institutional language; FR 22 formal recognition), **`unicorn-wound-keeping.md`** (herd-memory discipline preserving wound-recognition; *knowledge treated as hazard, not asset*), **`circling-of-the-returned.md`** (quarantine-and-reintegration rite for returning Strayers, with exile/sleep/death/long-wandering as possible outcomes).

### Pass 6 — Faedanar

Created five new pages: **`fae-da-nar.md`** (hidden Woodkin society of the Frontier; survival through coexistence with humans; *Fae-da'Nar does not ask whether the individual is precious; it knows the individual is precious — then it asks whether keeping them alive will kill everyone else*); **`four-laws-of-fae-da-nar.md`** (don't frighten humans / don't interfere / oppose Shunned threats / obey Druids); **`the-shunned.md`** (predatory races outside the compact; functional category, not racial); **`frontier-hospitality.md`** (human-side of the compact: First Bowl / No Iron on the Table / Fair Measure Under Witness / No Mocking the Mask / Guest-Fire Peace; Peace-Brass and Guest-Bronze; the Iron Paradox *iron at table is threat, iron in trade is consent*); **`threshold-cities.md`** (five-stage growth pattern from Guest-Bowl Settlement to Severed City; five long-term endpoints — Faithful, Ceremonial, Severed Expansion, Ruined Caution, Relocated; *trust begins with faces; cities spend it as coin*). The truncated `05_faedanarr_*.txt` was moved to `raw/deprecated/` pre-ingest; the better-formatted faedanar triple supersedes it.

### Pass 7 — Imma + Velveth (with A1 corrections)

Created three new pages, the largest cross-page-impact ingest of the day: **`imma.md`** (Imma Who-Did-Not-Stop-Laughing; **A1 correction applied**: Sylph acknowledged her divinity, did not elevate her; Imma may have misread acknowledgement as elevation; mortal name Imma Brella-of-the-Wagon-and-the-Cup; office in Solarion with wagon-wheel sigil and loaf+bowl porch; cups on desk marking integrated soul-lives; portfolio of daily-laughter-feeding-the-Weave + daily Veil renewal); **`velveth.md`** (Velrathi goddess of love/betrayal/duty; **A1 correction applied**: Velveth = **Kathira Spellsinger of House Valtharion**, fiancée to **Emperor Thoramis Firethorn**, the last Tarran Emperor; Spellsinger is earned cognomen, Valtharion is actual house; Ascension via threshold-crossing + divine acknowledgement; office three doors from Imma's; silent corridor nod; institutional portfolio of Velrathi vow-prayers, oath-arbitration, duty-against-love cases); **`decree-of-shali-shani-ioa.md`** (cosmic decree binding gods to silence on unrecoverable cosmological endings — Chaos-unmaking, demonic consumption, spirit-destruction; the Curator-Not-Speaker Loophole permits the Tome to *show* what the gods may not *speak*; load-bearing kindness, not paternalism).

Substantial update to **`great-betrayal.md`**: Emperor Thoramis Firethorn and Kathira Spellsinger of House Valtharion named for first time in canon; "Kathira Spellsinger" added to How She Is Remembered table alongside historical names; Velveth reveal explicitly connected; Spellsinger cognomen explained; Velena's death added as personal-context for Kathira's acceptance of the divine task; folk-comfort fiction reading of Veyr'Keth legends documented as compatible with Velveth Ascension.

## 2026-05-14 (sixth) — Magic-system make-it-mine pass: Sorcerers/Weavespinners fully expunged

User directive: *We need to fully expunge all references to deprecated sorcerers and weavspinners.* Executed as the make-it-mine pass for the entire Sorcerer/Weave/Weavespinner system that had been deferred since the 2026-05-09 ingest. The pass introduced substantial new canon and swept terminology across 53 files.

### User-canonised new framings

Three sentences from the user established the new framework:

1. **Anti-Magic Crusade** — the Sorcerer Crusade is renamed and rescoped: it was a **crusade against all magic as wicked**, not a sorcerer-targeted persecution. Broadens the historical impact: the Crusade targeted wizards, druids, [[netharim|Netharim]], [[lexanari|Lexanari]], priests of disfavored gods, hedge-witches, and folk-magicians under a single *Cold Hearth* doctrine. The new doctrine: *the Demon War proved magic to be a world-ending force; all magic therefore wicked; all magic users targets*.
2. **Windspeakers** — Weavespinners are renamed and reframed. Windspeakers are **[[netharim|Netharim]] born with greater innate capacity than their peers, with the heavy duty of anchoring the conduit junctions** of the [[seven-conduits|Seven Conduits]]. They are not a separate order — they are Netharim, members of [[order-sharanel|Order Sharanel]] — but the magnitude of their innate gift and the gravity of the duty distinguish them. They are geographically bound to their junctions; the duty consumes their lives; they cannot retire.
3. **The Weave** — major reframe. The Weave is now **a purely defensive cosmological structure** (not a creative/transmissive substrate), it **carries [[eldritch|Eldritch]]** (new connection), it is **sustained by the lives of every magic user in Eadras** (broader sustenance: every practising mage's life contributes), and **Windspeakers anchor the conduit junctions** within it (load-bearing structural function).

The user also clarified: **Netharim are the members of Order Sharanel**. The Order is the institution; Netharim are its members.

### Pages created (3)

- **`wiki/windspeakers.md`** — Full new page for the renamed role. Documents the Netharim-with-greater-innate-capacity framing, the conduit-junction-anchoring duty, the geographic binding, the life-consuming exertion, the cosmological succession mechanism, the strategic importance, and the historical significance (Three Unanchorings during the Anti-Magic Crusade producing the Thousand-Year Dimming).
- **`wiki/anti-magic-crusade.md`** — Full new page replacing the old Sorcerer Crusade. Documents the *Cold Hearth* doctrine; the Black Hand engineering (preserved, with the Spear-search-diversion canon intact); the avatar intervention (preserved, with Lirra detecting Weave degradation as the trigger); the Three Unanchorings (renamed from Three Unspinnings, mechanism preserved); the Thousand-Year Dimming; the tiers-of-knowledge table (updated for the broader magic-user-sustains-Weave canon); the political revolution against tower rule (Windspeaker-rule version).
- **`wiki/order-sworn-netharim.md`** — Renamed and elevated from a deprecation stub to a live page about the Sworn-Oath tier of Order Sharanel. Documents what the Oath does (binds for life, grants the Sworn Eye amulet, opens narrow priestly-magic access), what it does not do, why most graduates do not Swear, and the distinguishing markers.

### Pages substantially rewritten (3)

- **[[magic-in-eadras]]** — Removed `partial-rework-pending` banner; rewrote the Four Major Orders section (added Lexanari, replaced Sorcerers with Netharim, updated Wizards); completely rewrote The Weave section (purely defensive, carries Eldritch, sustained by every magic user, Windspeakers anchor junctions); deleted the seven-spheres section (sorcerous composition framework retired); updated cross-links.
- **[[order-sharanel]]** — Removed `rework-pending` banner; framed as the order whose members are Netharim; updated the founding to *capacity conferred on ten thousand mortals* rather than *transmuted into sorcerers*; rewrote the *Netharim as Living Sustainers of the Weave* section to reflect the new "every magic user sustains the Weave" canon; updated the grade structure (Lirrian Councilor seven-per-Tower preserved as institutional fact, but the seven-sphere assignments retired; Voice of Lirra reframed as the leadership-coordination title carried by senior Windspeakers); updated all cross-references.
- **[[weavespinners]]** — Stub updated to point to [[windspeakers]] as the active canon replacement rather than describing the deprecated mechanism.

### Pages deleted (2)

- **`wiki/sorcerer-crusade.md`** — Deleted. Content replaced by `anti-magic-crusade.md`.
- **`wiki/order-sworn-sorcerers.md`** — Deleted. The concept survives at `order-sworn-netharim.md` under the renamed framing.

### Terminology sweep (53 files, 331 substitutions)

Built `sweep_sorcerer_to_netharim.py` as a Python sweep script. Dry-ran first, then applied. Replacements:

- `Sorcerer Crusade` / `sorcerer-crusade` (in wikilinks) → `Anti-Magic Crusade` / `anti-magic-crusade`
- `[[weavespinners|...]]` / `[[weavespinners]]` → `[[windspeakers|...]]` / `[[windspeakers]]`
- `Weavespinners` / `Weavespinner` / `weavespinners` / `weavespinner` → `Windspeakers` / `Windspeaker` / `windspeakers` / `windspeaker`
- `Sorcerers` / `Sorcerer` / `sorcerers` / `sorcerer` → `Netharim`
- `Sorcery` / `sorcery` → `Netharim practice`
- `Sorcerous` / `sorcerous` → `Netharim`

Excluded from the sweep:

- `log.md` (append-only history)
- `inspirations.md` (Galloway *Sorcerer apparatus* historical-influence record)
- `tags.md` (canonical tag taxonomy; updated by hand to retire the `sorcerer` modifier tag)
- The four newly-written pages (`anti-magic-crusade.md`, `magic-in-eadras.md`, `order-sharanel.md`, `windspeakers.md`) which already used the new canon
- The deprecation stubs (`dashar.md`, `weavespinners.md`, `heart-of-the-goddess.md`) which describe what the concepts *were*

### Post-sweep manual fixes

The sweep over-corrected in a few places that required manual repair:

- **5 broken `[[order-sworn-Netharim]]` wikilinks** (capitalised-N slug from the sweep hitting `order-sworn-sorcerers`'s display text) — fixed across `index.md`, `lirra.md` (×3), and `open-questions.md` to point to `[[order-sworn-netharim|Order-Sworn Netharim]]` (the new lowercase slug).
- **Self-referential meta-statements in `worldbuilding-needs.md` and `open-questions.md`** that the sweep had mangled (e.g., *"the Galloway-derived Netharim order"* — the Galloway-derived order was Sorcerers, not Netharim) — manually rewritten to mark the magic-system rework as *COMPLETED 2026-05-14* with the previously-rework-pending items marked **RESOLVED** with strikethrough.
- **`magic-in-eadras.md` line 39** — *"governance over magic and sorcery"* — trimmed to *"governance over magic"*.
- **`magic-in-eadras.md` line 98** — *"Weavespinner sanctums"* → *"[[windspeakers|Windspeaker]] sanctums"*.
- **`tags.md`** — removed the `sorcerer` modifier tag from the canonical taxonomy (no pages currently use it).

### Open canon (post-rework)

The rework leaves these items still open for later development:

- **The succession mechanism for Windspeakers** — what coordinates the timing of identification and assignment to junctions (direct Lirran selection, Voroik weaving, Bureaucracy prophetic-office coordination, or self-organising properties of the Weave-conduit system).
- **The exact division of domains across the seven Lirrian Councilors** at each Tower of Lirra.
- **How the Voice-of-Lirra title circulates among Windspeaker ranks.**
- **Whether a Windspeaker can refuse the duty.**
- **The specific procedural mechanics of an Oath-of-Service breach** that doesn't rise to full Order removal.
- **What containment looks like for a future magic-user catastrophe** if the Weave's defensive function ever fully fails.

### Final lint state

0 ERRORs. 26 WARNs (all pre-existing known/false-positive items: sealed-page Summary convention, log historical references inside backtick-quoted bug-name documentation, inspirations.md template HTML-comment). 5 INFO orphans (4 rpg/* pages by design, 1 planewalkers.md as the residual real orphan).

The wiki canon-content is now fully scrubbed of the deprecated *sorcerer* / *Weavespinner* / *Sorcerer Crusade* terminology. The only remaining mentions are in `log.md` (preserved per user), `inspirations.md` (Galloway-influence record), and the source-line metadata of the four newly-written pages (which document the rework's user-direction provenance).

## 2026-05-14 (fifth) — Deprecated-content cleanup

Executed the *ALL deprecated content* cleanup directive across the wiki. Distinguished mechanical fixes from content decisions and acted accordingly.

### Mechanical fixes applied

- **`wiki/xarvion.md` — "Tower of Stars" residue removed.** The Ascension section was still naming the Velrathi arcane stronghold as the *Tower of Stars*, a name retired from canon during the 2026-05-13 spear-prison-sequence revision. Rewrote the section to describe the stronghold as a major Velrathi arcane site without committing to the retired name. The stronghold itself remains canonical; the name does not.
- **`wiki/_sealed/fourth-attempt-impalement.md` — *body of the Mythos* phrasing replaced.** Per `feedback-mythos-terminology` (2026-05-06), *body of the Mythos* is deprecated phrasing. Rewrote the alien-artifact-principle section to use *the Mythos itself* and *wounding the Mythos* — preserving the meaning while using canonical phrasing.

### Sealed page deleted

- **`wiki/_sealed/fourth-hiding-place.md` — DELETED.** Symmetric with the flesh-crafters erasure pattern. The previously-canonical Pacific-conclave / Self-Crowned / Voroik-key version of the Spear's fourth hiding was deprecated on 2026-05-13 when the new sealed canon ([[_sealed/fourth-attempt-impalement|fourth-attempt-impalement.md]]) took its place. The deprecated sealed page was preserved as historical record for one day, then erased per the user's *ALL deprecated content* directive.
- **`wiki/_sealed/README.md` — entry removed.** The fourth-hiding-place bullet was removed from the *Current contents* list and replaced with an HTML comment marking the deletion and the reasoning.
- Two inbound references in `_sealed/fourth-attempt-impalement.md` (the *Replaces* line at the top and an open-canon item about the previously-canonical Pacific conclave material) were rewritten to describe the deletion in prose rather than wikilink to the now-gone page.

### Stubbed-out: 4 magic-system pages

For four pages whose narrative described pre-2026-05-09 Sorcerer/Weave concepts that no longer exist as canon, replaced the full narrative with a deprecation stub that (a) preserves the slug so existing wikilinks resolve, (b) carries `canon_status: [deprecated]`, (c) briefly states what the concept WAS, and (d) points to active-canon replacements:

- **`wiki/dashar.md`** — Da'shar were transmuted sorcerers in the pre-rework Sorcerer/Weave system. Stubbed; points to [[netharim]], [[lexanari]], [[druids]].
- **`wiki/weavespinners.md`** — Weavespinners were the seven transmuted sorcerers stabilising the [[seven-conduits|Seven Conduits]]. Stubbed; notes the conduits themselves remain canonical and their governance under the reworked magic system is open canon.
- **`wiki/order-sworn-sorcerers.md`** — Order-Sworn Sorcerers were a sub-category within Order Sharanel under the old system. Stubbed; points to [[netharim]] and the surviving-in-reworked-form [[order-sharanel|Order Sharanel]].
- **`wiki/heart-of-the-goddess.md`** — Heart of the Goddess was a non-physical Weave-space concept. Stubbed; notes the Weave itself is candidate-for-removal in the make-it-mine pass.

The original narrative on each page is preserved in [[log]] under its original ingest entry (2026-04-29 / 2026-04-30); the user can reconstruct from the log if any future canon makes a stubbed concept relevant again.

### Kept-with-banner: 3 transitional magic-system pages

Three pages with `rework-pending` (or `partial-rework-pending`) status describe concepts/events that **survive the magic-system rework in some form** — their banners already distinguish what's deprecated from what's canonical. After review, the banners are doing the cleanup work; no further surgery needed.

- **`wiki/magic-in-eadras.md`** (partial-rework-pending) — The umbrella magic-system page. Banner clearly identifies the Sorcerer / Druid / Weave sections as superseded while preserving the broader canon. Kept.
- **`wiki/order-sharanel.md`** (rework-pending) — The Order's *institutional name, founding context, and historical role through the Sorcerer Crusade* all remain canonical; the underlying mechanism (Weave-strand sorcery → Netharim intuitive practice) is rework-pending. Banner is explicit about which is which. Kept.
- **`wiki/sorcerer-crusade.md`** (rework-pending) — The historical event itself remains canonical; only the underlying magical mechanics are open until the make-it-mine pass. Banner is explicit. Kept.

### Verified-clean items from the audit

- Velrothi → Velrathi rename (only in raw-source filename citations, which are immutable)

- *Weave-buffered Sourceflare* → atmosphere/magnetic-field filtering (no canon hits)

- Elyra / Elena → Velena (only in log)
- Salem → Witchfinder General Trials (only in retcon-documentation citations on [[dao]])
- Flesh-crafters body-horror canon (only in log; verified earlier today)
- *Body horror* in Chaos Crusades context (canonical, NOT flesh-crafters residue)
- *Ssar'veth* (canonically-preserved folk-corruption of Kudur-eṭir; documented; not deprecated)
- *Merfolk* (canonically-documented colloquial grouping term; not deprecated)

### Final lint state

0 ERRORs. 23 WARNs (all pre-existing known/false-positive items: sealed-page Summary convention, log historical references inside backtick-quoted bug-name documentation, inspirations.md template HTML-comment). 5 INFO orphans (4 rpg/* pages by design, 1 planewalkers.md as the residual real orphan).

## 2026-05-14 (fourth) — Principles of Eadras page created

Created a dedicated canonical home for the load-bearing principles that organise the setting, by user request: *"can you create a principles page defining the emerging principles underlying my setting?"*

### Pages created (1)

- **`wiki/principles-of-eadras.md`** — Two-part structure:
  - **Part I — In-world principles** (36 items, organised into seven subsections): I.A Cosmology and reality, I.B Spirits and metaphysical beings, I.C Gods and the divine, I.D Civilisation and institutions, I.E Magic and the natural order, I.F Anthropological texture, I.G Narrative and tone. These are canon facts about how Eadras works — true *inside* the world.
  - **Part II — Author-side craft principles** (8 items): the design discipline that emerged from building the setting — true about *how* the setting is built, not in-universe canon.
  - **Thematic spine** (7-word) and **anti-grimdark tonal frame** elevated to the top of the page above both parts.
  - Closing note on how the page is maintained: principles are *discovered*, not pre-decided; they are added once a candidate principle has cleared the *surfaces from more than one independent source* bar.

### Pages updated (2)

- **[[inspirations]]** — The *Setting-wide design principles* section was the de-facto home for the principles catalog (32 numbered items at last count). That section now consists of a brief pointer to [[principles-of-eadras|Principles of Eadras]] explaining that the catalog has moved. Inspirations.md returns to its original purpose: external-work influence cataloguing. Header sources line + Last updated refreshed.
- **[[index]]** — Added `[[principles-of-eadras]]` entry to the *Wiki Meta* section, immediately after `modernity`, with a one-line summary of the two-part structure and the anchoring thematic spine + tonal frame.

### Composition note (what got included)

The 32 principles formerly on [[inspirations]] are all preserved on the new page, redistributed across the in-world / craft split. The in-world principles are restated in their in-world framing (since most of the 32 already functioned as in-world canon and were only catalogued as craft principles because of where they happened to live). Several additional in-world principles emerged from the canon and have been added on the new page that were not formally in the 32:

- *Reality requires an observer* and *Eadras runs observer-hungry* (from [[observer-and-naming]])
- *The Mythos is bounded structure imposed within unreality* / *Chaos is the absence of reality, not a force* (from [[mythos]] and [[chaos]])
- *The alien-artifact principle* (from [[spear-of-crystallized-entropy]] — the gods cannot destroy / eject / hide it absolutely)
- *Spirits are Spirits* / *True form is a direct reflection of self-perception* / *Spirits cannot create life or new spirits* (from today's spirits-canon work on [[spirits]] and [[back-rooms]])
- *Gods deceive gods* and *Divine presence requires mediation* (from [[divine-containment-protocols]] and [[icons]])
- *The Doctrine of the Unheld Hand* (from [[doctrine-of-unheld-hand]])

The craft side preserves the original eight most-clearly-craft principles (cognitive-first design, multi-axial measurement, sacredness as emergent structure, antagonists as grammatical inversion, resonance as deep logic, aesthetic refusal of genre defaults, preserve form / reassign function, plus the benchmark question). Most of the others moved to Part I because they read more naturally as in-world facts about Eadras than as craft discipline (e.g., *bodily limitation as kindness*, *catastrophes are bigger than their catalysts*, *desire is dangerous geometry* are all stronger as canon than as craft notes).

### Maintenance going forward

Future principle-additions go on [[principles-of-eadras]], not on [[inspirations]]. The same *surfaces from more than one independent source* bar applies. When a principle surfaces from a new ingest, it's added once it clears that bar.

---

## 2026-05-14 (third) — Backrooms canon addition

(Cumulative entry for four user messages on 2026-05-14 expanding the Backrooms canon, from the initial paragraph through three follow-on clarifications.)

User-supplied canon paragraph elevating the back-rooms concept from a subsection of [[spirits]] to its own dedicated page, resolving the open-canon question raised on the spirits page itself ("Whether *back rooms* should be promoted to its own dedicated page").

### New canon from the supplied paragraphs

- The Backrooms are a **network of interconnected spaces** (a coherent connected infrastructure, not isolated rooms-per-realm)
- Designed for spirits of **all hierarchies**
- **Originally inspired by early mortal civilizations** (reverse-influence: divine infrastructure borrowed mortal social-architecture patterns)
- **Created with divine help** (which gods is open canon)
- Spirits **shed their shells and roles** here and **interact as equals** (egalitarian-by-design)
- Specific amenities: **lounges, locker rooms, dining areas serving mana in the form of food, serene parks** (indoor and outdoor-like)
- **Styled after [[arathi|Arathi]] [[crystalmancy]] and [[magitek]]** — major aesthetic/architectural canon with theological implications (the Backrooms cannot predate the Arathi era in their current form)
- **Secret from mortals** (second user message) — the Backrooms are an off-duty refuge *from mortal concerns specifically*; the secrecy is the defining condition of their function. Multiple enforcement layers: architectural concealment via [[limina|Limina]], soul-routing exclusion (souls of dead mortals are not routed through Backroom spaces), cultural reinforcement (spirits do not mention them to mortals), and Tome-curation (sealed at the esoteric tier). `knowledge_access` set to **esoteric** accordingly. A few Order Sharanel scholars at the deepest tier have *inferred* their existence from negative-space evidence but the specific canon is not in mortal scholarship.
- **Mana-as-food does both jobs** (third user message) — provides magical energy to the consuming spirit *and* has flavor. Spirits eat the food because it satisfies, not merely because it sustains. Cross-realm dishes are a known Backroom phenomenon; the elemental-plane Backrooms in particular reportedly produce the most distinctive cuisine. Resolves the prior open-canon item on whether mana-as-food was nutritional or purely cultural.
- **Cross-realm network spanning eight spirit realms** (third user message, corrected in fourth user message from "10 spirit realms" to **eight**) — the Backroom network is *one network*, not a collection of per-realm-isolated installations. The eight spirit realms it connects are **Celestia** (originally written as Solarion; user corrected on fifth user message to **Celestia**), **Nyxar**, **Feywild**, **Shadowdark**, and the **four elemental planes** (Fire, Water, Earth, Air). The Prime and [[limina|Limina]] are not spirit realms.
- **Hidden entrances in [[limina|Limina]]** (sixth user message) — the network is accessed through hidden entrances scattered throughout Limina. This composes elegantly with Limina's existing travel rule (a clearly articulated destination is required for Limina travel — see [[limina#Travel]]): a mortal who has not heard of the Backrooms cannot *articulate* them as a destination, so the access rule itself is the knowledge-gated lock. Cross-realm Backroom movement is therefore mediated by Limina at each segment-to-segment transition, not by walking through some cross-plane corridor.
- **Separate layer, spirits only** (eighth user message) — the Backrooms are **architecturally separated from each realm's normally accessible space**. They are *a separate metaphysical layer*, not a wing of any realm's regular geography. The layer is **for spirits only** — the combination of separate-layer architecture, the Limina access lock, internal protocols, and Tome-curation makes mortal presence inside the network structurally excluded, not merely uncommon.
- **Not segregated, universal** (ninth user message — major retcon of the segmentation framing built up over the preceding messages) — the Backrooms are **one shared space, not eight per-realm segments**. A celestial spirit and an infernal spirit share the same lounge, eat from the same dining halls, walk in the same parks. There is no Celestial wing and no Infernal wing. Per-realm rest-space names from the prior spirits-umbrella canon (*Dreadharrow locker rooms*, *celestial rest-halls*, *Feywild glade-clearings*, *Shadowdark quiet rooms*) are reframed as **bureaucracy-internal vernacular** for the universal layer — each workforce calls "the place we go off-shift" by its own folk-name. The physical layer is shared. Egalitarian-by-design canon strengthened: the equality is not just cross-rank within a realm but cross-realm across all eight populations; cross-cosmological friendships between, e.g., devils and Seraphim are *normal*. Open-canon question on per-realm Backroom administration is now moot — replaced with a new open-canon question on **who administers the universal layer** (co-administration, dedicated body, divine maintenance, or self-organizing).
- **All four (now: all eight) spirit types are Spirits; they all mingle** (tenth user message — reinforcement of the universal-mingling canon).
- **No realm-specific Backrooms; one architectural style** (eleventh user message — reinforcement of the universal-styling canon, removing residual realm-specific styling I'd written for the four elemental Backrooms).
- **Hidden entrances are in each spirit realm, not in Limina** (twelfth user message — major retcon of the earlier Limina-entrance canon I had written following the sixth user message). The earlier "hidden entrances in Limina" framing was *wrong*: the entrances are scattered through each of the eight spirit realms themselves, like Disney-theme-park service entrances threading the visible guest spaces. All entrances lead to the same universal Backroom layer. The Limina-articulation lock as a secrecy mechanism is therefore retired; the secrecy is now door-finding gated (entrances are part of each realm's architecture but designed to be missable) plus separate-layer architecture plus spirits-only access plus Tome-curation.
- **Disney analogy** (thirteenth user message) — the architectural model is hidden service entrances scattered through visible park space, all connecting to the same shared underground utilidor network. A cast member enters through any service door in the park and ends up in the same underground area regardless of which surface zone the entrance was in.
- **Most-important point: Spirits are Spirits; no fundamental difference no matter the role** (fourteenth user message — elevated to the page's load-bearing thesis). The celestial Seraph, infernal devil, Feywild brownie, Shadowdark wraith, and four elemental spirit-types are all the *same kind of being*. The differences mortals catalogue are differences of role, uniform, and assignment, not differences of substance. The Backrooms are the layer in which this principle becomes visible — with shells off and roles set down, the universal true form is what remains, and it does not vary by realm. The page now opens with a dedicated *Spirits are Spirits* section reproducing this principle at the top.
- **Cross-bureaucracy mobility + Elemental Bureaucracy exists + elemental glow colours** (fifteenth user message — significant institutional and chromatic canon addition):
  - **Three bureaucracies, not two**: the Divine Bureaucracy (Celestia + Feywild) and the Infernal Bureaucracy (Nyxar + Shadowdark) are now joined by the **Elemental Bureaucracy** as the third institutional administration of the spirit realms. Resolves the open-canon question on who administers the four elemental planes. Internal structure of the Elemental Bureaucracy (headquarters, leadership, bureau organization, shell catalogues) remains open canon.
  - **Spirits can swap bureaucracies — celestial to infernal to elemental and vice versa.** It is "not easy" but *is* possible. This is the cleanest cosmological expression of the *Spirits are Spirits* principle in institutional terms: if spirits are fundamentally the same kind of being regardless of role or realm, then any spirit can in principle wear any bureaucracy's shells. The institutional friction of the swap is a paperwork layer, not a fundamental barrier. Procedural mechanics (who approves, what the receiving bureaucracy requires, whether glow colour shifts on bureaucracy change) are open canon.
  - **Elemental glow palette canonized**: Fire **yellow**, Air **light blue**, Water **dark blue**, Earth **brown**. Added as four new rows to the [[spirits#Glow colour: realm of origin|glow-colour table]] under a new *Ring* tier (matching the [[eadras-cosmology#Layout|elemental ring]] geometry around the Prime). Completes the eight-realm glow palette.
- **Spirit androgyny, chosen gender, and divine origin** (sixteenth user message — foundational spirit-nature canon):
  - **All spirits are initially androgynous.** Confirms and strengthens the existing *featureless-androgynous true form* canon on [[spirits]]: androgyny is the cosmological baseline, not a stage spirits grow out of.
  - **Some spirits choose to take on aspects of gender** — typically spirits whose duty cycle puts them in close, sustained interaction with mortals. The choice is the spirit's, not bureaucratic assignment. *(Earlier framing — that the gendered aspect was a work-overlay shed with the shell — was wrong; corrected on user feedback in the seventeenth user message, see entry below.)* This is the canonical mechanism behind mortal religious iconography of gendered angels/demons/dryads/satyrs — folk theology was reading the spirits' actual identities at the identity level, but mis-categorised them as gender-typed rather than recognising that gender belongs to the spirit who chose it.
  - **Spirits cannot create life or new spirits.** Hard cosmological constraint. No combination of two spirits, no Backroom arrangement, no bureaucratic procedure, no act of will by any spirit can produce a new spirit.
  - **New spirits come into being by the will of a god.** Divine act of will is the canonical mechanism. Procedural form of the act (spoken / shaped / drawn from reservoir / pure will) is not preserved in open Tome chapters. Resolves the prior open-canon item on *spirit reproduction and population* on [[spirits]]. New open-canon item recorded: which gods specifically can perform the act, and with what frequency.
  - Distinguishes spirits sharply from engineered mortal races (which reproduce biologically) and explains the bureaucratic *over-staffing* pattern as a divinely-rate-limited workforce arranged around the size the gods have given. Corollary: the destruction of a spirit is theologically grave because it is irreplaceable except by a fresh divine act.
- **Gendered aspects are core identity, not work-overlay** (seventeenth user message — correction of my framing in the previous entry):
  - When a spirit adopts gendered aspects, the adoption is **real and permanent at the true-form level** — the gendered state becomes the spirit's actual identity, not a costume worn for mortal-facing work and removed off-shift. There is no putting the androgyny back.
  - **The shell expresses identity outward; it does not create identity.** Personality, character, and (if adopted) gender belong to the underlying spirit. The shell is an interaction medium and a uniform, but the spirit underneath is who they actually are.
  - **In the Backrooms, spirits show their actual true form** — androgynous for the majority, gendered for the minority who have settled into gendered identities. A devil and a Seraph in true form in a lounge may be both androgynous, one gendered and one not, or both gendered, in any combination, and all configurations are normal. There is no off-duty erasure of gender because gender was never on-duty work.
  - Folk theology of gendered angels/demons/dryads/satyrs was reading spirits accurately at the identity level — what folk theology got wrong was *categorising spirits by gender* rather than recognising that gender belongs to the individual spirit who chose it.
- **Gendered traits are an aspect of self-perception** (eighteenth user message — refinement of the mechanism):
  - The change happens *inside the spirit's own sense of who they are*, not through assignment, performance, labelling, or mortal-imposed framing.
  - Mortal interaction is the **context** in which gendered self-perception tends to develop (it puts spirits in long proximity with gendered modes of being, giving them the material against which self-perception can shift); the **mechanism** is the self-perception itself.
  - Intersects cleanly with the [[observer-and-naming]] cosmological principle: in Eadras, what is perceived is part of how things are, and a spirit's own observation of themselves is sufficient to shift their true form. No external observer is needed for this kind of change.
  - The shell does not create the gender; the underlying spirit's *self-perception* does. Personality is revealed through the shell, not produced by it.
  - Cross-linked spirits.md → observer-and-naming.
- **The true form displayed when not in a shell is purely a fact of self-perception** (nineteenth user message — generalisation of the gender canon to the entire true form, surfacing the deepest mechanism):
  - **The whole shell-off form is a direct reflection of self-perception**, not just the gendered aspect. A spirit looks like what the spirit perceives themselves to look like, exactly, with no intermediation, translation, or filtering between the perception and the form. Self-perception and true form are the *same thing* expressed in two registers, not two things in a causal relationship. *(Phrasing tightened to "direct reflection" on the twentieth user message.)*
  - **Two exceptions** that remain fixed regardless of self-perception: glow *colour* (determined by realm of origin) and glow *brightness* (determined by raw spiritual power). Everything else — body shape, facial features, gendered aspects, posture, presence — answers to the spirit's own settled self-image.
  - **The "featureless androgynous humanoid" form previously described as the universal true form is now reframed as the cosmological-baseline default** — the starting state of a newly-created spirit whose self-perception has not yet developed past the baseline. Most spirits never develop past it; the vast majority of Backroom true-form sightings look like this. The form is not a fixed *substrate* underneath self-perception; it is the *typical* output of an undeveloped self-perception.
  - **Gender is now formally the canonically-documented example of self-perception driving true form**, not the only mechanism — the broader principle implies other forms of self-perception-derived variation (bearing, size, substance, sensory aspect) are theoretically possible, though not yet canonically documented. Listed as open canon.
  - Reorganised the *Universal true form* section on [[spirits]] to lead with the self-perception principle, treat the androgynous-humanoid form as the baseline default rather than as a fixed universal, and connect explicitly to the observer-and-naming cosmological principle. Backrooms cross-reference updated to match.

### Downstream sweep done this session (continued)

- **[[spirits]]** — *Initial androgyny and chosen gendered aspects* subsection added under True Form; new top-level *Origin: how new spirits come into being* section added before Open canon; resolved-item strikethrough applied to the previous spirit-reproduction open-canon entry; new open-canon entry on *which gods can create new spirits, and how often* added.
- **[[back-rooms]]** — *Spirits are Spirits* section updated to reference the androgyny canon and the Backroom-typical return to androgynous true form on shell-removal.

### Downstream sweep done this session

- **[[spirits]]** — glow-colour table extended with the four elemental rows; *Ring* tier introduced; Elemental Bureaucracy named; new *Cross-bureaucracy mobility* section added under the Back rooms section explaining the swap canon.

### Downstream sweeps still flagged but not done

- **`elemental-bureaucracy.md`** — new page candidate, parallel to `divine-bureaucracy.md` and `infernal-bureaucracy.md`. Hold for now; current canon is only "it exists and administers the four elemental planes plus the cross-bureaucracy-swap participation". Spin out when more canon accumulates.
- **[[eadras-cosmology]]** — should be updated to formally label the four elemental planes as *spirit realms* with native populations (not just cosmological constructs).
- **[[divine-bureaucracy]]** / **[[infernal-bureaucracy]]** — their scope-of-administration maps don't change, but each should mention the existence of the Elemental Bureaucracy as a peer institution, and reference the cross-bureaucracy-swap canon.
- **Per-elemental-realm pages** — Elemental Fire / Air / Water / Earth could be canonized as their own pages parallel to celestia/nyxar/feywild/shadowdark; currently they exist only as table rows on eadras-cosmology.md.

### Major canon expansion: the eight spirit realms

The cross-realm Backroom canon formally names **the four elemental planes as spirit realms with native populations**. Previous spirits-umbrella canon (see [[spirits]]) was scoped to "the four non-mortal realms" (Celestia, Nyxar, Feywild, Shadowdark). The eight-realm canon is now load-bearing for any future Eadran cosmology work involving spirits. Downstream pages flagged for follow-up sweeps (not done in this entry):

- **[[spirits]]** — umbrella canon needs to extend the universal-true-form, glow-colour, shells, and back-rooms framing to elemental-plane spirits. Per-realm glow-colour table and shell catalogues need elemental entries.
- **[[eadras-cosmology]]** — the four elemental planes need to be re-marked as *spirit realms* with native populations, not merely cosmological constructs.
- **[[divine-bureaucracy]]** / **[[infernal-bureaucracy]]** — scope-of-administration map currently covers Celestia + Feywild (Divine) and Nyxar + Shadowdark (Infernal). Elemental-realm administration is open: either one Bureaucracy expands its scope, a third Bureaucracy is documented, or the elemental realms operate outside Bureaucratic shell-administration.

### Pages created (1)

- **`wiki/back-rooms.md`** — Full page. Frontmatter aliases catch the common spellings (`back-rooms`, `back rooms`, `Backrooms`, `Back Rooms`). Sections: what they are, origin, styling, amenities, per-realm instances (consolidating the existing four-realm references from [[spirits]]), mortal-perspective vignette, open canon. Cross-linked to [[spirits]], [[devils]], [[seraphim]], [[divine-bureaucracy]], [[infernal-bureaucracy]], [[dreadharrow]], [[celestia]], [[feywild]], [[shadowdark]], [[arathi]], [[magitek]], [[mana-metals]].

### Pages updated (2)

- **[[spirits]]** — Trimmed *Back rooms* section (lines 115–131 in the prior version) to a one-paragraph summary that points to [[back-rooms]]. Removed the open-canon entry "Whether *back rooms* should be promoted to its own dedicated page" — answered yes.
- **[[index]]** — Added `[[back-rooms]]` entry under *Cosmology & Structure → Eadras Internal Planes*, immediately after [[spirits]]. Updated the existing [[spirits]] entry's mention of "back rooms" to wikilink Backrooms.

### Open-canon items recorded

- Which gods supplied the divine help in construction (Ioa / Vos / Lirra portfolio-plausible; none confirmed).
- Whether the Arathi styling was original or retrofitted (and what triggered the redesign if retrofitted).
- Institutional administration of the four elemental Backrooms (Divine? Infernal? Third Bureaucracy? Non-bureaucratic?).
- Shells, hierarchies, and population of the four elemental spirit realms.
- What containment looks like when a mortal does find one (memory removal, deferred soul-routing, ejection, negotiated continued presence — all attested as possibilities).

### Open-canon items resolved this session

- ~~*Whether back rooms should be promoted to their own dedicated page.*~~ → Yes (this page).
- ~~*Whether the network is cross-realm-connected.*~~ → Yes, single network across all eight spirit realms.
- ~~*Whether mana-as-food is nutritional or purely cultural.*~~ → Both. Provides magical energy AND has flavor.
- ~~*Solarion vs Celestia naming for the celestial spirit realm.*~~ → Celestia is the realm; Solarion remains the city within it, where the Game of the Gods is played.

## 2026-05-14 (second) — Lint-cleanup pass

Wiki-wide lint pass via new `lint_wiki.py` script (read-only audit; saved at repo root). Scanned 240 pages, 4,196 wikilink edges, 143 aliases. Initial report surfaced 6 ERRORs + 28 WARNs + 5 INFOs; mechanical-fix subset applied. **0 ERRORs** after cleanup.

### Mechanical fixes applied

- **`index.md`, `log.md`** — Added bare frontmatter (`title:` + `tags: [meta]`) per CLAUDE.md *When the schema doesn't apply* section. Both were missing it entirely.
- **`naming-conventions.md`** — Added the four missing required frontmatter fields (`canon_status: [established]`, `perspective: [reference]`, `historical_horizon: [all]`, `knowledge_access: [meta]`) plus `cssclasses: [hide-props]` and the show-properties toggle. Reference pages take the full schema per CLAUDE.md.
- **`mitans.md`** — Added `aliases: [mitan, Mitan]` per the renames safety-net convention. Resolves the `[[mitan]]` dangling link in `arathi-servitors.md` and any other unmigrated singular-form references.
- **`dragon-empire.md`** — Swept `[[mythic-retellings-of-the-cataclysm-and-demon-war]]` (× 2, one in piped form) to `[[mythic-recitations]]`. The retellings slug was an earlier working name that never landed; canonical slug is recitations.
- **`divine-bureaucracy.md`** — Repointed `[[sealed|sealed-folder pattern]]` to `[[_sealed/README|sealed-folder pattern]]`. The link is OOC-meta about the sealed-folder mechanism itself, so linking into `_sealed/README` (which is itself OOC-meta) is canon-compatible.
- **`demons.md`** — Fixed two tail issues: removed stray `N` after *"is Eadras's demon problem a local affliction, or universal?)"*, and wrapped the bare related-pages bullet list in a canonical `<details><summary>Related pages</summary>` block. The bullets had been hanging in space after the open-canon list with no heading.
- **`_sealed/fourth-hiding-place.md`** — Tag-count 6 → 5 (dropped `rathar`; this page is the deprecated Pacific-conclave sealed version and the rathar tag isn't load-bearing on the deprecated variant).
- **`philosophy-of-contribution.md`** — Tag-count 6 → 5 (dropped `tradition`; redundant with `culture`).
- **`rpg/priest-mechanics.md`** — Tag-count 6 → 5 (dropped `splat-material`; redundant with `rpg`).
- **`worldbuilding-needs.md`** — Converted `[[modern human kingdoms]]` to plain text on the cultural-drinks gap entry. No umbrella page exists for the concept; the individual kingdoms are linked separately in the same line.

### Findings deferred (already known or by design)

- 17 pages still reference the **5,000-year Grand Conjunction** figure under the deferred-cycle-period sweep (per the same-day user decision; tracked in [[open-questions#Cosmology and Metaphysics]]).
- 10 body-convention items on `_sealed/*` pages (missing `**Summary**:` lines) — appears to be the established sealed-page convention; the OOC plot-spine blockquote + `## Status` section pattern replaces the public-page Summary line. Not corrected.
- 4 historical dangling links in `log.md` ([[eyeless-vigil]], [[flesh-crafters]], [[lirran-orders]], `[[mythic-retellings-...]]`) — append-only log policy; old entries preserved verbatim.
- 2 false-positive dangling links in `inspirations.md` ([[wiki-page-1]], [[wiki-page-2]]) inside an HTML-comment template block.
- `spirits.md` → `[[back-rooms]]` — concept exists inline but has no dedicated page; user-call deferred.
- **Orphan: `planewalkers.md`** — only referenced from index/log; no content-page inbound. User-call deferred.
- 4 `rpg/*` pages orphaned by design (splat-book separation from in-universe canon, per [[project-magic-system-rework]]).

### Tooling note

`lint_wiki.py` is read-only and idempotent; safe to rerun any time. It handles UTF-8 BOM, image embeds, path-prefixed wikilinks (`rpg/foo`, `_sealed/foo`), `../`-prefixed relative wikilinks from sealed pages, and memory-file cross-refs from the log. Joins `verify_no_stale_slugs.py`, `sweep_wikilinks.py`, `sweep_padded_links.py`, `find_padded_links.py`, and `backfill_schema.py` as part of the wiki-maintenance toolchain at the repo root.

## 2026-05-14 — May-14 six-topic stub ingest (stars-spear-sithis + future-Spear branches + icon/containment/anti-agathic refinements)

Ingest of six pre-structured topic-triples added to `raw/` on 2026-05-14:

- `stars-spear-sithis-topic-{01,02,03}` — substantive (~4.5 KB total)
- `potential-future-spear-wielder-{01,02,03,04}` — substantive (~2.2 KB total; 04 is a new "narrative scenes" doc-type)
- `icon-mechanics-{01,02,03}` — stub (~600 bytes)
- `divine-containment-protocols-{01,02,03,04}` — stub (~830 bytes)
- `arathi-anti-agathics-{01,02,03}` — stub (~560 bytes); tagged `[WIKI_REFINED]`
- `probability-timeline-fracture-{01,02,03,04}` — stub (~830 bytes)

Most documents were 160–700 byte placeholder stubs; substantive content concentrated in two of the six topics. Took an unusually-discussion-heavy approach to compensate for the thinness, per CLAUDE.md ingest workflow.

### User decisions taken before writing

Four questions surfaced; user resolved:

- **Precessional cycle reconciliation** → Adopt **~10,000 years** as the new working figure for the cycle; **defer full canon sweep** until dates are solidified. The new [[night-sky-cosmology]] page presents the 5,000-year (Lirran observatory / existing wiki canon), 10,000-year (Order Sharanel modern working figure), and 26,000-year (Ratharil dragon star-charts) numbers as in-universe scholarly debate; no other pages were swept. Tracked in [[open-questions#Cosmology and Metaphysics]].
- **POTENTIAL_FUTURE material disposition** → `wiki/_sealed/`. Both the Sculptor of Silence (Sixth Wielder identity) and the probability-fracture child go into the sealed folder; not linked from public pages.
- **Stub depth** → New page only where stubs add something novel. Wrote `divine-containment-protocols.md` (genuine new 4-phase procedure). Skipped `icon-mechanics` (existing [[icons]] supersedes it in detail) and `arathi-anti-agathics` (already covered on [[arathi]] / [[arathi-cataclysm]]).
- **Stars-as-Mythoi placement** → New dedicated page `night-sky-cosmology.md`.

### Pages created (4)

- **`wiki/night-sky-cosmology.md`** — Stars-as-other-Mythoi cosmology; Limina's distortion as the smearing medium; the **Great Precessional Cycle** as cosmic lock (not recharge); three competing cycle-length figures left unreconciled; civilizational interpretations (unicorns read it correctly; dragons treat it as math; humans treat it as divine; Sharanel knows; Tome acknowledges open / records sealed); knowledge gradient table; OOC craft note on the lock-vs-recharge framing decision.
- **`wiki/divine-containment-protocols.md`** — The four-phase Elder God procedure for containing ascended Spear-wielders: **Observation → Convergence → Pocket-universe imprisonment → Icon sealing**. Phase 4 = Total Icon Binding viewed from the procedural side. Historical applications: Kudur-eṭir (hours, then Worldender-annihilated) and Xar'vion (decades, still bound). Core craft principle: *gods deceive gods*, containment is psychological and conceptual, not physical. Limits-of-protocol section flags that the procedure has never been tested against a forewarned Unrestricted.
- **`wiki/_sealed/sculptor-of-silence.md`** — `POTENTIAL_FUTURE` / `TIMELINE_CONTINGENT`. Projected Sixth Wielder identity: **Elian of the Unbroken Line, Memory-Smith**. Domain inversion under Dao's curse: preservation → uniformity, memory → stagnation, silence → imposed perfection. Includes the *children of Stillwind* scene fragment. Not stable canon; reclassified from active canon to contingent future-state during this ingest, which resolved divine-mechanics contradictions, containment inconsistencies, and timeline confusion the earlier framing had produced.
- **`wiki/_sealed/probability-fracture-child.md`** — `POTENTIAL_FUTURE`. The Tome's detection of a future child Spear-wielder whose name appears in records dated two centuries forward but who has no birth record. Divine response: institutional crisis management, preemptive Phase-1 Observation, surveillance escalation, bureaucratic strain. *The most Eadrasian response to prophecy is exhausted bureaucracy.* Parallel branch to the Sculptor; the orders treat them as one threat with two faces. Used Weave-neutral phrasing ("ward disturbance") per the magic-system rework, with a note on the older "Weave disturbance" terminology.

### Pages updated (5)

- **[[house-sitharis]]** — New section *"The underlying thesis"* between *Place within the Amunorians* and *Source of wealth*. Canonizes the load-bearing thesis **"Consciousness alteration is social power"** and the famous compression **"Why sit on the throne when you can own the man who sits on it?"** Reframes the house's apparent decadence as the *method* by which the house exercises power, not the symptom of softness. Sources + Last updated refreshed.
- **[[inspirations]]** — Setting-wide design principles expanded from 23 to **32 principles** with 9 new entries from the May-14 ingest: (24) Mystery is stronger than explanation; (25) Institutions feel exhausted; (26) Culture interfaces with infrastructure; (27) Humor prevents tonal collapse; (28) Deep time is core identity; (29) Probability is more interesting than destiny; (30) Prophecy creates administrative panic; (31) Perfect memory is destructive; (32) Containment is psychological, not physical. Header sources line + count + Last updated refreshed.
- **[[open-questions]]** — Added two entries under *Cosmology and Metaphysics*: the precessional-cycle period (5k / 10k / 26k unreconciled), and the lock-vs-recharge framing of the cycle. Both deferred from this ingest. Sources + Last updated refreshed.
- **[[_sealed/README|_sealed/README]]** — Added entries for the two new sealed pages (`sculptor-of-silence`, `probability-fracture-child`) under *Current contents*.
- **[[index]]** — Added `[[night-sky-cosmology]]` under *Cosmology & Structure → The Omniverse* (after [[observer-and-naming]]) and `[[divine-containment-protocols]]` under *Deities → Divine Constructs & Doctrine* (after [[icons]]). Sealed pages not added to the public index, per [[_sealed/README]].

### Reconciliation notes (per the source-reconciliation-is-user-decision policy)

- **Spear name**: source canonized "Spear of Crystallized Entropy" — matches existing wiki canon. No change.
- **"Unrestricted Elder God"**: source uses the term; matches existing wiki. No change.
- **Spear current location**: source says "near mantle depth beneath the Worldbreaker Scar, protected by a metaphysical enclosure, functionally inaccessible" — reads as the *public/outer* description of the sealed-canon fourth hiding (impaled in the First Breach Wound, with Arathyn as scar tissue). No contradiction; the depth specificity is new but compatible. No public page edited.
- **House Sithis vs Sitharis**: source spells it "Sithis"; existing wiki canon (since May 8) is **Sitharis** with the four-letter trailing form. Treated the source spelling as meta-doc shorthand and used the established Sitharis spelling on the thesis update. No rename.
- **Icon mechanics**: source's two-state framing (Imprisoned/Active = inert/autonomous) maps to existing **Stillness State / Habitation State** on [[icons]]. Source is lower-fidelity than existing canon. Skipped; existing page is authoritative.
- **Arathi anti-agathics**: source confirms longevity systems → cultural stagnation, memory saturation, slowed evolution. Already implicit on [[arathi-cataclysm]] and [[arathi]]. No edits.
- **"Weave disturbance" terminology in probability-timeline-fracture-01**: flagged in the magic-system rework as Weave-candidate-for-removal terminology. On the sealed page, used **"ward disturbance"** as the canonical form with an inline note that older institutional records use "Weave disturbance" for the same phenomenon.
- **Narrative scene fragments (doc 04, new in this ingest)**: most were single-line scene openings. Used the substantive two on the relevant sealed pages (Stillwind / clerks-found-the-name); discarded the marble-table-fractures fragment after using it as the OOC closing flavor on [[divine-containment-protocols]].

### Format-Guide observation

The May-14 ingest is the first observed instance of the **quad-pattern** (01 facts / 02 meta / 03 principles / 04 narrative scenes) instead of the triple. The narrative-scenes doc functioned the way `wiki/rpg/closed-time-bubble.md`'s opening prose did — author-side seed material that becomes scene texture on the wiki page when it fits. Most of the May-14 scenes were stub openings rather than developed scenes; only two carried enough texture to be worth quoting on a page. The format itself is useful when populated; the May-14 sources mostly under-populated it.

The remaining four of the six topics arrived as 160–700 byte stubs — significantly thinner than any previous pre-structured ingest. The decision to skip new pages where the stub had nothing the existing wiki didn't already cover (icon-mechanics, arathi-anti-agathics) is the canonical handling for under-populated stubs going forward.

## 2026-05-13 (second) — Cheese-cultures + three-cultures ethical triangle ingest

Ingest of `raw/cheese-cultures-and-the-three-civilizational-ethics.md` (one of the four 5-11/5-12 pre-formatted Format-Guide-style ingest docs delivered today). New canon: two cheeses + the three-pole philosophical configuration that organizes them. The companion **[[dragon-empire]]** page (third pole of the triangle) is queued for the next ingest in this session.

### User decisions taken before writing

The cheese doc references "the desert empire" as canon-established earlier. The wiki has no such entity by that name. Surfaced three questions; user resolved:

- **Desert empire identity** → the rural / nomadic / caravan-and-pastoral facet of the [[amunorians|Amunorian Empire]]. Tchoukou is canonized as Amunorian caravan-ration cheese.
- **Dragon Empire founding date** → after the Demon War (~5000 BP onwards). Locks the triangle as a modern-era configuration with all three poles active in the modern period. To be written into the next ingest doc.
- **Goblin tunnel cheese placement** → own page (matches the [[goblin-ancestor-liquor]] / [[elfen-blossom-wines]] / [[orden-whale-honey-mead]] / [[taran-venom-aged-liquor]] / [[orcish-drinks]] pattern).

### Pages created (3)

- **`wiki/tchoukou.md`** — Amunorian caravan-ration cheese. Camel-and-goat blend, sun-dried, indefinitely shelf-stable. **Imperial-seal grading system** (basic / spiced / aged grades; seal serves quality control + loyalty signaling + tax administration). Functions as portable currency in the deep desert; aged wheels reserved for the imperial table. Cross-references the three-cultures triangle as the pragmatic-middle-pole exemplar.
- **`wiki/goblin-tunnel-cheese.md`** — Goblin signature foodway. Brie-blue hybrid aged in damp working tunnels with whatever native cave-bacteria happen to live there. **Inherently regional** (each tunnel produces a distinguishable batch reflecting its specific microclimate). Prized internally as a delicacy on the order of any other culture's prestige food; regarded as cursed by most surface-dwellers; small connoisseur market across the species gap. Cross-references the three-cultures triangle as the live-and-let-live-pole exemplar.
- **`wiki/three-cultures-ethical-triangle.md`** — Modern-era philosophical configuration positioning the [[goblins|goblin tunnel cultures]] (live-and-let-live anarchic pole), the [[amunorians|Amunorian]] caravan-and-pastoral hinterland (pragmatic middle pole), and the far-eastern [[dragon-empire|Dragon Empire]] (authoritarian-meritocratic pole) along the axis of *individual liberty vs. centralized harm-minimization*. Each pole's internal logic, mutual perceptions, and the trade / smuggling / espionage / diplomatic-flashpoint geometry the triangle produces. Setting does not endorse one pole; each has internal coherence, real virtues, and real costs. The Amunorian movable middle is the dramatic-energy generator.

### Pages updated (3)

- **[[amunorians]]** — new section *"The caravan-and-pastoral hinterland"* between *Cultural notes* and the modern-diaspora material, introducing the empire's rural/nomadic face, the tchoukou foodway, and the empire's position as pragmatic middle pole of the three-cultures triangle. Sources + Last updated refreshed. Three new Related-pages links (tchoukou, three-cultures-ethical-triangle, dragon-empire).
- **[[goblins]]** — new subsection *"Tunnel cheese"* under *Society* (alongside the existing *Drink, work, and rest*) and new subsection *"The 'live and let live' ethic"* positioning goblin civilization as the maximally-permissive pole of the three-cultures triangle. Sources + Last updated refreshed. Three new Related-pages links.
- **[[food-and-drink]]** — new *Cheese traditions* hub section linking tchoukou and goblin-tunnel-cheese as the first two cheeses canonized so far, with a note that the Dragon Empire's own foodways remain open canon. Sources + Last updated refreshed. Three new Related-pages links.

### Index update

Added three new entries to `## Races & Peoples → Culture` block (tchoukou, goblin-tunnel-cheese, three-cultures-ethical-triangle), positioned alongside the existing race signature-drink entries.

### Format Guide observation

This was the first ingest of one of the four pre-formatted Format-Guide-style docs in `raw/` (the others queued: dragon-empire, mythic-retellings, spear-containment). The format is exceptionally clean — explicit `[CANONIZED]` / `[FLAG_FOR_REVIEW]` / `[META]` / `[IN-WORLD]` flags, explicit cross-reference and integration-hooks blocks, explicit LIVE WIRES, explicit OOC craft notes. Mapping into wiki pages is almost mechanical once the canon-supersession and identity-confirmation questions are resolved upfront. Reinforces [[project-pre-structured-triple-ingest|the locked policy]] — when canon-stabilized topics are pre-formatted this way, the bulk of ingest work is canonical placement and cross-linking, not content interpretation.

### Pending follow-ups (added)

- **[[dragon-empire]]** — page does not yet exist; cross-referenced throughout this ingest. Next task this session.
- **Dragon Empire's own cheese tradition** — explicitly open canon per the cheese doc; an administered fresh / fermented imperial cheese (Tang / Khmer fusion register) is the obvious shape but undeveloped.
- **Regional spice blends of tchoukou** — different desert regions presumably have signature spice traditions tied to merchant houses or pastoral cooperatives. Open canon.
- **Specific famous goblin tunnels by their cheese signature** — a regional-appellation system in goblin form. Some tunnels presumably have established reputations.
- **The Empire's customs-office cheese ritual** — what gets stamped, taxed, refused, and reported up the line at an Amunorian / Dragon Empire frontier crossing. Dramatizes the three-cultures tension at the institutional level.

Previous follow-ups queued.

## 2026-05-13 (third) — Dragon Empire ingest

Ingest of `raw/dragon-empire-far-eastern-meritocracy.md` (second of the four 5-11/5-12 pre-formatted Format-Guide-style ingest docs). New canon: an **entirely new modern-era polity** in the far east of Eadras, the third pole of the [[three-cultures-ethical-triangle|three-cultures triangle]] introduced in the prior cheese ingest. No prior wiki canon existed for the Empire; this is a fresh seed-canon page.

### User decisions taken before writing

- **Founding date** → after the [[demon-war|Demon War]], specifically the post-~5000 BP window. Treated as open canon *within that window*; the page does not lock a specific century.
- **Geography** → "far east of Eadras," kept as the page's only spatial framing (consistent with the modern-day continental map being undeveloped per [[project-map-development|the locked policy]]).

### Page created

- **`wiki/dragon-empire.md`** — full seed-canon treatment of the Empire as a polity:
  - **Origin** — post-Demon-War dragon-mercenary coup (*"our bosses suck, guess I'll be the boss now"*); no imperial family, no Dragon Emperor, no hereditary line. Whom the founders had been working for and what kingdom or polity fell when they took charge are open canon.
  - **Coalition** — small, very experienced, very high-skill; no permanent seats; members come and go across centuries; membership by recognition not heredity; long-lived dragons accumulate the lattice's high ranks across centuries to millennia before joining the coalition.
  - **Semi-divine status** — the lived religious experience of citizens; whether the coalition dragons are *literally* Ascended Mortal Dragon Gods or simply ancient powerful dragons revered as such is open canon.
  - **Aesthetic** — Tang + Khmer fusion (urbane scholarly empire + god-king monumental temple-mountain architecture + tropical agrarian hinterland). Dragons in administered settings — paperwork and protocol, not wild mountain caves. *"Fire-breathing bureaucrats."*
  - **Skill-rank system** — universal coverage of every productive / creative / military / scholarly / craft domain; free public education in every graded discipline; citizen self-improvement as civic duty; pictogram-and-hashmark notation legible across language barriers; civilian plaque-on-cord display vs. military / bureaucratic embroidered-uniform display; tattooing rejected because ranks change.
  - **Even dragons are graded.** Load-bearing rule: the rulers wear the marks. Junior dragons do not automatically outrank master-ranked mortals in disciplines where the mortal outranks them. Saves the system from cosmetic meritocracy.
  - **Triangle position** — the authoritarian-virtuous pole. Sees [[goblins|goblin]] chaos as an existential threat and [[amunorians|Amunorian]] caravan pragmatism as moral compromise. The other two cultures see the Empire as *arrogant busybodies who would strangle vitality rather than tolerate imperfection*. Generates predictable smuggling / espionage / diplomatic-flashpoint patterns at the Empire's frontiers.
  - **Mythic voice** — the dragons' canonical mythic register of *grim satisfaction over cosmic hierarchy correcting violation*. Consistent with the [[mythic-retellings-of-the-cataclysm-and-demon-war|forthcoming mythic-retellings canon]] (queued next ingest); the Empire's official cult almost certainly elaborates this voice further with formal chanting in imperial temples and ranked-priestly annotation.

Eight items deliberately preserved as open canon (geography, dating, population composition, religion, magic, foreign relations, the Empire's own cheese, dragon-rank display modality).

### Pages updated (1)

- **[[dragons]]** — new subsection *"The Dragon Empire"* under *Modern Dragons*, briefly cross-referencing the new page and clarifying that the Empire's dragons are *some* modern dragons, not all of them; the coalition's relationship to the broader [[ratharil|Ratharil]] / post-Banishment / [[nine-embers-of-renewal|Nine Embers]] / dragon-god framework is open canon. Sources + Last updated refreshed.

### Index update

Added one new entry to `## Factions & Institutions` (Dragon Empire). Cross-linked from the three-cultures-triangle, tchoukou, goblin-tunnel-cheese, and food-and-drink pages already updated in the prior ingest, which had been forward-linking to [[dragon-empire]] as a placeholder.

### Author-craft preservation

The 5-12 source-chat's craft notes — *the Empire was developed as a deliberate philosophical foil*, *Tang+Khmer is the right fusion*, *pictogram-and-hashmark is genre-native*, *the "even dragons are graded" rule is what saves the system from cosmetic meritocracy* — are preserved in the page's OOC block per the canonical OOC-block pattern.

### Pending follow-ups (added)

- **Dragon Empire dating** — narrow within the post-5000-BP window. Does the Empire predate the [[sorcerer-crusade|Sorcerer Crusade]] or postdate it? Does it overlap with the late [[amunorians|Amunorian Empire]]?
- **Geography** — where on the modern continental map is the Empire? Continent-level placement awaits the broader [[project-map-development|map development]] but a coarse "this region of Eadras" pin would help.
- **Coalition size** — how many dragons sit at the coalition table on a typical day? Decision-making forms when they disagree?
- **Religion** — Empire's official cult, relationship to [[nine-embers-of-renewal|Cindirith / Davian / Koruss]] / the broader dragon-god strand, role of [[ratharil|Ratharil]] (if any) in imperial religious life.
- **The Empire's own cheese / foodway** — open canon; an administered graded imperial cheese is presumed but undeveloped.
- **Exam administration** — who tests citizens? Failure / retake / fee / waiting-period mechanics.
- **Dragon rank display modality** — scaled plaques? magically projected pictograms? scale-etchings? ceremonial mantles?
- **Restricted / forbidden disciplines** — the Empire's authoritarian-meritocratic logic implies disciplines graded downward, marked as suspect, or actively forbidden. What gets a citizen interrogated for studying it?
- **The Empire's military** — meritocratic exam-state with embroidered uniforms implies an extremely orderly army. Dragon shock troops? Beast-folk auxiliaries? Navy of war-junks?
- **Relations with the Amunorian caravan-and-pastoral hinterland** — what does an imperial customs office look like at a desert-trade-route gate?
- **Internal reform faction** — is there a dragon at the coalition table arguing for restraint against the harm-minimization mission creep?
- **Far-eastern neighbours** — independent kingdoms, tributary states, frontier tribes, hostile beast-folk confederacies. A polity this large does not exist alone.

Previous follow-ups queued.
