## 2026-04-30 — Major Canon Revision: The Black Hand Reframed

**Source ingested**: `Black hand revised.txt` (717 bytes, written 2026-04-30) plus an extended in-conversation answer covering inner-purpose phases, demonic operations, recruitment loop, and the 10,000-year ebb-and-flow.

**The change**: The Black Hand was previously written as if its full character — Xar'vion connection, resurrection cult origins, post-ascension fragmentation factions — were broadly known. Per user: *"a great deal of what is currently written is wrong."* The Hand operates under strict compartmentalization. The Outer Hand has always been about information, infiltration, and power. Only the Inner Hand has ever known about Xar'vion or the Spear, and the Inner Hand's own purpose has shifted three times across ten thousand years.

### Key new canon

- **Outer Hand (always)**: information gathering, blackmail, espionage, infiltration, "less savory means." Power is the goal.
- **Member motivation**: most join for personal power. Cover stories are believed by most members, not just shown to outsiders.
- **Recruitment-and-control loop**: tempt initiates with the lure of power → compromise them with manufactured evidence → ensnare with blackmail → use them to extend reach and gather information.
- **Inner Hand purpose phases**:
  1. **Pre-ascension to first ~2 centuries after Xar'vion's ascension**: resurrect Elyra. Records vanished from Hand archives within roughly 2 centuries.
  2. **Mid-history (post-Demon War) until ~5,000 years ago**: free Xar'vion from his Icon (means unclear).
  3. **~5,000 years ago to present**: use the Spear to free Xar'vion from his Icon.
- **Goal reframe**: the "Second Crown Doctrine" is the inner theology, but the operational target is unmaking the Icon-prison, not "second ascension layered over first."
- **Demonic operations**: replaces the deprecated "Demon-Scarred Offshoots" faction. Almost all demonic influence has been removed from Eadras post-Demon-War; the Black Hand is one of the deliberate exceptions, maintaining a small cadre of Warlocks (with demon pacts) and Magic Users (who summon by true-name) for selective deployment.
- **Cycles of Power across 10,000 years**: extreme ebb and flow.
  - **Lowest troughs**: a handful of survivors (sometimes just one Inner Hand line plus a few Bone Ledger archivists).
  - **Highest peaks**: hundreds of thousands of members, a standing army, dozens of strongholds, and direct rule of three nations outright.
  - When the Hand grows too visible, the world coalitions mount **anti-Hand crusades** that drive it back to a trough. Specific crusades and the three peak-rule nations are not yet named.
- **Faction reframe**: previously listed Hollow Loyalists / Mourning Hand / Opportunists / Resurrection Purists / Demon-Taken Hand are deprecated. The Outer Hand had nothing to be loyal-to or apostate-from; only the Inner Hand could fragment, and on a much smaller scale than the earlier wiki implied.

### Pages updated

- `black-hand.md` — **Full rewrite.** New structure: Public perception → What outsiders know → What members know → Recruitment and control → Grade structure → Survival structure → Methods (with Demonic operations subsection) → Inner-circle truth (gated section: origin, Inner Purpose phases, Gaze access, Lost Zenith) → Cycles of Power → Modern remnants → Cultural echoes → Open canon. Tag merged: `faction` → `organization`.
- `white-palm.md` — Reframed founding population from "Mourning Hand" to "Inner Hand defectors" specifically. Noted that Outer Hand defectors couldn't have brought across the inherited intelligence the order rests on. Added that the founding intelligence is now ten thousand years old and supplemented by present-day work. Tag merged: `faction` → `organization`.
- `xarvion.md` — Black Hand's Present Plan section: changed "second ascension layered over his first" to "free him from his Icon"; clarified Inner Hand vs Outer Hand; added phase history pointer to `black-hand.md`.
- `lost-zenith.md` — Same fix in Overview; tag merged `event` → `events`.

### Open canon

- The **three nations** the Black Hand has ruled outright at peak — none named yet.
- **Specific anti-Hand crusades** — none named yet. There must be at least several across ten thousand years.
- The Hand's **current cycle position** — rebuilding from a recent trough? Approaching a peak?
- Modern **Inner Hand size** distinct from Outer Hand membership.
- The "almost all demonic influence has been removed from Eadras" canon may warrant its own small page or expansion in `demon-war.md` / related.

## 2026-04-30 — Major Canon Addition: The Chaos Crusades

**Source ingested**: `Chaos Crusades.txt` (921 bytes, written 2026-04-30) + clarifying user answers in conversation.

**The change**: Two entirely new historical events established — the **First Chaos Crusade** (~600 Mya) and **Second Chaos Crusade** (~200 Mya) — when raw [[chaos|Chaos]] breached the [[mythos|Mythos]] of Eadras through the cosmic aperture Ssar'veth had drilled to contact the Neverborn. A new cosmological law was also established: **Chaos must take temporary physical form when entering a Mythos, or it dissolves** (symmetric: Mythos things dissolve in raw Chaos). And a major secret was added: **the Neverborn punched the seal open both times**, elevating it from passive Chaos remnant to active intervener.

**Also confirmed in this turn**: The user established that **this wiki is in-universe the Tome of Baldaran**. Saved as project memory `project-tome-of-baldaran-framing.md`. The framing motivates the epistemic-layered structure that's already been used in pages like `black-hand.md` and `dao.md`: secrets are recorded but tagged as secrets.

### Pages created (1)

- `chaos-crusades.md` — Both events: forms taken, defenders, damage, resolution. Form-or-dissolve law section. Gated section on the Neverborn's secret role.

### Pages updated

- `chaos.md` — Added form-or-dissolve law section with concrete example pointing to the Crusades. Added line about Ssar'veth's aperture having two further uses. Fixed stray "THe" typo on line 5. Tag merged: `[cosmology, void]` → `[natural-law, omniverse, cosmology, void]`.
- `neverborn.md` — Added gated *Secret: the Neverborn punched the hole open twice* section. Cleaned up the deprecated "Ssar'veth the Unwanting / Empty Crown" framing in Creatures of Neverborn Influence (those names were ruled out elsewhere in canon). Tag merged: `[cosmology, void, entity]` → `[characters, eadras, void, entity]`.
- `ssarveth.md` — Added paragraph noting the Null Observatory aperture had two later uses by the Neverborn.
- `dragons.md` — Added participation in both Crusades (First during their dominance era; Second alongside Unicorns post-Compact). Tag merged: `race` → `races`.
- `unicorns.md` — Added Second Chaos Crusade section. Tag merged: `race` → `races`.
- `tome-of-baldaran.md` — Added "Naming conventions" and "Knowledge held in the Tome" sections to articulate the in-universe framing. Tag merged: `artifact` → `[item, document]`.
- `index.md` — Added `[[chaos-crusades]]` entry under History & Events.

- Specific named regions of the Prime Material consumed in the First Crusade.
- The continent affected by the Second Crusade.

- The Neverborn's motive for the two punches and whether a third is being prepared — not even the Tome records this.
- Dragon and unicorn internal names for the Crusades.

## 2026-04-30 — Canon Additions: Moon Reflections, Order Hierarchy, Demon Mythos

**Source**: User answers to open canon questions in conversation 2026-04-30.

### Moon reflections (canonical)

All four moons of Eadras (Gaia, Daj, Shali, Shani) have **Feywild and Shadowdark reflections**, just as the planet itself does. Moons are named after gods (Gaia name predates the Elder Pantheon).

### Major new cosmology: Feywild and Shadowdark are *complete* reflections

The Feywild and Shadowdark each reflect the **entire Eadras Prime** (planet + all four moons + everything else), but they are **not bounded by the reflected geography**. Each plane extends **near-infinitely** beyond the Prime-reflected region. The reflection is a kind of anchored shore from which the rest of the plane extends. This is a major piece of cosmology that wasn't previously stated.

### Order Sharanel grade structure (canonical)

Six grades:
1. **Novice** (in training)
2. **Initiate** (in training)
3. **Graduate / Lirrian Adept** (sworn graduate)
4. **Lirrian Master** (senior practitioner)
5. **Lirrian Councilor** (one for each of the seven [[magic-in-eadras|spheres]] — exactly seven Councilors at any time)
6. **Voice of Lirra / Weavespinner** (apex; up to ten by the Tenfold Allowance; same office under two titles — *Weavespinner* names the metaphysical function, *Voice of Lirra* names the mortal-relational function)

### Demon Mythos (Nethar / Vorath)

- True demonic-language name is unpronounceable by humanoid mouths.
- Concordance names: **Nethar** or **Vorath**.
- The Mythos is in a **terminal state**: demons have **eaten all other planes** of their Mythos, leaving only their hellish Jupiter-like Prime. This is what they have to retreat to and what continues to produce them.

### Pages updated

- `four-moons-of-eadras.md` — All moons now noted as reflected; gods-named-after framing added.
- `daj.md`, `shali.md`, `shani.md` — Added planar-reflection note.
- `feywild.md` — Major new section "Near-infinite extent beyond the reflection." Tag merged: `[plane, eadras, cosmology, fae]` → `[geographic-feature, eadras, cosmology, plane, fae]`.
- `shadowdark.md` — Same major new section. Same tag merge.
- `order-sharanel.md` — Full Grade Structure section added with all six tiers and the seven-Councilor / ten-Weavespinner numerics.
- `weavespinners.md` — Added cross-reference noting Voice of Lirra is the same office as Weavespinner in the Order's hierarchy. Tag merged: `magic` → `profession`.
- `demons.md` — Major addition: *The demon Mythos: Nethar / Vorath* and *Just the Prime Material* sections explaining the terminal-Mythos canon.

### Memory updated

- `project-canon-corrections.md` — TBD: append section.

## 2026-04-30 — Clarifications: seven spheres, federated Tower structure

**Source**: User confirmations in conversation 2026-04-30.

### Spheres = strands = conduits

The "seven spheres" each Lirrian Councilor oversees are **the same** as the seven strands of the Weave (and the seven stabilizing conduits). The Order's internal vocabulary uses *sphere* where other contexts use *strand* or *conduit*; all three are interchangeable, referring to the seven aspects of magic that compose the Weave.

### Each Tower has 7 Councilors (federated structure)

The earlier framing implied a single Order-wide Council of seven. **Corrected**: the Order is a **federation of Towers of Lirra**, and **each Tower has its own Council of seven Lirrian Councilors**, one per sphere. The total number of Councilors across the Order is therefore seven times the number of Towers. The Voices of Lirra (up to ten Weavespinners) sit above the Tower-level Councils as the Order's unifying apex.

### Named identities of the seven spheres / strands / conduits

Still open canon.

### Pages updated

- `order-sharanel.md` — Reworked the *Headquarters* section into *The Towers of Lirra* (federated chapter-house framing). Updated Councilor row in grade structure to specify per-Tower Councils. Updated Open Canon list with new questions about Tower count, locations, and seniority.
- `magic-in-eadras.md` — Updated the Weave-governance cross-reference to describe per-Tower Councils with Voices of Lirra as apex.

## 2026-04-30 — Major Canon Additions: Towers, Conduits, Spheres, Bold

**Source**: User answers in conversation 2026-04-30.

### Conduit-Tower mechanics (canonical)

- A **Tower of Lirra is built directly on top of a [[magic-in-eadras|conduit end]]** — one of the fourteen places where the seven world-piercing Weave conduits emerge to the surface.
- A conduit end appears as a **magic sink** to ordinary perception and as a **column of unbearable magical power** to magical perception.
- Any magician who steps inside the column is **dissolved** — flooded with so much power their body unmakes itself.
- Towers are built around conduit ends, not over them.

### 14 conduit ends, 7 surviving Towers

- **7 Towers stand** today. They form the Order's federated backbone.
- **6 Towers were destroyed in the [[sorcerer-crusade|Sorcerer Crusade]]** ~5,000 years ago — the two ends of each of the three conduits broken when three Weavespinners died. None has been rebuilt.
- **1 conduit end never had a Tower at all** — the **[[verdant-scar|Verdant Scar]]**. The Arathi-era ruins of Arath-Veyr already stood there from before the Demon War, and the magic-regulating forest grew over those ruins; Lirra found a distributed regulator already in place and never raised an institutional Tower. *(Mid-write user clarification: "there was never a true 'tower' at the Verdant scar, just the arathi ruins.")*

### Tower of Bold

- The **oldest Tower of Lirra is in the city of [[bold|Bold]]**. Founding chapter-house of the Order.
- Whether Bold's Tower carries formal authority over the other six surviving Towers, or only ceremonial seniority, is open canon.

### The seven spheres named (sorcery only)

The seven spheres / strands / conduits — three names for the same seven aspects of the Weave — are: **Fire, Water, Earth, Air, Divine, Mind, Aether (also called Confluence)**.

**Critical scope**: the seven spheres are **exclusive to sorcery**. *(Mid-write user clarification: "the seven spheres are exclusive to sorcery.")* Wizardry, druidism, pact magic, witchcraft, spirit binding, mana magic, dragon-taught elemental magic, unicorn psionics, divine magic from non-Lirran gods, and demon magic do *not* use the sevenfold structure. They draw on different substrates and obey different rules. The seven spheres are the framework of the Weave specifically, and the Weave is the substrate of sorcery specifically.

### Pages affected

- `order-sharanel.md` — Major addition: *The Towers of Lirra* section now describes the conduit-Tower mechanics, the 14/7/6/1 breakdown, and the Tower of Bold. Councilor row in grade structure updated with named seven spheres. Open Canon list refocused around Tower locations and the destroyed-six identities.
- `magic-in-eadras.md` — New *Seven spheres (sorcery only)* subsection naming the seven and explicitly scoping them to sorcery. Other-magic-types disclaimer added.
- `bold.md` — New page for the founding-Tower city.
- `verdant-scar.md` — Added explicit *Antipodal location and the conduit end* update: Verdant Scar is one of the fourteen Weave conduit ends, the one site where no Tower was ever built.
- `sorcerer-crusade.md` — *The Thousand-Year Dimming* section now explicitly states that six Towers of Lirra were destroyed (the two ends of each of the three broken conduits).
- `index.md` — Updated Verdant Scar entry; added Bold entry.

### Open canon
- Locations and names of the six destroyed Sorcerer-Crusade Tower sites
- Locations of the six other surviving Towers (besides Bold)
- Whether Bold's Tower has formal or only ceremonial seniority

## 2026-04-30 — Golden Age Map ingested

**Source ingested**: `Eadras – Golden Age Map.txt` and `Eadras – Golden Age Map.png` (raw/, 2026-04-30). An illuminated Arathi cartographic masterpiece depicting Eadras a generation before [[ssarveth|Ssar'veth]] raised the Spear, with Altea at the world's center as *"Heart of the Conduits."*

### Pages created
- `arathi-golden-age-map.md` — hub page covering the in-world map artifact: depicts pre-Cataclysm Eadras, lists named Termini and regions, embeds the image, and documents two non-canonical claims in the map's accompanying text.

### New canon (additive — no conflicts)
- **Altea's epithet**: *"Heart of the Conduits."* Added to `altea.md` aliases.
- **Altean Plains**: surface plain immediately around Altea, on top of the Altean Highlands continental upland.
- **Eleven named Termini** (fortress-cities at conduit ends, pre-Cataclysm): Northwatch, Frosthold, Skyreach, Sunspire, Dawnward, Emergate, Starfall, Southwatch, Stoneward, Westwatch, Stormpear.
- **Major regions** of pre-Cataclysm Eadras: Haelings, Cloudhelm Mountains, Veridian Wilds, Evergreen Vale, Eldrim Forest, Golden Savannas, Aurelian Plains, Sea of Glass, Sea of Mirrors, Sea of Origins, Kharosian Waste, Crystal Wastes, Obsidian Highlands, Thalorian Range, Sea of Giants.
- **Arathi cartography style**: illuminated gold-leaf, glowing crystal inlays, living ley-line illumination (the cartouche's conduit lines glow with stored Eldritch), Arathi-script borders.

### Errata — non-canonical claims in the map source

The cartographer's notes contain two assertions that contradict established canon. Both confirmed non-canonical by user 2026-04-30 (*"yeah, map text is wrong"* and *"7 conduits, 14 exits; antipodal, map may not have this indicated correctly"*):

- *"Thirteen Crystal Conduits"* — **canon: 7 conduits / 14 exits.** Some of the visual lines on the map are surface ley-roads/highways, but the visual may not cleanly separate them from the true conduits.
- *"Verdant Scar where Altea once stood"* — **canon: Verdant Scar is at the antipodal point from Altea.** Altea's site became Arathyn; the Verdant Scar grew over Arath-Veyr at the planet's opposite side. The map's visual depiction may also not indicate this antipodal relationship correctly.

The map remains canonical for **named places, geography, and cartographic style**; canon takes precedence over the map's text and visual where they conflict.

### Pages updated
- `altea.md` — Added "Heart of the Conduits" alias and section. Embedded the map image. Added Altean Plains note. Cross-link to map page.
- `Arathi.md` — Cities section now references the Golden Age cartographic record and lists all named Termini and regions.
- `index.md` — Added the map page entry to History & Events.

### Files added
- `images/Eadras Golden Age Map.png` — copied from `raw/Eadras – Golden Age Map.png` (em-dash dropped from filename for clean Obsidian linking).

### Open canon
- Which Termini stood at true world-piercing conduit ends versus surface ley-road termini
- The fate of each named Terminus during the Cataclysm and the Sorcerer Crusade
- Mapping of pre-Cataclysm regions to modern continents — pending iterative plate-tectonics map work
- Individual pages for the named Termini and regions — currently listed in `arathi-golden-age-map.md` as a hub

## 2026-04-30 — Visual reference + anatomical canon: Arathi crystalmancer

**Source ingested**: `arathi image.txt` (1.2 KB AI-image-generation prompt) plus `Arathi image.jpg` (the rendered output) — both dropped in `raw/` 2026-04-30. User confirmed in conversation that the visual palette is **species-typical** for Arathi, not individual variation.

### New canon details (anatomical)

- **Eight limbs total**: **four reptilian upper limbs** (larger primary pair for major spell-work + smaller secondary pair for fine manipulation/grip) and **four jointed insectoid lower limbs** supporting the body in a half-centaur stance. (User-corrected from my initial "two humanoid arms + four lower limbs" misreading of the image. The prompt's "six-limbed" descriptor and any 6-leg rendering in the image are generation artifacts — canon is 4 + 4 = 8.)
- **Eyes**: golden, with vertical-slit pupils.
- **Scales**: iridescent with inner Eldritch shimmer (species-typical). *Specific* scale colors vary individually — the image's emerald-green and violet is one example, not a template. (Initial reading mistakenly took the image as defining the canonical palette; user clarified that the picture is *an example, not a straightjacket*.)
- **Crest**: always rainbow / multi-colored (species-typical pattern). The *specific* colors vary by individual within the species palette (see below). The rainbow character itself is species-defining, not any particular combination.
- **Species color palette**: Arathi pigmentation — across scales and crests — draws from **anything in the visible spectrum from red to violet, with two omissions: never yellow and never orange.** Allowed: reds, magentas, pinks, greens, cyans, blues, indigos, violets, in any combination. Excluded from scales/crests: yellow, orange, gold, and other yellow-adjacent tones. (User clarification 2026-04-30: *"anything from red to violet, only avoiding yellow and orange."*)
- **Eye exception**: **Golden eyes occur but are rare**, and they **indicate exceptional strength in Eldritch** (subsequent user clarifications). A gold-eyed Arathi is visually marked as magically powerful, disproportionately likely to be a crystalmancer, archmage, or member of the ruling council. The pictured crystalmancer is one of the rare gold-eyed individuals — fitting for her crystalmancer station.
- **Applied orichalcum (further user clarification)**: the gold seen on Arathi scales and crests is **not pigment** — it is **artificially applied [[mana-metals#Orichalcum|orichalcum]]** worked as integrated metalwork (filaments along scales, accents in crest feathers, harness plates, jeweled circlets, levitating ornaments). Orichalcum is decorative and functional simultaneously: a mana-storing alloy fitted to the wearer's magical practice. This means the pictured crystalmancer's gold accents are **canonical, not artifacts** — the previous "out-of-palette generation artifact" framing is now corrected. The species color palette rule applies only to *natural* pigmentation; *applied* orichalcum is unconstrained.
- **Hands**: clawed; capable of holding raw Sourceshine in the open palm.
- **Personal magical equipment**: orichalcum harness armor embedded with mana-gems (new — the orichalcum framing came in a later clarification). The objects orbiting the body are **not jewelry** but **working magical crystals, magic items, and spelled gems** — a magus's deployed toolkit kept in personal orbit (storage crystals, focusing gems, channeling rods, ward-shards, active spell-anchors). Earlier framing as "levitating crystalline jewelry" / "ornaments" is corrected.
- **Typical Arathi cityscape (later clarification)**: the background of the reference image depicts a typical Arathi cityscape, not unique to Altea. Canonical features visible: towering crystal spires; **glowing arcane circuitry** traced on every major building (cyan/electric-blue lines, both ornament and live magical infrastructure); **rainbow light-bridges** of solidified light spanning between spires and floating platforms; multiple altitudes of floating crystal platforms (workspaces, observation decks, ritual surfaces, plazas); lush bioluminescent vegetation; volumetric Eldritch lighting at twilight. Added to `Arathi.md` Cities section.

### Pages updated

- `Arathi.md` — Appearance section rewritten with new anatomical and aesthetic detail. Embedded the new image.

### Files added

- `images/Arathi crystalmancer.jpg` — copied from `raw/Arathi image.jpg`. Named distinctly from the existing `images/Arathi.jpg` since this one specifically depicts a crystalmancer.

## 2026-04-30 — Final batch resolved questions (logged earlier in same conversation)

### Resolved during the same conversation

- **The seven spheres are exclusive to sorcery.** Wizardry, druidism, pact magic, etc. do *not* use the sevenfold structure.
- **The Verdant Scar never had a Tower** — only the Arathi ruins. It is the one conduit-end where no Tower of Lirra was ever built.
- **Plate tectonics during the Cataclysm shifted the surface under the conduits.** Conduits are cosmologically fixed; the planetary surface drifted relative to them. Pre-Cataclysm conduit-end surface locations (e.g., Altea, Arath-Veyr) do not map cleanly onto modern conduit-end surface locations.
- **The Verdant Scar's modern conduit antipode is one of the six Sorcerer-Crusade-ruined Towers**, meaning the Verdant Scar's conduit was one of the three broken conduits.

### Pages updated for these clarifications
- `magic-in-eadras.md` — Seven spheres section explicitly scoped to sorcery; other-magic disclaimer.
- `verdant-scar.md` — Reframed as a Tower-less conduit end (never had a Tower); added shifted-surface canon; antipode-is-ruined-Tower note.
- `arathi-cataclysm.md` — Added "Conduit drift" item to Physical Consequences list.
- `order-sharanel.md` — 14/7/6/1 breakdown corrected: 7 standing + 6 destroyed Crusade + 1 Verdant Scar (which never had a Tower).

## 2026-04-30 (later) — Race-origin gaps resolved (centaurs, Sidhe chaos-infusion, golem-craft)

Three canon questions flagged on yesterday's race pages were answered by user clarification.

**Centaurs are fae** — `centaurs.md` rewritten. They descend from the chaos-infused Sidhe like all fae, and predominantly live on the Prime rather than the Feywild.

**The Sidhe were chaos-infused during the First Chaos Crusade (~600 Mya)** — `fae.md` updated. The chaos-infusion produced two streams: Feywild-dwelling fae and Prime-dwelling fae. Both trace to a single Sidhe lineage transformed by a single cosmic event. Outstanding question on the chaos-infusion is now resolved; new outstanding question added (which other modern fae are part of the Prime-dwelling stream beyond centaurs).

**Modern golems and Warforged are gnome creations from scavenged Arathi crystal minds** — `golems.md` rewritten with full origin chain (Arathi crystal-mind tech → Cataclysm scattered the minds → Grug magitech aptitude → gnomes inherit it → modern gnome restorers rehouse the minds). `gnomes.md` adds a "Golem-craft" section as the defining gnome trade. Warforged are a martial subtype within the same gnome tradition. Sapience belongs to the salvaged Arathi mind, not the gnome-built body. Mind supply is finite — golem-craft is archival, not generative.

**Pages affected**: `centaurs.md`, `fae.md`, `golems.md`, `gnomes.md`. Memory `project-canon-corrections.md` extended with all three resolutions.

## 2026-05-01 — Crystalmancy, Magitek, Inki, Trolls, food-and-drink hub

**Sources ingested** (5 new files dropped 2026-04-30 evening, processed 2026-05-01):
- `Crystalmancy.txt` — the Arathi art codified: seven Greater Crystal Lineages, hierarchy, Twin Pillars doctrine, the Dragon Truth on Sourceshine vs Eldritch
- `Inki.txt` — modern Ascended Mortal God of invention, gnomish patron
- `Gnomish Food Culture.txt` — origin of gnomish cuisine from an Arathi food-fabricator vault; raven's eye pepper
- `Gnomish Prank v Dwarven Retort.txt` — centuries-old brewery feud (gnomish spice raid vs Palebone Clay)
- `Trolls.txt` — Arathi-engineered living mineral constructs; elder hibernation; dwarven mining as desecration

### Pages created (5)

- `crystalmancy.md` — comprehensive page (single, per user direction): seven lineages (Celestite, Emberite, Aqualith, Verdantite, Voidglass, Solariite, Prismite), four-class hierarchy (Wild → Cultivated → Attuned → Heart-Stones), station rules, modern survival (gnomes, certain high elves, Lirran Weavespinners), and the Dragon Truth context.
- `magitek.md` — own page (per user direction; will expand): Twin Pillars doctrine; Crystal Rail Network, Skyfleet, personal teleportation; Echo Orbs, Whisper Bands, Servitor Constructs, Comfort Engines; military magitek; what survived (gnome golem-craft, Conduit Ends, floating shards, major artifacts).
- `inki.md` — modern Ascended Mortal God; gnomish patron; symbol the six-pointed gear; legend of first vault breach; white-haired Inki-blessed gnomes as prodigies.
- `trolls.md` — Arathi-engineered living constructs of refined ores and gems; bud reproduction, single gender; elder hibernation cycle; how some survived the Cataclysm; the unresolved dwarf-troll mining conflict.
- `food-and-drink.md` — cultural hub; will become parent for race-specific food/drink sections (Elfen, Tarran, Velrathi planned). Currently covers gnomish cuisine origin (the vault, raven's eye), the brewery prank-and-retort feud, and the Palebone Clay tradition.

### New canon (additive)

- **Sourceshine refinement**: under normal solar conditions Sourceshine is **transparent** to most living things, felt only as faint warmth or vague vitality. It becomes active and dangerous **only during major Source Flares**. Earlier "dangerous in its raw state" phrasing now refined.
- **The Dragon Truth**: dragons experience **only one Fire** — no division between raw Sourceshine and reflected Eldritch. Every other race (including unicorns and the Arathi) experiences the divide. This is dragon-exclusive metaphysics.
- **Twin Pillars of Arathi supremacy**: Crystalmancy + Magitek as a single self-reinforcing system. To an Arathi citizen there was no separation between magic and technology.
- **Verdant Scar origin mechanism**: the Scar grew as **uncontrolled Verdantite overgrowth** post-Cataclysm — a regulating Arathi crystal lineage left without singers, eating outward through the ruined Arath-Veyr array.
- **Altea's central spire** was grown from a **single titanic Celestite heart-stone** (largest of its lineage class). Its annihilation contributed to the planet-wide failure of every conduit downstream.
- **Inki canon**: not Salem-origin, not Three-related — a modern post-Banishment Eadras-origin ascended mortal god of gnomes. White-haired gnomes are Inki-blessed prodigies.
- **Trolls** now in canon as Arathi-engineered living mineral constructs. <12 mountain-sized elder trolls, hundreds of smaller elder hibernators; none have woken in 39,000 years; oldest dragons remember the previous awakening with unease. Dwarves treat troll bodies as ore strata; living trolls call the dormant ones "Sleeping Ancestors" and "Grandfather Stone."
- **Gnomish cuisine** is from a single recovered Arathi food-fabricator vault that dispensed seeds in survival mode. Original Arathi cuisine relied on giant insect meat and cannot be fully replicated. **Raven's eye** (fingernail-sized black pepper) is the signature ingredient and the master-chef test.
- **Gnomish brewery prank** (cinnamon, cardamom, star anise, sliver of dried raven's eye into a sealed dwarven vat) and the **dwarven Palebone Clay retort** (rare absorbent white clay normally reserved for top-tier metalwork; reduces a vat to "watery shadow") — *"We still have more clay."*

### Errata flagged

- `Crystalmancy.txt` repeats the *"thirteen (later more) Crystal Conduits"* claim from older sources. **Canon is seven conduits piercing the world like poles, fourteen surface end points.** Same treatment as the Golden Age Map errata.
- The lineage-deity associations stated in `Crystalmancy.txt` (Aqualith ↔ Nara, Verdantite ↔ Qoxli, Voidglass ↔ Nox, Emberite ↔ Raja & Daj) are noted as likely **post-Cataclysm scholarly attribution**, since the Elder Gods were not yet active deities in the Arathi era. Flagged in `crystalmancy.md` "Open canon."

### Pages updated

- `magic-in-eadras.md` — Sourceshine refinement; full Dragon Truth section; conduits-pierce-the-world phrasing; cross-links to crystalmancy and magitek.
- `eldritch.md` — same refinements; Dragon Truth pointer; reflected/raw clarification.
- `dragons.md` — new Dragon Truth section between Origin and Modern Dragons.
- `Arathi.md` — "Magic System" section restructured into "The Twin Pillars" and "The Eldritch Conduits"; new "Engineered Races" section (trolls + crystal-mind golem-craft pointer).
- `gods-of-eadras.md` — Inki added as Gnomish God under Ascended Mortals.
- `verdant-scar.md` — Verdantite-overgrowth origin added under Overview.
- `altea.md` — Celestite heart-stone spire added under Construction materials.
- `gnomes.md` — Cuisine section added (vault origin, raven's eye, brewery prank); cross-links to inki and food-and-drink.
- `dwarves.md` — Brewing/Palebone Clay section; Trolls section (mining as desecration).
- `peoples-of-eadras.md` — Trolls added to Order of Creation table and Modern Era races; tag migrated `race` → `races` per merge map.
- `index.md` — new entries: crystalmancy, magitek (Magic), inki (Other Gods), trolls (Modern Era Races), food-and-drink (Culture).

### Open canon

- The full taxonomy of *lesser* crystal lineages (canon names only the seven Greater Lineages).
- Whether Inki himself opened the food-fabricator vault or whether legend conflates two separate vault breaches.
- The exact circumstances and date of Inki's death and ascension in Eadras's chronology.
- Whether troll budding inherits memory or only constitution.
- Whether the "dragons' visible unease" at remembered elder-troll awakenings is from witnessed events or only from troll-told records preserved in Ratharil archives.
- Whether the surviving non-elder trolls have institutional structures pursuing redress against dwarven holds.
- Modern Elfen-, Tarran-, and Velrathi-line food culture — to be filled in on the food-and-drink hub as canon develops.

New canon: two-mode psychology (Work / Relaxation), multi-generational homes with 24-hour creches and elder-female creche service, deep underground holds with surface trade-post / observatory / hidden agricultural-valley outposts, **studied and refined Rathari underground architecture** (the Shada'din were not first underground but advanced the tradition), heavy magitek (lights, steamworks for great hammers), the **gnome-Shada'din magitek factory partnership** (gnomes invent, Shada'din craft and operate; can produce almost anything in bulk), magic capability across all schools with stabilization/structural specialty, **Rock Sense** as Din'shadar's blessing, **axe-and-hammer weapon culture** with the *"Make the other guy die"* doctrine, **clan-based** society with **Overclan / Overking** election, **Arena of Government** with locked-door-one-issue-ritual-combat-axe-or-hammer rules and the rare general melee (2-3 times in recorded history). - `ratharil.md` — major expansion: **construction method** (dragon breath + magic + claw quarrying; entire buildings fused into single seamless monolithic stone; no mortar anywhere); **mosaics** as defining aesthetic (intricate colored-rock works dragons consider breathtaking, surface races find overwhelming); **The Temple** — newest building, a single Temple for all the gods the dragons know about, grand harmonious mosaic of holy symbols, truly neutral sacred space; Council Chamber refined as a vast tiered dome with 9 tiers × 11 = 99 dragons and a central **speaking well**; **colossal scale** noted (Council Chamber bigger than any enclosed structure of the younger races); **timeline** — built across multiple periods of recovery between dragon-wars. Tag migrated `race` → `races`.
- `gods-of-eadras.md` — added **Shada'din Gods** subsection (Din'shadar) and Baldaran in Human Gods. Added **Worship patterns** section codifying the three tiers (Elder Gods accept, Elderborn actively desire, Ascended Mortals actively desire most fervently) and the cross-racial-worship norm.
- `gnomes.md` — added the gnome-Shada'din factory partnership section (gnomes invent, Shada'din build/operate; goblin-tested prototype loop completes the three-leg economy).
- `tome-of-baldaran.md` — Baldaran reference now links to the new god page.
- `index.md` — added religion-in-eadras (Divine Constructs & Doctrine), din-shadar and baldaran (Other Gods), updated dwarves entry to display the canonical Shada'din name.

### New canon (additive)

- **Shada'din** is the in-universe canonical name for Dwarves; **Dwarves** is the younger-races' common term.
- **Din'shadar** — new ascended mortal god of mining and the Shada'din people; Rock Sense is his blessing.
- **Baldaran** — new ascended mortal human god of knowledge, history, books, and libraries (the Tome's creator now has a god page).
- **Religion-in-Eadras structure**: dragons' early Source-only worship → Elder God recognition → unicorn priesthoods → 10kya the Weave proves not all magic is divine → ongoing theological upheaval. Elder Gods don't crave worship; Godborn / Ascended Mortals do.
- **Ratharil construction**: monolithic seamless stone, dragon breath / magic / claw, no mortar; colossal scale; mosaic tradition; built in war-recovery periods; **single Temple of all gods** is the newest building.
- **Council Chamber** = vast tiered dome, 9 tiers × 11 = 99, central speaking well, Ratharil Stone on the floor.
- **Goblins**: Rube Goldberg invention culture; "goblin solution" idiom; gnome-goblin-Shada'din three-leg testing-and-fabrication economy; orc neighbor relations.
- **Beast-folk ↔ Shada'din**: Veil Districts; "Stone Cousins" / "Laughing Cousins"; Shada'din purchase Beast-folk relaxation clothing and tapestries.

None this round.

### Errata flagged in canon

- The map explanation text says first dragons at 1mya post-Cataclysm and first unicorns at 2mya. **Both are wrong** under the locked timeline (correct values: 2mya and 4mya post-Cataclysm respectively). Wiki captions on `eadras-tectonic-history.md` use the corrected dates.
- The map explanation describes 4mya post-Cataclysm as the **peak of the Dragon-Unicorn Wars**. Cannot be right under the locked timeline — unicorns are *just emerging* at that horizon. Wiki captions soften this to "wars *began* because Eldravath brought the species into forced contact"; peak intensity falls later.

Likely an artifact; flagged for user direction.~~ **Resolved (user clarification 2026-05-01): canon-consistent.** 10my minus ~30,000 years rounds to 10my at million-year resolution. Sea'tua creation falls shortly before or around humanoid emergence. Existing phrasing stands.
- **Dragon-Unicorn Wars duration corrected (user clarification 2026-05-01)**: the Wars are *short* — they began ~5,000-10,000 years after unicorn emergence and lasted only a few thousand years. The map's "peak of Dragon-Unicorn Wars at 4mya" label is correct because the entire war fits inside that single million-year-resolution snapshot. My earlier edit softening the framing to "wars *began* but peaked later" was wrong and has been reverted on `eadras-tectonic-history.md`, `eldravath.md`, and `eadras-timeline.md`.

## 2026-05-01 (afternoon) — Major Update: Worldbreaker origin retcon, Velena, Five Modern Oceanic Races, Kuo-toa rewrite, timeline shifts

**Source ingested**: `Updates afternoon 5-1-26.txt` (15,892 bytes, written 2026-05-01 16:47).

**Headline changes**:

1. **The Worldbreaker is no longer a "called-down Falling Star."** Ssar'veth drilled the **First Breach** through the Mythos Shell *long before* God's Day, in the course of forbidden research aimed at eliminating entropy. He contacted the Neverborn through that breach. On God's Day, his already-fractured mind was shattered further by Dao's curse, and his unregulated deific reach pulled the Worldbreaker through the existing breach unintentionally. Once in the Mythos, the Worldbreaker passed through Limina before striking Altea.
2. **Velena** is the canonical name for Xar'vion's elder sister. Earlier drafts (Elena, Elyra) are deprecated. She was Velrathi, raped and murdered by Tarran noble youths during the Firethorn Empire's degenerate decline. She currently resides in the Verdant Fields of Solarion, content, not yet seeking return.
3. **Kuo-toa rewrite**: re-canoned as the **Fracture Cult** — fanatical Limina-worshippers who study the Gaps. Their core doctrine — *all major fractures in the Prime Material open into Limina first* — is canonically correct and a load-bearing fact of Eadran cosmology.
4. **Five Modern Oceanic Races** (all Sea'tua-descended, all replacing the unified "merfolk" concept): [[merrow|Merrow]] (Tideweavers), [[sirens|Sirens]] (Echo Weavers), [[shimmercloaks|Shimmercloaks]] (Echo Traders), [[ink-lords|Ink Lords]] (Story Eaters), [[tideclad|Tideclad]] (Current Wardens).
5. **Sahuagin** Blood Fleets clarified as **submarine** living war-constructs grown from coral, bone, and ancient sea-beast shells. "Islands that hunt."
6. **Timeline shifts**: Unicorns emerge at **~4 mybp** (not ~6 mybp) on the post-Eldravath continental geography; Eldravath breakup at **~5 mybp**; Ratharil founded around the same horizon as unicorn emergence; Firethorn Empire begins **18,000 ya**, peaks **15,000 ya**, dissolves **10,000 ya**.
7. **Closed-cycle rule**: no entirely new sapient races have been created in the last 10,000 years (except golems, homunculi, and other artificial constructs). Modern races descend from the progenitors via natural devolution, cultural divergence, or the special cases of Katharim and Beast-folk.
8. **Great Banishment refined**: not "all individuals exiled," but vast majority. Some enclaves remained behind on Eadras (especially Velrathi archives and Elfen deep wilds).
9. **Firethorn fall reframed**: the empire was already rotting from a millennium of decadence (Rome's final centuries); Xar'vion was the final, devastating catalyst, not the cause.

## 2026-05-01 (evening, late) — Ingest: Velrathi Servant Race Naming Conventions + Houses-formed-during-Empire clarification

**Source ingested**: `Velrothi Servant Race Naming Conventions.txt` (3,061 bytes, written 2026-05-01 17:48). Plus a key follow-up clarification from the user mid-ingest: *"Velrathi houses formed during the empire."*

**The change**: Adds canonical naming rules and formal-address structure for the three Velrathi engineered servant races ([[orug|Orug]], [[grug|Grug]], [[rathar|Rathar]]) during the Firethorn Empire era. Two new structural facts:

1. **The "ser" particle** — During the Empire, servant races used `[Given Name] ser [Velrathi House] [Own Clan/Workshop/Hold]`. The "ser" marked allegiance to a specific Velrathi House. **Formal induction into a House** (rare, the highest honor a servant could receive) elevated the address to `of House [Velrathi House]` — dropping "ser" entirely. Rathar are presented in canon as already at this elevated form.
2. **Post-Banishment evolution** — After the Banishment, the surviving servant cultures (Orug were already extinct; Grug survived as Goblins/Gnomes) slowly dropped the "ser" as the Velrathi House structure that gave it meaning fell away.

**Plus the user's mid-ingest clarification**: **Velrathi Houses formed during the Firethorn Empire era** (~18,000 to ~10,000 years ago). The House system is therefore relatively young — a Firethorn-era institution layered onto the older [[velrathi#Culture|Conclave]] governance. The engineered servant races (which existed before the Empire) were brought under the new House structure when it formed.

### Pages updated

- `naming-conventions.md` — New major section: **Velrathi Servant Race Naming**. Explains the structure, the "ser" particle, the elevated form, the post-Banishment evolution, the Velrathi-vs-Rathar Houses distinction, and the per-race details for Orug and Grug (cognomens, examples). Also incorporates the Houses-formed-during-Empire timing.
- `velrathi.md` — Added paragraph in Culture acknowledging that the **Velrathi House system formed during the Firethorn Empire era**, parallel to (not replacing) Conclave governance. Houses serve as the lineage/patronage structure to which engineered servants were sworn.
- `rathar.md` — Updated The Ten Houses section to clarify that the Houses solidified during the Firethorn era. Notes that Velroth and Kathor are additional Velrathi Houses not in the Rathar Ten. Also notes that Rathar were always at the elevated "of House" form.
- `orug.md` — New "Naming" section with Orug phonetic profile, cognomens (Oathkeeper, Steadfast, Ironshield, etc.), formal-address pattern, and post-Banishment notes. Examples: *Varak ser Velroth Stoneward*, *Thragara ser Narveth Oathbound*, *Korvash ser Korthal Ironshield*.
- `grug.md` — New "Naming" section with Grug phonetic profile, cognomens (Sparkfinger, Gearwhisper, etc.), formal-address pattern, and post-Banishment notes. Examples: *Grix ser Korthal Sparkworks*, *Vexara ser Valtharion Gearvault*, *Tikzar ser Kathor Deepcoil*.
- `orcs.md` — Brief Naming section noting Orug-derived patterns; modern orcs have dropped the "ser" form but ceremonial echoes survive.
- `gnomes.md` — Brief Naming section noting Grug-derived patterns; workshop-name fragment of the old servant address survives vigorously.
- `goblins.md` — Brief Naming section noting Grug-derived patterns; cognomens persist in satirical / boastful tone.

### Memory implications

- The naming convention memory updates: Velrathi Houses are Empire-era (post-18,000 ya); pre-Empire Velrathi society was Conclave-only.
- The "ser" particle is now canonical and applies to Empire-era servant naming for Orug, Grug, and (in elevated form, "of House") Rathar.

### Open canon (specific to this ingest)

- ~~**House Velroth** and **House Kathor** — referenced in canonical Orug/Grug servant-naming examples but not in the Rathar Ten.~~ **RESOLVED 2026-05-01 (late evening) by user clarification**: Velrathi Houses and Rathar Houses are two entirely separate institutions; Velroth and Kathor are Velrathi Houses with no Rathar counterpart, which is consistent with the two systems being distinct. The full Velrathi House roster is still open canon.
- The relationship between Velrathi Conclaves and Velrathi Houses during the Empire — both governance structures coexisted, but their division of authority is not specified.
- ~~Whether non-servant Velrathi commoners (i.e. Velrathi who were not aligned with any House) existed during the Empire era~~ — **RESOLVED 2026-05-01 (late evening) by user direction**: *"all velrathi associated with a house."* No unaligned Velrathi exist.

## 2026-05-01 (late evening) — User clarifications: Rathar/Velrathi House distinction; all Velrathi houseparty-aligned

**Sources**: Two short user clarifications.

1. **"Rathar houses are not Velrathi houses."** — The Rathar Ten Ancient Houses and the Velrathi Houses are two **entirely separate institutions**, not overlapping subsets. Some names match across the two rosters (Korthal, Narveth, Valtharion), but a Rathar House Korthal and a Velrathi House Korthal are different organizations with the same name. Other Velrathi Houses (Velroth, Kathor) have no Rathar counterpart at all. The Rathar — though Velrathi-engineered — organized their own separate House system rather than being sworn under the "ser" particle to Velrathi Houses; Rathar use the elevated "of House [Rathar House]" form referring to their own Houses. The Empire-era servant naming structure (the "ser" particle) therefore applies primarily to **Orug and Grug**, not to Rathar.
2. **"all velrathi associated with a house"** — Resolves the previous open question: every Velrathi is a member of a Velrathi House. There are no unaligned Velrathi commoners.

### Pages updated

- `naming-conventions.md` — Velrathi-vs-Rathar Houses subsection rewritten as "two separate systems"; the Rathar entry in the servant-naming table clarified as a special case (their House system is distinct from Velrathi's); Rathar's Core Rules note that the Ten Houses are distinct from Velrathi Houses.
- `velrathi.md` — Houses paragraph rewritten: Velrathi Houses are an Empire-era institution; **all Velrathi are associated with a House**; Velrathi Houses are NOT the same as Rathar Houses; Rathar organize their own separate system.
- `rathar.md` — The Ten Houses section explicitly notes that Rathar Houses are not Velrathi Houses; some names happen to match across the two systems but the institutions are distinct; Rathar are not "ser"-sworn servants.
- `orug.md`, `grug.md` — Formal-address sections clarified that "ser [Velrathi House]" refers to a Velrathi House, not a Rathar House. Where a Velrathi House name in canon examples (Korthal, Narveth, Valtharion) matches a Rathar House name, the institutions are still distinct.
- `project-naming-conventions.md` (memory) — updated to reflect both clarifications.

---

## 2026-05-01 (late evening, additional clarification) — Rathar = servants AND a College society (Oxford analogy)

**Source**: User direction: *"rathar were servants, but also had their own houses (which were more like oxford university colleges)"*

**The clarification**: My previous framing treated "Rathar were servants" and "Rathar had their own Houses" as mutually exclusive (suggesting they organized "instead of" being sworn to Velrathi Houses). The user corrected this: **both are simultaneously true**. The Rathar Houses function like **Oxford University colleges** within the broader Velrathi academic "university":

- Each Rathar **served** a Velrathi House in their day-to-day work (this is the "engineered servant race" status).
- Each Rathar **also belonged** to a self-governing Rathar House (their College — own fellows, focus, traditions, archives, Hold).
- Formal address uses the College (Rathar House), not the master Velrathi House — analogous to how an Oxford academic introduces themselves by their college, even though they also belong to the university faculty.

This unifies the previous framing: Rathar were correctly Velrathi servants and correctly had their own Houses, with the College structure providing the strong identity and the servant-Velrathi-House relationship being a fact about their work rather than identity.

### Pages updated

- `rathar.md` — The Ten Houses section reorganized: new "Oxford-college model" subsection making the analogy explicit; Rathar were servants AND had Colleges; College is identity, Velrathi-House service is work.
- `velrathi.md` — Rathar paragraph in Houses section clarified: Rathar served Velrathi Houses AND had their own Colleges; the previous "instead of" framing replaced.
- `naming-conventions.md` — Rathar special-case paragraph and the Rathar entry in the servant-naming subsection both updated to use the Oxford analogy.
- `project-naming-conventions.md` (memory) — updated.

---

## 2026-05-01 (late evening, third clarification) — Rathar combined formal address

**Source**: User direction: *"they used ser (velrathi house) of (Rathar House) form"*

**The clarification**: Rathar formal address is **combined**, not just "of [Rathar House]" alone. It displays both their Velrathi House service AND their Rathar House (College) membership in a single string.

**Empire-era full form**: `[Given Name] ser [Velrathi House] of [Rathar House], [Hold]`

The two particles each carry weight:
- *ser [Velrathi House]* — same particle Orug and Grug use; marks servant status to a Velrathi House.
- *of [Rathar House]* — marks College/fellow status in one of the Ten Ancient Rathar Houses.
- *[Hold]* — the specific Rathar archive-city.

The canonical Rathar examples in *Naming conventions.txt* (e.g. *Valthar of House Valtharion, Ninth Crystal Vault*) lack the *ser [Velrathi House]* portion — they reflect the **post-Banishment short form**, used by the small number of surviving sealed-Hold Rathar today after the Velrathi House service relationship ended. The Empire-era canonical full form is the combined version.

### Pages updated

- `rathar.md` — Formal address subsection rewritten with the combined Empire-era full form (with examples) and the post-Banishment short form.
- `velrathi.md` — Rathar paragraph in Houses section updated with the combined address.
- `naming-conventions.md` — Multiple updates: General-structure section now distinguishes Orug/Grug servant form vs. Rathar combined form; Rathar entry in servant-naming subsection shows the combined form with three new Empire-era examples (*Valthar ser Korthal of House Valtharion, Ninth Crystal Vault*, etc.); Rathar Naming subsection at the bottom now has both Empire-era and post-Banishment examples.
- `project-naming-conventions.md` (memory) — updated.

### Note

The three Empire-era example addresses I generated (*Valthar ser Korthal of House Valtharion, Ninth Crystal Vault* / *Thalira ser Valtharion of House Narveth, Deep Archive of Thalor* / *Pharzen ser Velroth of House Korthal, Runeward Hold*) are **synthesized** from the canonical given names and House lists — they are valid by canonical pattern but not lifted directly from the user's source files. The post-Banishment short-form examples remain canonical from the source.

## 2026-05-01 (evening) — Canon correction: Tower of Stars defenders were Velrathi wizards, not sorcerers

**Source ingested**: `More Xarvion.txt` (812 bytes, written 2026-05-01 18:07).

**The correction**: Earlier wiki framing described the Tower of Stars (Spear hiding place at the time of Xar'vion's ascension) as guarded by *sorcerers led by a Weavespinner*. **This is anachronistic**: sorcerers and the Weavespinner role were both products of [[lirra|Lirra]]'s creation of the Weave, which happened only **after** the [[demon-war|Demon War]] — and the Demon War was triggered by Xar'vion's ascension itself. Pre-ascension defenders therefore could not have been sorcerers.

The corrected canon: the Tower of Stars was simply a **place of significant arcane power** — specifically, a **Velrathi wizard stronghold** held by a **Velrathi arch-wizard** with large numbers of wizards, priests, and troops. Xar'vion destroyed the city and tower, killed the wizards, troops, and the arch-wizard, and claimed the Spear.

### Pages updated

- `xarvion.md` — Ascension section corrected: defenders were Velrathi wizards, priests, troops, and the arch-wizard who claimed the Tower; explicit deprecation note explaining why the sorcerer/Weavespinner framing was anachronistic.
- `spear-of-crystallized-entropy.md` — Darkhoof entry updated: post-Darkhoof hiding describes the Tower as a Velrathi wizard stronghold rather than a "chapter of sorcerers led by a Weavespinner." Xar'vion entry updated with the same correction. Velena rename also propagated to this page (was still "his murdered older sister" without naming). The "Prisons of the Spear" table updated to read "Velrathi wizard stronghold" instead of "sorcerer chapter."

### Note on consistency

The deprecated sorcerer/Weavespinner framing was a long-standing canon error that survived earlier passes. This is a useful reminder: sorcery in Eadras is **post-Demon-War**. Anything set before Xar'vion's ascension cannot involve sorcerers, the Weave, Weavespinners, Dashar, or Order-sworn sorcerers. Pre-Weave magic users are **wizards, priests, or druids**: (User direction 2026-05-01)

- **Wizards** — book-based, study-trained practitioners (the Velrathi mainline tradition; the Tower of Stars defenders). **Wizards are multi-source** (eldritch/quintessence + positive/negative energy + alien mana), and the Weave acts as a *conduit* for these energies to the wizard in the modern era. Pre-Weave wizards used these energies via direct or labor-intensive methods (local-field tap, planar reach, ley-vault regulation). (User direction 2026-05-01.)
- **Priests** — divine magic via Godpower / divine bureaucracy (e.g. priests of any of the Elder Gods).
- **Druids** — draw on raw Sourceshine ("the All") directly; aligned with nature and the older [[elfen|Elfen]] traditions. Druids never depended on the Weave.

### Wizard mechanics (added by clarification 2026-05-01)

`magic-in-eadras.md` Wizards section rewritten: wizards use eldritch/quintessence, positive/negative energy, and alien mana depending on the spell. Modern wizards are Weave-dependent for energy *delivery* (the Weave conducts these to them) but are not native users of the Weave the way sorcerers are. Pre-Weave wizards accessed the same energies through more direct, labor-intensive methods.

## 2026-05-01 (evening, late) — Major Ingest: Goblin / Pre-Vault Gnome / Post-Vault Gnome / Arathi naming + Kudur-eṭir rename + Tarloth-as-dragon + Three Last Lights Arathi names

**Source ingested**: `Grug, Goblin, Arathi and Gnome naming conventions.txt` (25,671 bytes, 2026-05-01 20:01) plus three short user clarifications mid-ingest:
1. *"Tarloth is a dragon"*
2. *"names are Ra-shakir, Ilum-nāṣir, Ašar-etir"* (Three Last Lights Arathi mortal names — Auralis, Thamior, Ixthal respectively)
3. *"Ssarveth rename to Kudur-etir"*

**The change** is large: this ingest brings four new naming canons (Goblin / Pre-Vault Gnomish / Post-Vault Gnomish / Arathi), a major character rename (Ssar'veth → Kudur-eṭir), a species correction (Tarloth is a dragon), and adds Arathi mortal names to the Three Last Lights.

### Headline elements

1. **Arathi naming canon** is **Ancient Near Eastern in flavor** — Akkadian / Egyptian / Hebrew-adjacent. Compound theophoric/arcane names built from sacred elements (Ilu, Ra, Bel, Nabu, Bāb, Qir, Zēr, etc.) + verb/role suffixes (-iddin, -nāṣir, -eṭir, -mukin, -shakir, -kalib). Three formal-name structures: theophoric/arcane, royal/civic, descent. Multi-tier high names with personal + house (aplu ša X) + civic title.
2. **Goblin naming canon** is the rough sibling branch of Grug — clipped, dented, doubled-letter forms (Grizz, Tikk, Vexx, Frik) with comic-violent insult-cognomens (Gearbiter, Wronglever, Boomhand). Optional den / crew / boss affiliations.
3. **Gnomish naming has two layers** divided by Inki's First Vault. Pre-vault: refined Grug names (Grixel, Vexin, Narik) with bench-craft cognomens (Locklistener, Finefinger, Measuremark). Post-vault: Arathi-imitation prestige names with Babylonian feel (Nariqu-Bāb-Nāṣir, Tikzāru-Nēr-Mukin). Modern gnomes carry **dual names** — birth name + bench cognomen + formal Arathi-style vault name.
4. **Inki's name evolves** from *Inki Quickfix* (pre-vault) through *Inki Bāb-Eṭir* (early formal) to *Inki-Bāb-Eṭir, First Opener of the Sealed World* (most sacred) — but commoners still call him affectionately ***Old Quickfix***. Doctrine embraces both registers.
5. **Ssar'veth renamed to Kudur-eṭir** ("Seal-Opener") — the canonical Arathi name; *Ssar'veth* is the post-Cataclysm folk corruption that survived in modern usage.
6. **Tarloth is a dragon**, not Arathi — corrects long-standing wiki framing that implicitly placed Tarloth in the Arathi/godly milieu.
7. **The Three Last Lights** have Arathi mortal names: Auralis = Ra-shakir, Thamior = Ilum-nāṣir, Ixthal = Ašar-eṭir. The post-ascension divine names (Auralis/Thamior/Ixthal) remain the form by which they're commonly worshipped.

### Pages created (1)

- `kudur-etir.md` — canonical biographical page replacing `ssarveth.md`. Same content with the Kudur-eṭir name, with explicit "On the name" section explaining the relationship to the corrupted Ssar'veth form.

### Pages deleted

- `ssarveth.md` — superseded by `kudur-etir.md`. All inbound references retargeted by sed across 30 files.

### Pages updated

- `naming-conventions.md` — Major addition: new top-level **Arathi Naming** section (phonetic feel, sacred/cosmic elements, verb/role elements, four name structures with examples, canonical Arathi-named characters); new top-level **Goblin Naming** section (sound traits, Grug→Goblin transformation table, given names, cognomens, den/crew affiliations, examples); new top-level **Gnomish Naming** section (Pre-Vault and Post-Vault layers with arc, post-vault elements table, Arathicizing transformations, post-vault cognomens, side-by-side evolution tables across Grug → Goblin → Pre-Vault → Post-Vault → Common-translation).
- `Arathi.md` — New "Naming" section pointing at the Arathi naming canon; canonical Arathi-named characters listed (Kudur-eṭir, Three Last Lights mortal names). "Fall" section updated to reflect Kudur-eṭir name + the Worldbreaker-via-First-Breach mechanic.
- `inki.md` — Major addition: **Inki's evolving names** section spanning pre-vault Quickfix → early Bāb-Eṭir formal → late "First Opener of the Sealed World" most-sacred → "Old Quickfix" affectionate. Doctrine of the dual register explained.
- `goblins.md` — Naming section rewritten with the full goblin canon: rough-sibling-branch framing, sound and form, cognomens, den/crew affiliations, what they don't use (no "ser"), reasoning for that.
- `gnomes.md` — Naming section rewritten with the full gnomish canon: Pre-Vault Gnomish (refined Grug, bench-craft) → Post-Vault Gnomish (Arathi-imitation prestige), the dual/triple-name modern system, the cultural arc.
- `three-last-lights.md` — Each of the three now headed with both names (post-ascension and Arathi mortal); summary mapping table; "A note on names" section explaining the naming layering.
- `ixthal.md` — Summary updated; "He is remembered by many names" list now leads with Ašar-eṭir as the Arathi mortal name and explicitly notes Ixthal as the post-ascension divine name.
- `spear-of-crystallized-entropy.md` — Tarloth entry rewritten as a dragon (User direction); 350-Mya dating deprecated under 10my timeline; precise dating left open.
- `neverborn.md` — Tarloth bullet in the Known Wielders section corrected (dragon, not Arathi).
- 30 files bulk-updated by sed: every Ssar'veth / Ssarveth / [[ssarveth]] / [[ssarveth|...]] reference renamed to Kudur-eṭir / [[kudur-etir]] / [[kudur-etir|...]].
- `index.md` — Characters listing for Kudur-eṭir updated; Worldender description updated to reflect the First-Breach pull mechanic; bulk-updated by sed.
- `kingdom-of-xanar.md`, `velena.md`, `kuo-toa.md`, `limina.md`, `chaos-crusades.md`, `arathi-cataclysm.md`, `worldender.md`, `eadras-timeline.md`, etc. — all references updated by sed.

### Memory implications

- The Ssar'veth name is **deprecated as canonical** — Kudur-eṭir is the canonical Arathi name. Folk usage of "Ssar'veth" remains acceptable as historical/folk-memory shorthand.
- Tarloth is now permanently a dragon, not Arathi.
- Pre-vault gnomes and post-vault gnomes are clearly distinct historical layers — useful context for any gnome NPC or location with deep lore.
- The Arathi naming canon must be applied consistently to any new Arathi historical figures, places, or artifacts — Ancient Near Eastern flavor only, no elven-flowery names.

### Open canon (specific to this ingest)

- **Tarloth's specific clan, color, and timing.** Now confirmed as a dragon, but not yet placed in the dragon hierarchy or dated within the 10my timeline.
- **Whether Tarloth's wielding affected the dragon population cap or treaty status.** Tarloth was eventually imprisoned by the Elder Gods; whether her removal counted against the 999,999 cap or otherwise affected draconic political history is undefined.
- **Dragon naming conventions** — not yet documented in any canon source. Tarloth's name doesn't obviously fit any draconic naming tradition we have.
- **Whether Auralis and Thamior have additional canonical content** beyond the Three Last Lights page (currently their pages are the divine-name sections within `three-last-lights.md`; they don't have standalone pages).
- **The full Velrathi House roster** (separate question, still open from prior ingest).

## 2026-05-02 — Curator clarification: cosmological geometry + post-Worldbreaker PMP-shell microfracture network

**Source**: Direct curator clarification (no raw file). Triggered by the curator catching a Brutal Team panel that mislocated the First Breach as opening "into Limina."

**Headline clarifications**:

1. **Cosmological geometry of the Eadras Mythos is a nested set of shells.** Outermost → innermost: Chaos → Mythos Shell (the seal/membrane) → Limina (the connecting plane filling the Mythos interior) → Prime Material Plane (with its own exterior shell, then the planet inside).
2. **The First Breach is in the Mythos Shell — not into Limina.** Material that crosses the Mythos Shell then transits Limina before it can reach the PMP (which has its own exterior shell inside Limina). Several pages had previously listed the Worldbreaker's path with the order partially reversed ("shattered the PMP shell, passed through Limina") — corrected to the geometry-correct order ("traversed Limina, then shattered the PMP shell").
3. **Post-Worldbreaker PMP-shell healing.** When the Worldbreaker entered the Prime from Limina on God's Day, it shattered the PMP's exterior shell. Across the ~10 million years since, that shell has *substantially* healed — but a dense network of **microfractures across the entire sphere** persists. Too small for entities of any meaningful size to traverse, but real, persistent holes between Limina and the Prime, present everywhere on the planet.
4. **The Kuo-toa "Gaps" are foundationally the microfracture network.** The few large historical Gaps (Chaos Crusade fractures, the First Breach in the Mythos Shell above) remain canonical Gaps and are revered as such, but they are exceptional landmarks in a planet-wide ambient microfracture field. The Kuo-toa belief that *existence is fundamentally broken* is grounded in the literal cracked-glass state of the PMP's exterior shell.

### Pages updated

- `arathi-cataclysm.md` — Added new subsection **"The Healed Shell and the Microfracture Network"** under the Worldbreaker arrival narrative; corrected the path order of the Worldbreaker's traversal (Limina before PMP shell).
- `kuo-toa.md` — Tightened "Belief: the Gaps and Final Reconciliation" so the Gaps are explicitly grounded in the post-Worldbreaker PMP-shell microfracture network as the foundational object of veneration. Added `arathi-cataclysm` to Related pages.
- `worldender.md` — Corrected the path order in step 6 of the canonical sequence (Limina before PMP shell). Added new subsection **"Lasting cosmological consequence: the microfracture network"** documenting the planet-wide cracked-glass residue of the impact.
- `limina.md` — Added new subsection **"The microfracture network — the modern Gap field"** clarifying that the dominant Limina↔Prime interface today is the planet-wide microfracture network in the PMP shell, not the few large historical Gaps.
- `kudur-etir.md` — Corrected the path order in *The Worldbreaker and the Cataclysm* (Limina before PMP shell) to match the geometry; explicit four-layer path appended.

### No pages created or deleted

The shell-healing topic is small enough to live inside `arathi-cataclysm.md` (the event that broke the shell) and `kuo-toa.md` (the modern religious consequence). A standalone `prime-material-shell.md` page was not created. If the topic grows, it can be split out then.

### Memory implications

- The breach-location memory `project-worldbreaker-first-breach.md` was rewriting to (a) add the explicit nested-shell topology, (b) make crisp that the breach is in the Mythos Shell, NOT into Limina (the previous phrasing *"all Chaos-side intrusions go through Limina first"* was technically true but misled the model), and (c) record the post-Worldbreaker microfracture canon and its connection to Kuo-toa Gap-worship. Memory index hook updated accordingly.

### Open canon (unchanged or slightly refined)

- Whether the microfracture network is *uniformly* dense or denser near the original impact (Worldbreaker Scar / Arathyn). The Kuo-toa would care intensely about this; canon is silent.
- Whether Kuo-toa cathedrals exist near the Worldbreaker Scar specifically (still open from the 2026-05-01 ingest; now extra-loaded by the microfracture canon).
- Whether the microfracture network is detectable to non-Kuo-toa scholars by means other than wild-magic flickers (i.e., is there a magical-instrument theory of microfracture mapping?).

## 2026-05-02 (afternoon) — Ingest: Draconic language + Ratharil's official Draconic name

**Sources ingested**: `Draconic language.txt` (3,249 bytes); `Draconic Capital City name change.txt` (1,247 bytes). Both written 2026-05-02.

**Headline canon**:

1. **Draconic is canonized as a real, structured language** — not a stylistic gesture. It is an **agglutinative abjad** built on **triconsonantal roots**, with every root composed of exactly three consonants. Meaning is layered through a strict three-vowel template (C₁V₁ C₂V₂ C₃V₃) and stacked suffixes. Dragons do not learn it; they awaken already speaking it.
2. **Phonology lock-in.** 14 consonants (S, Z, Tr, Dr, Rr, Shr, Zr, Rh, Lr, K, G, Ng, Kh, Gh). A transcription convention applies in mortal/Common script only: multi-letter consonants have only the first letter capitalized (KKhR, ZKhR, LrRhDr, RhTrKh, TrKhR). The native runic script has no case distinction.
3. **Naming conventions canonized.** Personal names: `[Root(s)] + Vowel Pattern + Optional Honor Suffix`, usually two or three roots. Clan names: `"[Root] [Root] Brood"` or `"of [Root] [Root]"`. Honor suffixes include `-ara` (Radiant / Flame-born), `-adru` (Guardian / Warden), `-akhe` (Shatterer / Stormbringer), `-rakh` (Eternal / Unyielding), and the highest honor *First Flare* (Council-granted).
4. **Magical/cultural significance.** Spoken with true intent, Draconic carries metaphysical weight and can subtly influence the [[eldritch|Fire]]. Mortals find correct pronunciation extremely difficult — even master [[weavespinners]] only approximate the deeper resonances. Dragons rarely speak true Draconic to non-dragons unless the matter is grave (profound respect or prelude to annihilation).
5. **Writing system canonized.** A **runic abjad of angular, flame-like glyphs** that flow and interlock; when carved into stone or traced with breath, the runes can appear to flicker with inner fire. The script is sacred; defacing it is a grave offense. The "scale-script" referenced in older Ratharil entries (Sealed Hall of First Flame, deep archive vault tablets) is the same script under a colloquial older name.
6. **Ratharil's official Draconic name is Rhtrakhadara** — *"The Eternal Radiant Gathering"*, more poetically *"The Place Where All Fires Burn as One Without Consuming."* Pronunciation: **Ruh-TRAKH-ah-DAH-rah**, heavy emphasis on the second syllable, deep rumbling *kh*, rolling *r*; from an elder it resonates like distant thunder. Etymology: RhTrKh (Eternal / Ancient / Unyielding Memory) + Rh (Radiant / Noble / Gathering) + Dr (Guard / Stone / Enduring Place), under a vowel pattern meaning *"a place where many come together in peace."* Common short forms among dragons: *Rhtrakha*, *Rhtrakh*. Formal Council speech: *Rhtrakhadara, Seat of the Ninety-Nine.* Poetic/ritual: *Rhtrakhadara RhTrKh* ("Eternal Convergence of the Fire"). The Common-language name *Ratharil* remains in use for surface-races and translated treaties; *Rhtrakhadara* is the proper name in dragon mouths.

### Pages created

- `draconic-language.md` — Full new page on the language: phonology, root template and morphology, naming conventions, runic abjad script, cultural and magical significance, plus a dedicated Rhtrakhadara subsection. Tags: `[language, eadras, culture]`.

### Pages updated

- `ratharil.md` — Summary now leads with both names. New **Names** section right after the summary documenting the Common/Draconic dual naming, pronunciation, etymology, registers of formal/informal/ritual speech, and proverbial usage. Cross-link to `draconic-language` added to Related pages.
- `dragons.md` — New **Language** section between Social Customs and Child Races; cross-links to `draconic-language` and `ratharil`. Related pages list expanded.
- `index.md` — New **Languages** section added (after Magic, before Factions & Institutions) with the `draconic-language` entry. Ratharil entry refreshed to include the Rhtrakhadara name.

### Memory implications

- The 2026-04-29 spelling memory's list of canonical forms is **expanded** (new canonical forms): **Rhtrakhadara** (Ratharil's official Draconic name), and the Draconic transcription convention (only the first letter of multi-letter consonants is capitalized in mortal script). Apply when transliterating any future Draconic name.
- The "Open canon" item *"Dragon naming conventions — not yet documented in any canon source"* (carried since the 2026-05-01 evening Grug/Goblin/Arathi/Gnome ingest) is **resolved**.
- Any future dragon character or place name must conform to: triconsonantal roots, three-vowel template, optional honor suffix; mortal-script transcription with only the first letter of each multi-letter consonant capitalized.

### Open canon (specific to this ingest)

- **The full inventory of triconsonantal roots and their core meanings.** The source lists seven roots (RhTrKh, Rh, Dr, Kkh, Lrrh, Drrh, Rhng) by example. A larger root glossary would let future dragon names be coined coherently rather than improvised.
- **Vowel-position semantics.** The source says each vowel position "carries semantic or grammatical weight (aspect, relational status, elemental affinity, honor level)" but does not specify which position carries which axis. The mapping is implied to exist; canon is silent.
- **Whether First Flare honors ever attach to non-dragons** (e.g., Ixthal, the dragon-creator). Probably not, given the sacred-speech constraint, but the source is silent.
- **Whether "scale-script" and the canonical "runic abjad" are formally identical**, or whether scale-script names a specific older variant or calligraphic style of the same alphabet. Treated here as colloquial-old/canonical-current of the same script; may warrant explicit canon clarification.

## 2026-05-02 (afternoon, second ingest) — Compiled Lore: Velrathi descendant races + Bold + Harvey Wash

**Source ingested**: `Compiled Lore - Velrathi and Their Descendant Races.txt` (5,196 bytes; written 2026-05-02 12:28).

This source is partly a recap of established canon (Velrathi as senior race; Velrathi-engineered Orug/Grug/Rathari child races; Orug → Orcs/Ogres; Grug → Gnomes/Goblins; Inki opening the first Arathi vault) and partly net-new lore — particularly around the modern political geography of Bold and the goblin philanthropist Harvey Wash.

**Pre-ingest spelling and canon flags resolved with the curator**:

1. **Rathari is the plural of Rathar** (singular *Rathar*; plural *Rathari*; analogous to *Arathi* / *Arath*). Older raw sources used *Rathar* as both — that remains acceptable for short reference, but the singular/plural distinction is now canonical going forward. Recorded in `feedback-spelling.md`, `naming-conventions.md`, and `rathar.md`.
2. **Elfin / Terran are typos** for canonical **Elfen** and **Taran**. Treated as silent typo corrections during this ingest.
3. **Inki is a gnome, not a goblin.** The source contains a typo within the Gnomes section calling Inki *"the goblin cultural icon Inki"* — the curator confirmed Inki's race is settled (gnome) and the source's wording is a slip. No retcon to `inki.md` or `gnomes.md`. The typo is recorded in `feedback-spelling.md` so future raw sources making the same slip are caught.

**Headline canon** (net-new content, after spelling adjudication):

1. **Orcs and Ogres are both Orug descendants.** The Orug line diverged into modern **Orcs** (cultural and martial inheritance, plains civilization) and modern **Ogres** (bigger, less articulate; likely a tribe changed by wild magic during the Demon War's long unraveling). This is consistent with `peoples-of-eadras.md`'s prior listing of Ogres as "diluted Orug blood"; the new framing is to call Orug → (Orcs + Ogres) a *divergence* rather than a unilineal descent.
2. **Plains Orcs follow the herds.** The historical analogues are explicit now: **Mongols** and **Plains Indians** — pastoral, mobile, herd-anchored societies. Orcs are skilled **blacksmiths** (added; previously the page listed only leatherworkers and weapons) and master leatherworkers. They have no cities of their own as a rule, with at most one possible exception not yet detailed in canon.
3. **Goblin society — three new explicit canon points.**
   - The rude nickname for goblins among surface-races is **"shit-pickers"**, descriptive of the trade rather than fanciful.
   - **Goblins are hoarders** with vast stocks of "might be useful someday" items, connected through a **multi-city distributed goblin network**. Gnomes routinely ask the goblin network to source rare ancient parts, and the network often delivers.
   - The network is **not unconditionally open**: it closes itself to civilizations that look down on or mistreat goblins. Cities that abuse their goblin populations gradually find their salvage flow drying up, their rare-parts requests unfilled, and their sanitation problems compounding — usually without the establishment realizing why.
4. **Gnomes' view of goblins is mixed.** Some gnomes treat goblins as **kin** and act on it; many others treat them primarily as **useful tools for dirty work** — the cousins who can find the rare part and abuse-test the dangerous prototype. The collaboration runs anyway because both sides need what the other provides. Recorded in both `gnomes.md` and `goblins.md`.
5. **Bold is the capital of its kingdom** (kingdom not yet named) and contains **the royal castle** — the first concrete modern political-geography canon for a Prime-Material kingdom. Bold is also "**one of the oldest cities in the world**." This adds substantial weight to the existing Bold page (which previously focused on the Order Sharanel's founding Tower).
6. **The Tower of Seven Spires** is the popular / civic name for what the Order Sharanel calls the *Tower of Lirra of Bold*. Treated here as the same building under two names (the alternative — that they are two different sorcerous fortresses in the same conduit city — is structurally unlikely and the source describes the Tower of Seven Spires simply as "a major sorcerous fortress" without contradicting the Tower of Lirra's existence). The naming origin of "seven spires" — whether it references the seven world-piercing conduits, the Order's seven surviving Towers, or the literal architecture of the building — is undocumented.
7. **Harvey Wash** — major new character. Goblin philanthropist of Bold; "King of the Golden Road"; runs the city's dawn-to-dusk waste-collection-and-processing empire (chamber pots → secondary yard → main dump well outside the city walls → fertilizer, urea, and salvage); reinvests all profits into the city's poor (soup kitchens, safe sleeping places, fair-wage employment); operates under a human alias (silks and high-quality clothing) to blend in with Bold's establishment; maintains a standing compact with Bold's Thieves' Guild (they don't steal from his operation; he throws them a private *humdinger* once a year); has been trying — so far unsuccessfully — to win formal civic recognition for a **Scavengers' Guild**. He deliberately placed his main dump far enough outside the walls that even Bold's expansion-rate would not encroach on it for centuries.

### Pages created

- `harvey-wash.md` — Full character page. Tags: `[characters, eadras]`.

### Pages updated

- `bold.md` — Substantial expansion. Summary now leads with "one of the oldest cities," capital + royal castle, and the Tower of Seven Spires (reconciled with the existing Tower of Lirra canon). New civic / political detail and a Modern notable institutions section featuring Harvey Wash. Open canon expanded.
- `orcs.md` — Plains Orcs section now explicitly cites Mongol / Plains-Indians analogues, herd-following, and the "no cities except possibly one undescribed exception" caveat. Trades section gains **blacksmiths**. New Origin paragraph explicitly notes the Orug → (Orcs + Ogres) divergence. Tag migrated `race` → `races`.
- `goblins.md` — New "shit-pickers" nickname, the integrated/feral split, the hoarding-and-network paragraphs (including the network-reciprocity rule), the explicit gnome mixed view, and a new "Notable goblins" section featuring Harvey Wash. Related pages expanded.
- `gnomes.md` — Goblin kin/tool relationship made explicit; cross-link to `goblins#Hoarding and the goblin network`.
- `conduit-cities.md` — New "Named conduit cities" section featuring Bold; tag migrated `place` → `places`.
- `naming-conventions.md` — Rathar Naming section gains a "Singular vs. plural" subsection (Rathar / Rathari).
- `rathar.md` — New "Singular vs. plural" section near the top.
