### Open canon (specific to this ingest)

- **The kingdom that Bold is capital of.** Most pressing next-step naming gap on the modern political map.
- **Bold's age in absolute terms** — the source calls it "one of the oldest cities in the world" but does not date it relative to the Firethorn Empire, the Sorcerer Crusade, or the founding of the Order Sharanel.

- **The composition of Bold's existing guild council** that has refused to recognize Harvey's Scavengers' Guild bid.
- **Harvey Wash's original goblin name.**
- **Whether Bold's specific kingdom has its own name for Harvey Wash** in any official capacity (city honor, royal warrant, etc.) — source is silent.
- **The one possible Orc city** — source allows "possibly one that has not been detailed yet"; not named or located.
- **The relationship between Bold's conduit and its Far-Kin partner** at the conduit's other end.

## 2026-05-02 (evening) — Ingest: The Flesh-Eaters (rejectionist dragon cabal)

**Source ingested**: `The Flesh-Eaters.txt` (1,551 bytes; written 2026-05-02 17:48).

A short, focused source establishing a new dragon-internal antagonist faction. Net-new content; no canon conflicts; no spelling discrepancies.

**Headline canon**:

1. **The Flesh-Eaters** are a small, secretive cabal of dragons who openly reject the [[ratharil#Council of 99 Eldest|Council of Ninety-Nine]] and the Great Exchange (the dragon-unicorn cultural exchange — see [[dragons#The Unicorns and Cultural Exchange]]). They hold that the only proper state of the world is one in which dragons rule over all other races as apex predators, and that everything since the pre-Exchange era has been a centuries-deep degeneration. They are *traditionalist* in the strict rejectionist sense.
2. **Practices.** They systematically hunt, consume, and terrorize smaller sapient races, with a particular taste for the young as the greatest delicacy. Among their most hated prey are **unicorns**, whom they continue to regard as exceptionally magical livestock — a direct repudiation of the Compact of Horn and Flame. They also **raid the nests of other dragons, steal eggs, and indoctrinate stolen hatchlings** in isolation — a deeper violation than the predation on smaller races, since draconic eggs are sacred under Ratharil's neutral-zone law.
3. **Status.** The Council of Ninety-Nine has formally **declared the Flesh-Eaters enemies of dragonkind**. They have proven hard to eradicate because they operate as small, highly mobile cells in remote wilderness or among the ruins of ancient draconic empires — there is no capital to seize, no court to behead, no clan hall to besiege.
4. **Naming taboo.** Most dragons consider speaking the name *Flesh-Eaters* in polite company to be in extremely poor taste. The cabal embraces the name precisely because polite dragons will not say it. Mainstream draconic society uses indirections (*the rejectionist cells, the egg-thieves, those who have not heard the Council*) when the topic must be raised at all.

### Pages created

- `flesh-eaters.md` — Full faction page covering doctrine, practices (predation, nest-raids, mobile-cell operation), Council status, the speech taboo, and open canon. Tags: `[organization, eadras, conspiracy]`. Cross-links to dragons, unicorns, ratharil, draconic-language.

### Pages updated

- `dragons.md` — New **Modern Dissidents — the Flesh-Eaters** section between Language and Child Races. Sources field expanded; Related pages list expanded.
- `unicorns.md` — New **Modern violation: the Flesh-Eaters** subsection within The Unicorn-Dragon War and Peace, framing the cabal as the active modern attack on the Compact of Horn and Flame. Sources field expanded.
- `ratharil.md` — New **Notable standing Council action — the Flesh-Eaters** subsection within Council of 99 Eldest, framing the denunciation as a Council action and noting the cross-link with the neutral-zone law against destroying eggs. Sources field expanded; Related pages list expanded.
- `index.md` — `flesh-eaters` added under Antagonist Entities.

### Memory implications

- None directly. Existing memory hooks (project-eadras-wiki, the canonical timeline, etc.) remain accurate.
- The "Open canon" line in [[worldbuilding-needs|Worldbuilding Needs]] about *standard fantasy bestiary mapping — what's the Eadras-canon answer for orcs that aren't player-character orcs, ogres, etc.* may eventually want to be cross-referenced with Flesh-Eater predation pressure on those same populations.

### Open canon (specific to this ingest)

- **Numerical strength** of the cabal — *small* is the only descriptor.
- **Age and continuity** — unbroken since pre-Exchange, or periodic recrudescence?
- **Cross-clan composition** — drawn from all nine clans or concentrated in some?
- **Specific named Flesh-Eaters and cells.**
- **Whether non-draconic factions ever quietly subsidize them** (Black Hand, hostile surface kingdoms, etc.).
- **Reformation of stolen hatchlings** — has any recovered Flesh-Eater-raised dragon ever rejoined mainstream society?
- **Unicorn counter-Flesh-Eater protocols** — given the depth of the targeting, mainstream herds presumably have organized response patterns; canon is silent.

## 2026-05-02 (evening, second ingest) — The Great Exchange

**Source ingested**: `The Great Exchange.txt` (2,715 bytes; written 2026-05-02 17:52).

A focused source canonizing the **Great Exchange** as a proper-noun event distinct from both the (older) post-war **Compact of Horn and Flame** and the (later) **Treaty of Ratharil**, plus the proper noun **Unicorn Plains** for the unicorn homeland and the proper noun **Chorus** for the unicorn collective decision-making body. No spelling discrepancies; no hard canon conflicts, but several existing pages conflated the Compact and the Exchange and were disentangled in this ingest.

**Headline canon**:

1. **The Unicorn Plains and unicorn prehistory.** For untold millennia before contact, unicorns lived deliberately hidden in the Unicorn Plains as ordinary-looking magical animals, mastering illusion to blend into the wild horse / antelope / megafauna herds. Through this hidden existence they had **already endured two full cycles of draconic civilization** — watching the dragons rise to dominance and collapse twice over.
2. **The Unicorn Plains War.** During one of the draconic collapses, dragon clans discovered the Plains and began hunting unicorns as prey. The unicorns first hid; when extinction became real, the **Chorus** made a *cold, calculated decision* to strike while the dragons were at their weakest. The brief but brutal Unicorn Plains War ended with the dragons decisively driven from the plains; the lesson "do not hunt the plains" became draconic instinct. This is the Compact of Horn and Flame in seed form.
3. **The Chorus** is established as a proper noun for the unicorn collective decision-making body — the herd-mind in deliberative mode, capable of long-time-horizon strategic thinking. The most famous Chorus decision is the resolution to strike against the dragons in the Plains War.
4. **The Great Exchange** is now distinct from the Compact. After the war and the Compact stabilized into background reality, **young dragons** at the edges of their fractured society and **young unicorns** experimenting with stepping outside the Chorus began meeting at the borders of their territories. Out of those tentative conversations grew a **centuries-long mutual teaching** that fundamentally transformed both species. The bridge phenomenon required *fringe* individuals on both sides — neither mainstream dragonhood nor mainstream Chorus-bound unicornhood could have made first contact at the time.
5. **What was exchanged (specific):**
   - **Unicorns → dragons:** disciplined arts of psionics, specifically *telepathy, telekinesis, psychic combat, psychic shielding* (a four-discipline mental tradition); cooperation without domination or hierarchy (the cultural DNA from which Ratharil's Council of 99 grew); and **the realization that other sapient species had existed on Eadras for approximately twenty thousand years** — the dragons did not know there were other thinking beings before unicorns told them.
   - **Dragons → unicorns:** the power and burden of individuality (the concept of a true, singular *"I"*); new and aggressive applications of Eldritch magic.
6. **Two cultural-legacy phrases** still in active use:
   - ***Walking the Dragon Path*** — said of a modern unicorn who lives as an individual.
   - ***Singing with the Unicorn Voice*** — said of a dragon who sets aside personal pride for the good of the whole. (Among traditionalists an insult; among Council-aligned dragons a high compliment.)
7. **Dating** (derived, not asserted by source): the unicorn-taught lesson *"sapient species had existed on Eadras for approximately twenty thousand years"* against the canonical 39,000 BP humanoid emergence yields a probable Exchange date of **~19,000 BP** — about a thousand years before the founding of the Firethorn Empire (18,000 BP). This places the Exchange itself at a much later horizon than the Plains War (~4 mybp), with millions of years of distant Compact-bound peace in between.

### Pages created

- `great-exchange.md` — Full event page covering the background (two prior dragon civilizational cycles), the Plains War as precursor, the bridge-individual phenomenon, the four exchanged lessons in detail, the cultural-legacy phrases, the post-Exchange institutional cascade (Compact reaffirmed, Treaty of Ratharil, modern dragon psionics, modern unicorn individuality), the Flesh-Eater rejection, and the dating inference. Tags: `[events, eadras, history]`.
- `unicorn-plains.md` — Geography page for the Unicorn Plains: vast grasslands; hidden-millennia unicorn life among ordinary herds; site of the Plains War; post-war "do not hunt the plains" norm; modern Flesh-Eater violations. Tags: `[geographic-feature, eadras]`.

### Pages updated

- `unicorns.md` — Substantial update. New **Hidden Millennia** section documenting the pre-discovery period and the two prior dragon cycles. New **Chorus** subsection within Nature and Society formalizing the collective decision-making body. New **Walking the Dragon Path** subsection. Restructured **Unicorn-Dragon War and Peace** section to disentangle War, Compact, and Exchange as three distinct historical layers. Sources field expanded; Related pages list expanded.
- `dragons.md` — **Unicorns and Cultural Exchange** section restructured into four labeled subsections (Plains War, Compact, Great Exchange, Treaty of Ratharil). The Exchange's specific lessons now itemized including the four psionic disciplines, the cooperation-without-hierarchy lesson, the ~20,000-year sapient-species realization, and the *Singing with the Unicorn Voice* phrase. Sources field expanded; Related pages list expanded.
- `flesh-eaters.md` — Inline references to "Great Exchange" wikilinked to the new `great-exchange.md`. Cross-references to `unicorn-plains` added.
- `eadras-timeline.md` — Plains War row reframed (with Chorus mention). New 19,000 BP row for the Great Exchange with explicit "derived dating" caveat.
- `index.md` — `great-exchange` added under History & Events; `unicorn-plains` added under Places.

### Memory implications

- Existing memories continue to apply.
- The 2026-05-02 morning's "the Great Exchange" reference (in the morning's Compiled Lore log entry) is now properly grounded in a dedicated wiki page; future references should wikilink to `great-exchange.md`.

### Open canon (specific to this ingest)

- **The exact horizon of the Exchange.** ~19,000 BP is a derived inference from the "20,000 years of sapient species" clue against humanoid emergence at 39,000 BP. Curator confirmation would lock it in.
- **The duration of the centuries-long bridge phase.** *Centuries* is given but no precise span.
- **Specific named bridge individuals** — no named young unicorns or young dragons from the Exchange period appear in canon yet.
- **Whether the Chorus formally sanctioned the bridge contacts** at any point, or whether they remained marginal-and-tolerated for the entire bridge phase.
- **The two prior cycles of draconic civilization** the unicorns observed from hiding — neither names, dates, nor any surviving cities or archives are in canon.
- **Continental placement of the Unicorn Plains** in the modern post-Cataclysm geography.
- **Whether the Exchange's institutional descendants** (Council of 99, Treaty of Ratharil) are dated to immediately after the Exchange or to a later still horizon.

## 2026-05-02 (evening, third entry) — Brutal Team panel save: Flesh-Eater rearing, herd-atrocity hunting, horn-crowns

**Source**: Curator collaborative session (Brutal Team panel), 2026-05-02. No raw file. Triggered when the curator invoked *Brutal Team evaluate flesh-eaters*; the resulting back-and-forth panel proposals were committed to canon on the curator's *save the brutal team info* command, with one mid-save framing correction (*horn-crowns are wide skull-mosaics, not tall stacks*) folded into the same save.

**Headline canon additions**:

1. **The Flesh-Eaters do not just hunt — they cultivate suffering.** Predation is calibrated for terror and (where possible) for the grief of those psychically or emotionally bonded to the victim. Live consumption is preferred over a clean kill; the victim's suffering is part of what is being consumed.
2. **Chorus-amplified atrocity tactics.** Flesh-Eater raids on unicorn herds are calibrated specifically to abuse the [[unicorns#The Chorus|Chorus]] link: separating a foal from its mother while the Chorus is still actively shared so every adult feels the child's terror in real time; sawing through a foal's horn while the child is still conscious and drinking the blood from the stump; cutting unborn foals from captured pregnant mothers' wombs to be devoured in front of the bleeding-out mother. The terror is the point; the meat is incidental.
3. **Severed unicorn horn is also ground into powder and snorted** by Flesh-Eaters for its euphoric high — the underground market this implies is one driver of the cabal's opportunistic raids.
4. **Egg theft specifically targets reformed and Council-aligned clans** — the clans most committed to the post-Exchange consensus — both because corrupting *those* eggs is the deepest possible affront to the consensus and because the resulting cohorts can later be used as ideological weapons against the very clans they were stolen from.
5. **The cohort indoctrination is total.** A Flesh-Eater rearing chamber's surfaces are rubbed with the rendered fat of sapient kills so the hatchling, before it has eyes, knows the *taste of the world* is the taste of cooked person. First food is fresh humanoid liver pressed gently against the hatchling's mouth by an elder crooning clan-comfort sounds — pairing love and the meat of thinking beings as a single inseparable sensation. By week two the hatchling will not eat anything that did not, that morning, have a name.
6. **Throwbacks (clan-genetic refusers) are walled into a chamber and starved**, while the elder who fed them sings the proper draconic mourning songs outside the wall — folding even the throwback's death into the surviving cohort's experience of *correct feeling*.
7. **Bite-mark walls.** Vertical strips of *educational meat* are hung at hatchling height in cohort rooms; by year three the brown-stained walls carry thousands of overlapping bite-marks, used by elders as **bite-records** to track each hatchling's developing aggression.
8. **The Council-Draconic mockery.** A reading-tablet etched with the Council of Ninety-Nine's denouncement of the Flesh-Eaters in formal Draconic hangs in every cohort-room; elders read it aloud weekly with mocking precision. Adult Flesh-Eaters speak fluent Council-formal Draconic, often more correctly than most Council members, and use it deliberately as the proper register for their kills. *The vocabulary is contaminated* — one of the reasons mainstream dragons consider the Flesh-Eater name in such poor taste.
9. **Control-case practice and the cohort kill-test.** Some holds keep a single uncorrupted hatchling alive for thirty or forty years as a *control case*, raised properly. When fully grown, he is presented to the cohort as a final test: hunt and kill your own brother. Refusers are themselves killed; passers are confirmed full Flesh-Eaters. A percentage of cohorts recognize the control by smell and refuse the test — these are released with the words *go home*. Most return broken; a small number reach mainstream clan-halls. **Those who do are the Council's only intelligence on what actually happens inside the holds; the Council protects them fiercely; the Flesh-Eaters never reclaim them.**
10. **The Horn-Crowns** — the cabal's most distinctive practice, given a major dedicated section. Severed unicorn horns are surgically grafted **directly to the wearer's skull-bone** (direct bone contact is required for the psychic link to remain active) using **dark Eldritch** — the aggressive applications of [[eldritch|Eldritch magic]] taught to dragonkind in the [[great-exchange|Great Exchange]], turned now to entirely new use. Each horn remains psychically tethered to the bereaved mother and herd it was taken from.
11. **The crown is wide, not tall** — *correction folded into the save mid-write*. A senior Flesh-Eater's head is a dense multicolored mosaic of dozens of grafted horns covering the entire skull surface, jutting outward like a tumor made of rainbows (pearl, crimson, emerald, violet, gold). The dragon's own scales are split and stretched tight between the grafts and weep pus and blood at every junction for the wearer's whole life.
12. **Each horn pulses with its linked mother's heartbeat**, out of phase with every other horn — a senior horn-crown visibly flickers with bioluminescent silver throbs at dozens of different rhythms simultaneously.
13. **Pin code** for taking-day pins on each horn: gold = matriarch, copper = foal-with-mother, blackened bone = elder taken personally, white = horn gifted under coercion (extorted via threat to an unborn).
14. **The yellow weep + the brow-cloth tradition.** The graft never properly heals; a translucent yellow fluid that smells faintly of warm milk (the bereaved mother's lactation reflex firing every time the link pulses) seeps continuously around every horn-base. Flesh-Eaters carry small woven cloths to dab the weep; the cloths are kept and never washed; old brow-cloth sets are inheritances passed down with the crown.
15. **Daily grooming** is performed by an apprentice with a paste of rendered foal-marrow, polishing each horn until the silver of the original Silver Run lineage glyph-bands shines through. The smell identifies a Flesh-Eater hold at a mile downwind.
16. **The inverted Chorus.** A horn-crown wearer hears every linked mother's grief-song simultaneously, twenty-four hours a day, for life — different voices, different unicorn-herd languages, different flavors of agony. The cabal teaches its members to experience this cacophony as **pleasure**; conditioning that produces this perception is the same that produces the cohort indoctrination. Senior wearers report that the songs eventually braid into a *kind of music*, audible only to themselves — an inverted herd-mind made of bereaved matriarchs.
17. **The eldest case.** A single ancient Flesh-Eater elder wears a crown so dense and heavy he cannot stand and must levitate permanently to support its weight. He has been listening to his inverted Chorus for so long that he has begun to **understand it as the unicorns themselves understand the Chorus, and to sing back into it.** He is, in the most literal sense, the only being in dragondom who has fully learned the language his cabal denied itself. He is also beyond reform: he loves the Chorus and intends the suffering that makes it sing. The Council has long suspected; one returnee has confirmed; he has not been located.
18. **The cabal's constitution.** A Flesh-Eater's authority within the cabal is exactly the horn-count and horn-prestige of his crown. Junior deference to the most-decorated mirrors mainstream Council age-deference — but redirected from age to **inflicted grief**. Cabal motto: *They bow to time itself, while we bow to what we have done with our time.*
19. **Hat-removal = death-demand.** To remove a Flesh-Eater's horn-crown by force is, by the cabal's own custom, to demand the wearer's death — and most of them welcome it, **because the crown's song does not stop when the wearer dies; it only acquires a new wearer.**

### Pages updated

- `flesh-eaters.md` — Substantial expansion. Summary updated. Practices section expanded into four interlocking subsections: *Systematic predation* (now with cultivated-suffering framing), *Hunting the herd: Chorus-amplified atrocity* (new), *Nest-raids and the cohort indoctrination* (now with rearing-chamber, Council-Draconic mockery, and control-case sub-subsections), *Operating in mobile cells* (unchanged). New top-level **Horn-crowns** section covering grafting, the visual, the pin code, daily maintenance, the inverted Chorus, the eldest case, and the cabal's constitution. Open canon updated to resolve the previously-open *recovery rates of stolen hatchlings* item (partial: returnees exist but are described as broken, not reformed) and to add new derived questions (the eldest elder's location, the horn-powder market's buyers, returnee long-term outcomes).
- `unicorns.md` — Horns subsection updated to reconcile the natural-decay rule with the Flesh-Eater dark-Eldritch grafting (decay is *halted* in slow ongoing failure, not arrested). Modern violation subsection expanded with the Chorus-amplified atrocity tactics and the horn-harvesting / horn-crown traffic.
- `index.md` — flesh-eaters entry refreshed to surface the new horn-crown and Chorus-amplified-atrocity content.

### Memory implications

- Existing memory entries continue to apply.
- The panel-save workflow recorded in `project-expert-panels.md` was exercised correctly: panel proposed; curator approved with *save the brutal team info*; canon committed. This is the first use of the save workflow on record.

### Open canon (specific to this save)

- The location of the eldest elder.
- The size and composition of the horn-powder drug market.
- Whether returnees ever fully reform (vs. live broken).
- Whether dedicated unicorn Border-Friend units exist as Flesh-Eater counter-forces.
- Whether the *gifted under coercion* white-pin practice ever produces voluntary unicorn collaborators (a horrifying possibility the source does not foreclose).

## 2026-05-02 (late evening) — Brutal Team panel save: The Eldest Elder

**Source**: Curator collaborative session (Brutal Team panel, second invocation on `flesh-eaters`), 2026-05-02. Triggered when the curator invoked *Brutal Team evaluate flesh-eaters* a second time after the earlier horn-crowns save; the resulting back-and-forth panel proposals were committed to canon on the curator's *save* command.

**Headline canon additions**:

1. **The Eldest Elder is now a major dedicated section** in `flesh-eaters.md` rather than the brief "eldest case" subsection of Horn-crowns. The previous Horn-crowns subsection has been replaced with a pointer.
2. **He is not a leader — he is the cabal's afterlife.** The cabal's mobile cells do not take orders from him; the holds do not rotate apprentices through his service. He is the *destination* every Flesh-Eater life is silently arranged toward. *He is what the cabal is for.*
3. **Body as architecture.** His skull is no longer dragonshape but a low dome of grafted horns several feet across; the dragon-bone of his actual head is a small dark core somewhere inside the mosaic, inferable only from the in-phase pulse of the central horns. The lair floor beneath him is permanently slick with dried-and-redried yellow crust and darker bands of older decay. He has not used his own jaws to eat in thirty years.
4. **The three apprentice-feeders.** Feeding the elder is the work of an apprentice trained from her own hatchling-cohort to do nothing else; she regurgitates pre-chewed sapient meat into the small visible aperture of his mouth four times a day, very gently — a horn-jostle could break a psychic link and silence a screaming mother. There are *three* apprentice-feeders in hereditary rotation, each training her own hatchlings to take over. **The role is the kindest practical work in the entire hold and the only one of the cabal's roles that approaches *tenderness*.**
5. **The lair.** Walls hung with eleven generations of inherited brow-cloth sets, layered like wallpaper, the older sets beneath the newer. The chamber's only light is the silver flicker of dozens of out-of-phase horn-pulses casting bioluminescent strobe across the cloth-walls — constant quiet shimmer; no torches; no daylight needed. Apprentices communicate via small ritualized hand-signals because the elder's perception of sound is now so given over to the inverted Chorus that a stray voice would register as painful static.
6. **His speech.** When he speaks — rarely, only to instruct or to receive a new graft — he speaks in **fluent Council-formal Draconic**, grammatically perfect to a degree the apprentices (untaught in the prestige register) understand only as rhythm. He is the only living being in dragondom whose speech is one hundred percent the language of the Council that has declared him an enemy. The apprentices treat the unintelligibility as holy. (This is the final structural completion of the [[flesh-eaters#The Council-Draconic mockery|Council-Draconic mockery]] taught to him as a hatchling.)
7. **The Council recovery operation that became him.** The Council has located the elder **once.** They trained a returnee — a dragon raised in a Flesh-Eater hold, escaped through the *go home* test, integrated into a mainstream clan — as a recovery agent (returnees are the only beings who can pass close to a Flesh-Eater hold without being detected; the cabal's outer pickets read them as one of the released ones returning). The returnee got into the lair, was admitted to the elder's antechamber, looked into the elder's mouth-aperture, and **sang back to him. And stayed.** The Council does not know whether he was a sleeper agent planted by the cabal in the original *go home* release, or whether the elder turned him in the moment of meeting. Either reading is canonically possible. **Either is, for the Council, equally catastrophic.** The recovery operation has not been attempted again. Internal Council documents refer to the matter as *the unfinished file.*
8. **The closure.** Because the lost returnee-recovery agent is now there singing with the elder, the eldest elder is the only place in dragondom where the rejection of the [[great-exchange|Great Exchange]] and the post-Exchange consensus have, in the strictest factual sense, **fully closed back into a single mind.** A dragon raised by mainstream-clan parents but stolen, indoctrinated, escaped, integrated, and finally returned — and an elder who is the cabal's purest distillation — are now one organism's two halves, and the organism is singing.

### Pages updated

- `flesh-eaters.md` — Promoted "The eldest case" Horn-crowns subsection to a full top-level **The Eldest Elder** section with subsections (What he is, Body as architecture, The three apprentice-feeders, The lair, His speech, The Council recovery operation that became him, The closure). The original "eldest case" subsection now contains a pointer to the new section.
- Open canon refined: the elder's *location* is now partly resolved (Council found him once via the lost returnee; classified internally as *the unfinished file*; no re-attempt). New open items added: the cabal's possible relocation of him post-recovery; whether other Council recovery operations have been attempted on lesser elders since; the hereditary apprentice-feeder families' inner experience of their work.
- Inline named figures: the **eldest elder**, the **lost returnee-recovery agent**, and the **three apprentice-feeder lineage-mistresses** — all currently unnamed but added to the *specific named Flesh-Eaters and cells* open-canon item.

### Memory implications

- None directly. Existing memory hooks remain accurate.
- The *unfinished file* is now the wiki's most concrete worked example of how the Flesh-Eater problem fails to yield to direct intervention; future panels and ingest passes touching Council-vs-Flesh-Eater material should reference it.

### Open canon (specific to this save)

- **The unfinished file's date and circumstances** — when did the recovery operation happen, who was on the Council at the time, what specific clan was the returnee-agent integrated into?
- **Whether the lost returnee can ever be retrieved**, even partially — i.e., whether the singing-back was assimilation or co-authorship.
- **Whether the elder has horn-grafts that the lost returnee personally contributed** since arriving — a concrete question with horrifying implications either way.
- **The location and physical scale of the lair**.
- **The three apprentice-feeders' lineage names and origins** — were they themselves Flesh-Eater-raised cohorts, or are they a parallel class within the cabal?

## 2026-05-02 (late evening, second pivot) — Faction rename Flesh-Eaters → Flesh-Crafters + scope-breadth correction

**Source**: Curator direction, 2026-05-02. Triggered when the curator observed that the morning's Brutal Team panel content had over-anchored on unicorn-targeting, and clarified that the cabal's correct name and identity is **Flesh-Crafters**, not Flesh-Eaters — the eating is only the opening phase of a *crafting* tradition that builds the wearer's body out of harvested parts of many races.

This is a **faction-identity retcon**, comparable in scope to the earlier Ssar'veth → Kudur-eṭir rename (where the older name persists as an acceptable folk reference but the new name is canonical going forward).

**Headline canon changes**:

1. **Page renamed:** `flesh-eaters.md` → `flesh-crafters.md`. The old wikilink target no longer exists; all cross-references updated.
2. **Faction renamed.** Canonical name is now **Flesh-Crafters** (the cabal's own self-name and the current Council-formal term). The older name **Flesh-Eaters** is preserved as the surface-society popular term — narrowly accurate (they do eat) but understating the actual identity. Both names remain in circulation; *Flesh-Eaters* survives in popular speech and in older raw chronicles, while *Flesh-Crafters* is the canonical current term used by the cabal itself, the Council, and informed dragons.
3. **Doctrine reframed.** The cabal's core conviction now has *two intertwined faces*: dragons as apex predators (the older surface-readable face) AND dragons as apex *craftsmen* who fashion the parts of lesser races into themselves (the deeper structural face). The predation-as-natural-order is the opening phase of a craft tradition that ends on the workbench, the surgical chair, and the wearer's own bone.
4. **Major new section: What they harvest.** Replaces the previous unicorn-monolithic framing with a multi-race material catalog:
   - **Eyes** — from races with magically-enhanced sight (eagle-eyed humans, twilight-vision elves, far-sighted halflings, scryers, divinatory priests). Grafted into bespoke scale-sockets across the wearer's neck/shoulders/back; each continues to see at its original owner's last refresh-rate. The most prized are eyes of victims whose last sight was the Flesh-Crafter who took them — the Flesh-Crafter then sees himself killing forever, from the victim's POV.
   - **Limbs** — from artisans, fighters, dancers, healers, miners, scribes. Grafted limbs retain signature movements; senior Flesh-Crafters become composites of eight-or-more arms each performing harvested craftsmen's habitual gestures.
   - **Internal organs flush with mana** — hearts of mages, livers of priests, lungs of singers, vocal cords of bards, brains of telepaths (consumed in ritual meals rather than grafted), reproductive organs of fertility-cult initiates. Grafted organs slowly fail under dark-Eldritch preservation and produce ongoing magical leakage that the wearer harvests as personal power. The cabal's only canonical access to psionics is via consumed telepath brains — a debasement of the unicorn-given gift the Great Exchange originally taught dragonkind.
   - **Bones and reinforcement** — skull plates as chest armor, giant femurs as spinal struts, ribs as cage-armor.
   - **Other harvests** — glands, scales, hair (woven into brow-cloths). The catalog is open; new harvest categories enter the cabal's repertoire roughly once a generation.
5. **Horn-crowns repositioned** as ONE specialty (the most ritually elaborate, the most jealously cultivated, the *constitution* line that determines cabal hierarchy) within the broader composite craft. Mainstream understanding sometimes mistakenly assumes horn-crowns are the whole practice — they are not; they are the keystone specialty.
6. **"A note on the name" → "A note on the names."** Section reframed to discuss both names: *Flesh-Eaters* (older, surface, narrow) and *Flesh-Crafters* (deeper, current, full). Speaking either in polite company remains poor taste. Indirect references expanded: *the rejectionist cells, the egg-thieves, **the harvesters, the bone-fitters,** those who have not heard the Council.*

**Scope-breadth correction.** The morning's Brutal Team panel content (Chorus-amplified atrocities, horn-crowns, the Eldest Elder, etc.) was retained as canon — none of it is being deprecated — but it is now **contextualized as the unicorn-line specialty** within the broader cross-race craft tradition. The unicorn material is no longer the whole identity; it is the most-developed *specialty*. Future content development for this faction (in panels or otherwise) should distribute across multiple races, not anchor on unicorns.

### Pages updated

- `flesh-crafters.md` (renamed from `flesh-eaters.md`):
   - Title and H1 updated to *The Flesh-Crafters*.
   - Summary rewritten with crafter-first framing.
   - Doctrine section rewritten to add the *apex craftsmen* second face.
   - **New top-level section "What they harvest"** added between Practices and Horn-crowns covering the cross-race material catalog (eyes, limbs, organs, bones, other).
   - Horn-crowns intro rewritten to reposition as one specialty among many, while preserving all the existing horn-crown content (grafting, visual, pin code, daily maintenance, inverted Chorus, eldest case pointer, cabal's constitution).
   - The Eldest Elder section unchanged (still Flesh-Crafters-internal canon).
   - "A note on the name" → "A note on the names" — full rewrite to handle both names.
   - Sources line preserves *The Flesh-Eaters.txt* as the actual raw filename.
- `dragons.md` — Modern Dissidents section rewritten to reflect the crafter framing and the multi-race harvest. All `Flesh-Eaters` text references → `Flesh-Crafters`. Wikilink target updated.
- `unicorns.md` — All `Flesh-Eaters` references → `Flesh-Crafters`. Modern violation subsection content unchanged (still accurately describes the unicorn-targeting practices, which are the cabal's most prestigious specialty). Wikilink target updated.
- `ratharil.md` — All `Flesh-Eaters` references → `Flesh-Crafters`. Notable Council Action section's wording updated. Source filename restored to *The Flesh-Eaters.txt*.
- `unicorn-plains.md` — All `Flesh-Eaters` references → `Flesh-Crafters`.
- `great-exchange.md` — All `Flesh-Eaters` references → `Flesh-Crafters`.
- `index.md` — Antagonist Entities entry rewritten to lead with the multi-race harvest (eyes, limbs, organs) and to mark horn-crowns as the most prestigious specialty. Display text now uses `[[flesh-crafters|Flesh-Crafters]]` to render properly.

### Memory implications

- **New feedback memory: `feedback-villain-scope-breadth.md`** — When developing antagonist faction practices/atrocities/aesthetics, distribute across multiple races rather than anchoring heavily on one. Curator's preference, not a universal rule.
- The earlier 2026-05-02 (evening, third entry) Brutal Team panel save log entry remains canonical for the unicorn-horn-crown content; the content itself has been rebalanced as a specialty within the new broader frame.
- Past log entries (2026-05-02 ingest of `The Flesh-Eaters.txt`; the first Brutal Team panel save; the second Brutal Team panel save) **are left as historical record** and continue to refer to the cabal as Flesh-Eaters. This is appropriate — the log records what canon was at the time of each change.
- The `feedback-spelling.md` memory probably wants a small entry noting the Flesh-Eaters → Flesh-Crafters rename so future ingests of older raw sources that use *Flesh-Eaters* know to interpret it as the older popular name for the canonical *Flesh-Crafters*. (To-do, not done in this save.)

### Open canon (specific to this pivot)

- **Whether the rename is in-world historical (the cabal evolved from Flesh-Eaters to Flesh-Crafters across some named historical transition) or terminological (the cabal was always Flesh-Crafters; the older name reflected outsider misunderstanding).** Page currently leans terminological-with-deepening-mainstream-understanding; in-world historical-evolution reading remains canonically possible.
- **Which non-cabal races have surviving accounts of being harvested for which body parts** — the page lists harvest categories by victim race-type but does not name specific historical incidents.
- **Whether any Flesh-Crafter has ever been physically deconstructed** by the Council to examine the integration of multiple grafts — the surgical autopsy of a captured Crafter would be a major intelligence event; canon is silent.
- **The cabal's surgeon class.** Every cell has at least one surgeon (per the horn-crown grafting account). Whether surgeons are themselves Flesh-Crafter-raised cohorts, hereditary like the apprentice-feeders, recruited from outside — undocumented.

## 2026-05-02 (late evening, third pivot) — Crafter/Eater historical layering + cabal population locked at <100

**Source**: Three-message curator clarification, 2026-05-02:

1. *"Maybe the flesh-crafters were the older branch, but modern day eats more than unicorns. Horn horses are delicious, no doubt about it, but humanoids are tasty snacks too."*
2. *"less than 100 total"*
3. *"100 at any given time, they replace their numbers by stealing eggs"*

This refines the previous Flesh-Eaters → Flesh-Crafters rename: rather than treating the two names as *outsider-shallow vs. insider-deep* labels for the same modern practice, the canon now treats them as **historical layers** of the same cabal:

- **Flesh-Crafters** = the older, ancestral, more refined harvest-and-craft tradition. The cabal's idealized self-image. Selective predation; victims chosen for their integratable parts.
- **Flesh-Eaters** = the modern, broader-practice expansion. The cabal still does the old craft work, but modern members also eat humanoids casually as *snacks* and unicorns (cabal slang: *horn horses*) as gourmet course.

**Older purists within the cabal regard the modern broader eating as *decline*** — a falling-away from disciplined harvest into mere gluttony. This is the cabal's first documented internal political tension.

**Headline canon additions and refinements**:

1. **Two-register predation model.** *Material* = victims taken specifically to harvest integratable parts (the old refined work). *Snacks* = humanoid sapients eaten opportunistically with no harvesting purpose (the modern broader practice). Modern Flesh-Crafters do both; cabal status depends on the composite (the work), not on the snack count.
2. **Cabal-internal slang locked in canon:**
   - ***Horn horses*** = unicorns (casual register; *unicorn* reserved for formal craft-work register)
   - ***Snacks*** = humanoid sapients eaten opportunistically (humans, halflings, gnomes, goblins, orcs, oceanic peoples)
   - ***Material*** = sapients destined for harvest (opposed to *snacks*)
   - ***The work*** = the surgical fashioning of harvested parts onto a wearer
   - ***Decline*** = older purists' internal critique of younger members who eat broadly without harvesting intent
3. **Population locked at <100 steady-state.** The entire cabal numbers fewer than one hundred dragons at any given time, distributed across all cells worldwide. This resolves the previously-open *numerical strength* canon item.
4. **Egg-theft is load-bearing for cabal continuity.** The cabal does not (in any documented form) reproduce internally — its <100 steady-state population is sustained entirely through the ongoing theft of eggs from Council-aligned clans plus the cohort indoctrination pipeline that turns each stolen egg into a finished Flesh-Crafter several decades later. *Stop the egg-theft pipeline → starve the cabal*. This gives the Council its most leveraged strategic option (sustained nest-defense + stolen-egg recovery campaigns), though wilderness reach and cell secrecy have so far prevented sustained interdiction.
5. **Indirect-reference vocabulary expanded.** Mainstream dragon polite-society indirections for the cabal now include *the snackers* alongside the existing *the rejectionist cells / the egg-thieves / the harvesters / the bone-fitters / those who have not heard the Council*.
6. **Two new open-canon items**: whether the cabal ever reproduces internally (probably not, but reasons undocumented); roughly how many eggs the cabal must steal per generation to maintain ~100 steady-state.

### Pages updated

- `flesh-crafters.md`:
   - Summary expanded to mention the modern broader-eating wing and the *snacks* / *horn horses* slang.
   - Doctrine section unchanged in core; the historical-vs-modern tension is captured in the new layered framing of "A note on the names" and in the two-register predation model in Practices.
   - **Practices → Systematic predation subsection rewritten** to introduce the two registers (*material harvest* and *snacks*) with the cabal's own distinction between them.
   - **"A note on the name" → "A note on the names" rewritten again** to reflect the historical layering: Crafters = older ancestral idealized; Eaters = modern broader actual-practice; modern cabal is both. New **Cabal-internal terms** subsection added with the canonical slang inventory.
   - **Status section gains "Numerical strength" subsection** locking the <100 figure, the steady-state framing, the egg-theft replenishment mechanism, and the strategic implication for Council interdiction.
   - Open canon resolves the previously-open numerical strength item; adds two new questions (internal reproduction; eggs-per-generation math).
- `index.md` — Antagonist Entities entry refreshed to include the <100 figure, the two-register framing, and the *snacks* / *horn horses* slang.

### Memory implications

- The `feedback-villain-scope-breadth.md` memory continues to apply — the page is now broader than just unicorn-targeting.
- The `feedback-spelling.md` memory should at some point note the Flesh-Eaters / Flesh-Crafters dual-name canon for future ingest of older raw sources that use either name. (To-do, not done in this entry.)
- No other memory updates required.

### Open canon (specific to this pivot)

- **Whether the older "Crafter purists" inside the modern cabal constitute a faction** with named leaders, or whether *Decline*-criticism is just a generational grumble.
- **Whether the modern broader-eating wing has its own internal name within the cabal** (analogous to the *Crafter* purist faction).
- **Whether the *Flesh-Eaters* name was ever adopted by the cabal itself** at any historical point, or whether it has always been an outsider-imposed term that the cabal merely tolerates.
- **The historical transition** from "Crafters-only" to "Crafters + casual Eaters" — when did broader predation become normalized? Was there a triggering event?
- **Whether other dragon factions (or non-cabal dragons) ever defect *into* the cabal** as adults, or whether 100% of cabal membership comes through the stolen-egg pipeline.

## 2026-05-02 (late evening, fourth pivot) — Wipeout-and-rebirth continuity model + "meat is meat"

**Source**: Two-message curator clarification, 2026-05-02:

1. *"not unbroken, wiped out many times, reborn from ancient caches of philosophy buried by earlier flesh-eaters. Always reborn."*
2. *"flesh eaters dismiss criticism with 'meat is meat'"*

These resolve two previously-open canon items at once: the cabal's *age and continuity* model, and the doctrinal substance behind the Crafter-vs-Eater internal split.

**Headline canon additions**:

1. **The cabal is not an unbroken tradition.** It has been **wiped out many times across draconic history** — by Council task forces, mainstream-clan vengeance, combined dragon-and-unicorn campaigns, and outside catastrophes including the Demon War. Each eradication is total or near-total: cells destroyed, holds burned, surviving members hunted, horn-crowns shattered or melted to deny inheritance.
2. **Always reborn.** Each generation of Flesh-Crafters knows it may be wiped out and prepares accordingly: they **deliberately bury caches of their philosophy** in hidden locations long before any imminent eradication, sometimes centuries before. The caches contain the cabal's foundational doctrines, surgical knowledge, rearing protocols, indoctrination rites, internal vocabulary, and personal letters from old Flesh-Crafters addressed to whatever future dragon may one day find them. A finder who is *taken* by the philosophy reconstitutes the cabal from the cache alone.
3. **The Buried Philosophy.** Caches are most often hidden in the ruins of ancient draconic empires (already a cabal hiding-place; many ruins now hold caches stacked across multiple wipeout cycles), in old destroyed Flesh-Crafter holds, and at unmarked locations indicated by clues planted in publicly-accessible draconic archives.
4. **"Always reborn"** is the cabal's motto across the cycles, carved into nearly every cache lid and every hold's foundation stones. The cabal regards its own mortality as temporary — *individual* Flesh-Crafters die, *the cabal* only sleeps in the caches between revivals.
5. **The Council can wipe out a generation but never the philosophy.** No Council has ever found and destroyed all the caches; the cabal has buried more than the Council can ever locate, and continues to bury new ones whenever it is active.
6. **The Decline cycle is structural, not accidental.** Each revival starts from the *pure* philosophy of the caches; subsequent generations broaden into modern *Decline* eating practice; eventually the broader cabal is eradicated again; new caches buried before eradication wait for the next finder. The current cabal is **the latest revival**, not the original.
7. **"Meat is meat"** is the Eaters wing's compressed counter-doctrine, used to dismiss the Crafter purists' *Decline* criticism. There is no metaphysical hierarchy elevating *material* over *snack*; food is food; the older insistence on disciplined harvest is sentimentality, not moral fact. The cabal's most-quoted modern saying. *The work* remains worth doing for its prestige and the composite power it confers, but eating freely outside the work is no betrayal of cabal identity. Most modern Flesh-Crafters hold both positions at once: doing the work when the opportunity is right, snacking when it isn't, reciting *meat is meat* when an older purist objects.

### Pages updated

- `flesh-crafters.md`:
   - **New top-level section "The cycle of wipeout and rebirth"** added after Status, with subsections *The Buried Philosophy* and *"Always reborn"*. Documents the cabal's non-continuous tradition, the cache mechanism, the locations where caches are buried, the cabal's motto, and the Council's structural inability to permanently eradicate the philosophy.
   - **Practices → Systematic predation subsection expanded** with the Eaters' *"meat is meat"* counter-doctrine, framing the Crafter-vs-Eater split as a real ideological dispute with two named opposing sayings (*Decline* vs. *meat is meat*).
   - **Cabal-internal terms table expanded** with *meat is meat* row.
   - **Open canon** resolves the previously-open *age of the cabal* item with the wipeout-and-rebirth model.
- `index.md` — Antagonist Entities entry refreshed to mention the *"meat is meat"* saying and the *"Always reborn"* motto and wipeout-rebirth cycle.

### Memory implications

- Existing memories continue to apply.
- The wipeout-rebirth model is canonically interesting in its own right and may be useful for analogous structural questions about other long-lived heretical groups in Eadras (if any are introduced later). No new memory file warranted yet.

### Open canon (specific to this pivot)

- **The number of preceding revivals.** The cabal's own internal records (preserved across cycles via the cache system) presumably include a count, but the count is not known outside the cabal.
- **The contents of a typical cache** beyond the broad inventory given (foundational doctrines, surgical knowledge, rearing protocols, indoctrination rites, internal vocabulary, personal letters). Specific cache-objects, ritual implements, preserved horn-crown fragments, or other named contents undocumented.
- **Whether any cache has ever been found by mainstream draconic society and destroyed before a finder could read it.** The Council presumably tries, but specific successful seizures are not documented.
- **Whether the cabal salts mainstream archives with cache-pointer clues actively** (a sustained ongoing operation requiring active members) or whether the existing salted clues are residue from previous active cycles.
- **The historical transition** between *Decline* phases of one cycle and *purification* phases of the next — does the philosophy actually self-purify each rebirth, or do successive rebirths accumulate downstream Decline more quickly?
- **Whether the Crafter purists' political faction inside the modern cabal** preserves continuity with the immediate-post-rebirth pure phase of *this* cycle, or whether they are themselves Decline-era purists looking back at an even-purer past.

## 2026-05-02 (late evening) — Ingest: The Neverborn update

**Source ingested**: `The Neverborn update.txt` (3,315 bytes; written 2026-05-02 19:11).

A focused source that **substantially refines the Neverborn canon** — sharpening the entity's nature from "passive Chaos remnant that lingers" to "fascination-driven entity for which the seals do not matter." No spelling discrepancies; no hard contradictions, but several existing framings (notably the "punched through the seal" framing of the Chaos Crusades) sharpened by the deeper truth that the Neverborn does not need the hole to be open at all.

**Headline canonical refinements**:

1. **Chaos defined poetically.** *"A place where everything everywhere all at once, and nothing anywhere ever, are both simultaneously and completely true. A rational mind simply cannot understand it."* Most entities that flash into existence in Chaos *are not destroyed; they simply cease to have ever been.*
2. **The Neverborn lingered.** *Not born. Not eternal. Not even properly real. It simply remained where remaining was ontologically impossible. A pre-ontological accident. A thing that should have un-happened the instant it occurred.* (This refines but does not contradict existing canon.)
3. **Presumably others elsewhere.** Across the infinite Omniverse there are presumably other Neverborn-class entities — pre-ontological accidents that lingered against the odds. **But this one is the only one that has ever shown any interest in this particular Mythos. Eadras has its full, undivided, alien attention.** This expands the canon: there is a *class* of Neverborn-style entities; "the Neverborn" specifically refers to the one Eadras knows.
4. **Fascination is the central characterization.** The Neverborn does not hate, does not desire worship, has no goals/malice/agenda. **It is simply fascinated by the fact that something as ordered and coherent as Eadras exists at all.** This is now the page's foundational characterization, replacing the older "lingerer that may or may not have intentions" framing.
5. **Contact with Kudur-eṭir refined.** The Neverborn *did not come through the hole* — it pressed itself against the wound *like a blind, amorphous thing slowly oozing its awareness through a crack in the skin of existence.* It answered no summons; it answered an *impossibility* — the precise mathematical shape of the wound Kudur-eṭir had carved into reality. Kudur-eṭir received not knowledge but *unnatural, deeply anti-life, completely insane understanding* that a rational mind was never meant to survive. Contact with a non-entity's non-mind is **devastating**.
6. **THE MAJOR REVEAL: the Neverborn never needed the hole open.** The gods sealed the First Breach perfectly after the Cataclysm and after each of the Chaos Crusades. **The seals were perfect. They were absolute. They held.** And the Neverborn opened the aperture again twice anyway. The deeper truth (which not even the Tome of Baldaran is sure how to express): the Neverborn does not require the seal to be tampered with. The First Breach gave it a *foothold* — an outline against which to define its noticing — and once it had that outline, it can open the aperture by deciding to notice it again, no matter how perfect the seal. **The gods believe they sealed the wound. They only sealed the hole.**
7. **The ultimate threat reframed.** The cosmologically worst-case scenario is not Chaos invasion. It is that one day the Neverborn may simply decide that *the distinction between "inside" and "outside" is no longer interesting — and stop respecting it.* There is no defense against this. There is no warning before this. The gods understand this in the abstract but have no means to address it directly. They can seal apertures; they cannot seal the Neverborn's fascination.
8. **The "every year the line grows thinner" framing.** The Neverborn does not invade. It does not corrupt. It simply lingers. And every year it lingers, the line between *what is real* and *what should never have been able to perceive the real* grows slightly thinner.
9. **Cthosh reconciled.** The older folk-attribution name *Cthosh* (which appears in `chaos.md` as if it were the entity's "true name") is now folded into the Neverborn names list as one more Arathi-era title. The fact that some Arathi-derived traditions treat *Cthosh* as a real name is itself canonically interesting — once enough mages spoke the name, the Neverborn acquired a faintly more solid outline in those traditions, which is presumably part of why the name persists.

### Pages updated

- `neverborn.md`:
   - Summary expanded to lead with the *fascinated, not hostile* framing and the *seals do not matter* fact.
   - **What the Neverborn Is** rewritten with the new poetic Chaos definition, the *lingered* framing, and the *presumably others elsewhere / Eadras has its full undivided attention* canon.
   - **Names** section expanded with *Cthosh* and a note on why this folk-name persists.
   - **Contact with Kudur-eṭir** rewritten with the *blind amorphous oozing*, *answered an impossibility*, and *unnatural anti-life understanding* refinements.
   - **The Danger** restructured to lead with the *fascination is worse than hatred* thesis (cannot negotiate, cannot predict, cannot threaten, cannot comprehend the shape of attention). Adds new subsections: *Conceptual contamination, not armies*; *The ultimate threat* (with the *stop respecting the distinction* framing).
   - **Secret subsection rewritten** as *The seals were real. The Neverborn never needed the hole.* Documents the deeper truth that the seals worked exactly as designed and the Neverborn worked around them by not requiring the hole at all. Closes with *The gods believe they sealed the wound. They only sealed the hole.*
   - Sources field expanded; *Last updated* bumped to 2026-05-02.
- `chaos-crusades.md`:
   - *The seal between Crusades* section refined to align with the deeper canon: seals were perfect AND irrelevant; the Neverborn used the First Breach as an outline-foothold and can open the aperture by deciding to notice no matter how perfect the seal. Cross-link to the new Neverborn section.
   - Sources field expanded; *Last updated* bumped to 2026-05-02.

### Memory implications

- Existing memories continue to apply. The earlier `project-worldbreaker-first-breach.md` memory about the First Breach geometry is unaffected — the breach location (Mythos Shell) and the Worldbreaker path remain canonical. The Neverborn refinement adds depth to *what the Neverborn does with* the breach, not where the breach is.
- The `feedback-spelling.md` memory probably wants a small note that *Cthosh* in `chaos.md` is canonically one of the Neverborn's older folk names, not a separate entity. (To-do, not done in this entry.)

### Open canon (specific to this update)

- **The other Neverborn-class entities elsewhere in the Omniverse.** Now confirmed to exist *presumably*; their nature, locations, and what (if anything) they have noticed are not part of Eadran canon and are unlikely to be — they belong to the cosmologies of other Mythoi.
- **What the Neverborn would do if it stopped respecting the inside/outside distinction.** By definition unanswerable.
- **Whether the Spear's Neverborn-anchor mechanism (each use teaches the Neverborn how to remain) has any limit** — i.e., does sufficient accumulated anchor-shadow at some point change the Neverborn's relationship to the Mythos, or is the anchor effect strictly additive without phase change?
- **Whether the *Cthosh* folk-name has ever been used by anyone other than Arathi-derived traditions** — and whether the Arathi traditions themselves understood Cthosh as the same entity later called the Neverborn.
- **Whether there are signs an observer could detect that the Neverborn's fascination has *intensified* recently** — e.g., changes in the line-thinning rate, new locations of impossibility incidents, etc. Canon is silent.

## 2026-05-03 — Ingest: Flesh eaters revised + Lairs and Contingency Planning (full canon overwrite)

**Sources ingested**:
1. `Flesh eaters revised.txt` — revised faction doctrine. Opens with the explicit overwrite directive *"Flesh crafters is incorrect, the following is correct"*. Includes a long opening vignette (the Marrin / Lysa Fen / abandoned-village sequence).
2. *Lairs and Contingency Planning* — saved inline-delivered canon as `raw/Flesh-eater lairs and contingency.txt`. Substantial additional detail on the cell's lair architecture, fallback systems, movement discipline, and failure modes.

This is a **full canon overwrite** of the prior `wiki/flesh-crafters.md` page. The body-horror surgical layer (horn-crowns, grafted eyes/limbs/organs, the Eldest Elder, chorus-amplified atrocity, horn-powder trade) is **deleted from canon** and not preserved as a separate faction. The cult is now a much leaner predator-cult: *everything not dragon is prey*.

### Curator decisions during ingest

- **Body-horror layer entirely removed.** No horn-crowns, no grafted parts, no Eldest Elder, no surgical craft.
- **Vignette included** as an italicized flavor block at the top of the new page. *(Curator noted vignette intros will become a recurring pattern; this page is the precedent.)*
- **Rearing chamber kept**, but scoped down: rendered-fat walls, first-meal humanoid liver with crooning, educational meat with bite-record streaks. **Throwbacks/walling-and-starving and the control-case kill-test removed.** Indoctrination now treated as producing complete ideological control.
- **Council-Draconic mockery sub-section kept** — fits the new tone, not body-horror.
- **Fear cultivation reframed as side effect.** The hunting pattern is driven by secrecy discipline; the resulting fear is incidental. *They genuinely do not care about the feelings of prey.* Fear is welcome only as a flavoring (thinking creatures taste better when afraid) — appetite, not cruelty as policy.
- **Backup plans / lair canon emphasized** per curator direction; the Lairs and Contingency Planning section is now a substantial top-level area of the page.
- **Light pass** on inbound links: rename only, plus minimum sentence-level cleanup for references to deleted concepts.

### Pages created

- `flesh-eaters.md` — new page replacing `flesh-crafters.md`. Opens with the full vignette as an italicized flavor block. Sections: Doctrine; Cabal terminology (table including new term *not even snacks*); Practices (with the side-effect-not-aim reframe); Territorial behavior (corpse-drops as standard draconic signal turned to abnormal target); Organization; **Lairs and contingency planning** (Primary lair / Secondary lairs at 200–500 miles / Emergency shelters / Movement and relocation / Entry and exit protocols / Deception and misdirection / Failure modes / Special case: ruin lairs); Counter-hunt behavior; Discovery conditions; Reproduction and recruitment with The rearing chamber and The Council-Draconic mockery subsections; **Continuity — the buried caches** (now featuring the **psychic resonance crystal with imprinted personality** as the cache centerpiece, replacing the older "personal letters" framing); Rebirth cycle; *"Always reborn"*; Susceptibility to conversion (ennui, dissatisfaction, curiosity, arrogance); Status with Numerical strength and Draconic response (9-dragon minimum, 27+ near settlements); Open canon.

### Pages deleted

- `flesh-crafters.md` — superseded entirely; not preserved.

### Pages updated (light pass on inbound links)

- `dragons.md` — *Modern Dissidents — the Flesh-Crafters* section renamed *Modern Dissidents — the Flesh-Eaters*; rewritten to drop body-horror references and reframe as predator-cult; cache-rebirth flagged. Wikilink target updated.
- `unicorns.md` — *Modern violation: the Flesh-Crafters* section renamed and rewritten without the chorus-amplified atrocity tactics, horn-grafting traffic, or horn-powder trade (all deleted from canon). Horns subsection trimmed of the Flesh-Crafter dark-Eldritch horn-grafting paragraph. Wikilink target updated.
- `ratharil.md` — *Notable standing Council action* section renamed and rewritten; egg-theft offense kept (still canonical), surrounding doctrine simplified. Source citation updated to the new raw filename. Wikilink target updated.
- `great-exchange.md` — Summary and *Modern position of the Exchange* section renamed; references to specifically-targeting-unicorns trimmed (the new doctrine treats unicorns as preferred prey but not exclusive target). Wikilink target updated.
- `unicorn-plains.md` — *The Plains today* paragraph renamed; cult continues not to respect the dragon-restriction norm. Wikilink target updated.
- `index.md` — Antagonist Entities entry rewritten to lead with predator-cult framing, layered lairs, corpse-drops, the *not even snacks* tier, and the psychic resonance crystal in the caches. Wikilink target updated.

### Raw files added

- `raw/Flesh eaters revised.txt` (curator-provided file, primary source for this rewrite).
- `raw/Flesh-eater lairs and contingency.txt` (saved inline-delivered canon block).

### Memory implications

- `project-flesh-crafters-canon.md` is now **stale** and rewritten as `project-flesh-eaters-canon.md` (or rewritten in place — see memory section). The 2026-05-02 elaborate body-horror canon documented there is no longer canonical. The curator-collaborative *rebuild* date stands as historical context but the page itself has been replaced by a leaner version.
- `feedback-villain-scope-breadth.md` continues to apply and was structurally honored by the new doctrine: the cult now distributes predation across all sapient races by size category rather than anchoring heavily on unicorns.
- A note: **vignette intros are becoming a wiki pattern.** This page is the first; future ingest sources are expected to deliver them. May warrant a memory entry once a second example exists.

### Open canon (specific to this overwrite)

- **The technology behind the psychic resonance crystals.** Whether they are draconic-magitek, an inheritance from earlier traditions ([[arathi|Arathi]] memory-crystal heritage is the structurally obvious candidate), or something else — and whether imprinting requires the testator's death.
- **What happens when a finder reads a cache and is *not* taken** by the philosophy. Can they leave with the crystal intact, destroy it, report its location? Canon silent.
- **The *not even snacks* tier and small humanoid populations.** Whether gnome/halfling/goblin populations have ever recognized that they are *passed over* by Flesh-Eater predation, and whether this has ever produced an unusual relationship with the cult or its hunting grounds. Canon silent.
- **Whether the corpse-drop signal is read by mainstream dragons** and (if so) whether the recognition produces an automatic Council escalation — the territorial-marking is *standard* draconic behavior, so a dragon flying over a sapient corpse-drop would presumably read it as *another dragon's claim with abnormal target* rather than a generic atrocity scene.
- **The hereditary basis (if any) of cell composition.** Whether cells preserve generational continuity within themselves (apprenticeship, mentor-protégé) or whether each rebirth from a cache produces a fresh structure with no inherited cell-internal lineage.

## 2026-05-03 (refinement) — Flesh-Eater self-conception: survival, not cowardice

**Source**: Curator direction, 2026-05-03: *"They justify all their behavior as survival, not cowardice. Tell themselves that council and draconic society are cowards for not being free, like they are. Do not see irony."*

A focused refinement to the new Flesh-Eaters page. Adds the cult's self-conception as a doctrinal layer — the **inversion of evaluations** by which the cult reframes its operational reality (hiding, fleeing, abandoning lairs, dying nine-against-one) as *freedom* and the Council's open civilization as *cowardice*.

### Headline canon additions

1. **Survival, not cowardice.** The Flesh-Eaters justify every aspect of their operational practice — the layered lairs, the rapid retreats, the storm-cover relocations, the lair-abandonment, the small-cell structure — as *survival, not cowardice*. Only the weak bind themselves to a place they cannot defend or to a society they cannot leave.
2. **The cowardice charge inverted.** The Council and mainstream draconic society are framed as *the cowards* — beholden to treaties, hierarchies, and unicorn-given cooperation, having lost the nerve to be free. *They are free; the Council is afraid to be free.*
3. **No self-recognition of the irony.** They spend their entire lives hiding, fleeing, and dying in coordinated hunts, and call it freedom. The Council's ability to fly openly and meet under the sky without fear reads to them as degeneration. **The reframe is total** — a Flesh-Eater notices not what his daily life looks like but only what his ideology says it means.
4. **Why this matters mechanically.** This is the mental architecture that makes the cult *resistant to argument* and gives its appeal to dissatisfied/arrogant Council dragons its hook. A Flesh-Eater has not rejected mainstream draconic *practices* — he has accepted a complete inversion of its *evaluations*. To convert him is to undo not a position but a worldview.

### Pages updated

- `flesh-eaters.md` — new top-level section *Self-conception: survival, not cowardice* added between *Doctrine* and *Cabal terminology*. Cross-links to *Susceptibility to conversion* and to the [[ratharil#The Court of the Unanswered Sun|Court of the Unanswered Sun]] (the canonical example of dragons gathering under open sky without fear, which the Flesh-Eaters read as proof of decadence).

### Memory implications

- `project-flesh-eaters-canon.md` updated with the self-conception doctrinal layer.
- This refinement structurally clarifies why the cult *cannot* be argued out of its position — useful context for any future scene involving captured Flesh-Eaters, returnees, or attempted negotiation. A Council dragon reasoning at a Flesh-Eater is not making a category error; he is talking *across an inverted evaluative frame* in which his own evidence is the proof he is wrong.

---

## 2026-05-03 — Ingest: Flesh-eater ideological framing and perception

**Source ingested**: Curator-supplied canon block (saved as `raw/Flesh-eater ideological framing and perception.txt`). Three structured sections: *Ideological Framing and Self-Justification*, *Perception and Identification*, and *Perception by Others*.

This is the **canonical full version** of what the prior 2026-05-03 refinement (*Flesh-Eater self-conception: survival, not cowardice*) sketched. It supersedes the inferred section I wrote earlier the same day with the curator's structured framework, and it adds two entirely new perception-axis sections describing how the cult is *identified* and *judged* by outsiders.

### Headline canon additions

1. **Three core principles.** The cult judges all actions by: *Survival is the only meaningful measure of strength; Freedom is the absence of imposed restraint; Predation is the natural and proper expression of dragonhood.*
2. **Inversion table.** Outside reading vs. Flesh-Eater reading: *secrecy → strategic movement; relocation → efficient survival; avoidance → intelligent predation*. Capstone: *"Remaining unseen is not cowardice. It is control."*
3. **The Council-vs-cult opposition table.** *Others obey laws; they obey only necessity. Others restrain themselves; they act freely. Others coexist; they dominate.* Reinforces identity as superior.
4. **The Freedom Doctrine** (three lines): *Freedom is the right to take what you can. Survival proves legitimacy. Anything that limits predation is weakness.* Applies equally to hunting prey, avoiding stronger enemies, abandoning territory — no perceived contradiction. *Fleeing a superior force is survival; hunting the weak is freedom.*
5. **Outcomes define truth.** The doctrine is self-validating: *if they survive, they are correct; if others die, those others were weak.*
6. **Two-category outsider classification.** Most sapient populations do not know the term *Flesh-Eater* and instead classify dragons as **Civilized** (don't attack on sight; may communicate; can exist near settlements) or **Monstrous** (attack without warning; kill and consume; no restraint). Flesh-Eaters fall entirely in the second category.
7. **The first-contact rule.** *A dragon that does not attack immediately is assumed civilized; a dragon that attacks immediately is assumed monstrous. Often this is the only distinction that matters.*
8. **Lack of terminology in surface populations.** Encounters described experientially: *"It came out of the sky." / "It took them." / "It ate them."* Knowledge is experiential, not theoretical. Among dragons and informed scholars the cult is recognized as a specific cult and named threat, but this knowledge is not widely shared.
9. **Mainstream draconic judgment.** The cult is read as **fundamentally sick, not merely dangerous** — *warped, degenerate, fundamentally wrong*. A sickness within dragonkind rather than a faction within it. Judgment arises from predation on sapient beings, *deliberate cultivation of suffering* (outside reading; the inside reality is appetite + secrecy discipline — but the behavioral signature is indistinguishable from outside, and the distinction is irrelevant to victims), and total rejection of restraint.
10. **New canonical euphemism set.** *"those who have not heard the Council" / "the egg-thieves" / "the hunters who forgot themselves"*. The third is new to canon; the first two were inherited from the previous canon. Older body-horror-specific euphemisms (*the harvesters, the bone-fitters, the snackers*) are retired with the body-horror layer.
11. **Non-draconic perception.** To non-dragons, Flesh-Eaters are not a defined group; they are *monstrous dragons, aberrations, proof that dragons can become predators of civilization.* Reactions: **revulsion, disbelief, denial, panic.** Even people familiar with dragons struggle to reconcile expected dragon behavior with cult behavior. **The cult breaks expectation before it breaks bodies** — forcing observers to confront that dragons can violate assumed limits and that safety is conditional.

### Inside vs. outside framing — preserved tension

The new canon explicitly notes the **inside/outside divergence on cultivation of suffering.** The earlier 2026-05-03 ingest established that the cult does not deliberately terrorize prey — fear is a side effect of secrecy discipline, with fear-as-flavoring as the only positive interest. The new perception canon says mainstream dragons read the cult as *deliberately cultivating suffering*. Both are canon: the *behavioral signature* is indistinguishable from outside, the *internal motivation* is appetite-plus-secrecy. Cross-reference now embedded in the Perception section.

### Pages updated

- `flesh-eaters.md`:
   - The earlier *Self-conception: survival, not cowardice* section (added 2026-05-03 morning) is **replaced in full** by the structured *Ideological framing and self-justification* section, with seven sub-sections (*Core belief / Interpretation of their own behavior / Perception of dragon society / Internal contrast / The Freedom Doctrine / Lack of self-awareness / The irony*). Closing paragraph from the prior section preserved as the section's exit (*"resistant to argument… complete inversion of evaluations"*).
   - **New top-level section** *Perception by others*, between *Ideological framing* and *Cabal terminology*. Two sub-sections: *How outsiders identify them* (two-category classification, first-contact rule, experiential vocabulary) and *How the cult is judged by those who know* (mainstream draconic *fundamentally sick* judgment, three-source basis, cross-reference to Practices for the inside-vs-outside divergence on suffering, euphemism set, non-draconic *monstrous dragons* perception with reactions and the *break-expectation* line).
   - Sources field updated to include `Flesh-eater ideological framing and perception.txt`.

### Memory implications

- `project-flesh-eaters-canon.md` updated with the structured ideological framing and the new perception-axis canon (two-category outsider classification, three-euphemism set, *fundamentally sick* judgment).
- The inside/outside divergence on *deliberate cultivation of suffering* is a useful structural fact for future writing: two different things can be canonically true about the same behavior depending on who reads it. Could generalize to other antagonist factions; flagging here, no separate memory yet.

### Open canon (specific to this ingest)

- **Whether informed scholars in surface civilizations have a *name* for the cult that differs from the draconic *Flesh-Eaters*.** Surface populations don't use the draconic term; whether scholars who *do* understand the cult use the same term, a Common-language equivalent, or a euphemism of their own is undocumented.
- **Whether any non-draconic faction (the [[black-hand|Black Hand]], a particular kingdom's intelligence service, an order of [[order-sharanel|sorcerers]]) has independently catalogued Flesh-Eater activity** at a level that approaches draconic understanding. Canon silent.
- **The specific historical incident behind *"the hunters who forgot themselves."*** The phrase implies a remembered event in which dragons recognized a deviation from proper predation; whether it refers to a specific named episode or to a general pattern is undocumented.
- **Whether the *first-contact rule* has produced documented misclassifications** in either direction (a civilized dragon mistakenly killed by panicked surface forces; a Flesh-Eater initially trusted because the first encounter was non-aggressive).
- **Whether non-draconic understanding of the cult has any historical depth** — i.e., are there surface-civilization records of past wipeout cycles, or does each rebirth rediscover the cult fresh from the surface side as well as the draconic side?
