## 2026-05-03 — Lint sweep (items 1–6 of audit)

A general-purpose audit pass produced 46 findings; the curator approved a single fix-up session covering items 1–6. Item 7+ deferred (soft flags, future work).

### Items addressed

**1. Unicorn timeline contradiction** — `arathi-cataclysm.md:103` previously asserted unicorns awakened at 4mya post-Cataclysm (6 mybp) on Eldravath. Canon (locked 2026-05-01) places unicorn emergence at **4 mybp** (= 6mya post-Cataclysm) on the **post-Eldravath** continental geography after the supercontinent had already broken apart at ~5 mybp. The bullet was edited to remove the unicorn line, and the trailing prose was extended to document the Eldravath fracture at 5mya post-Cataclysm and the unicorn awakening at 6mya post-Cataclysm with cross-links to [[unicorns#Origin]] and [[eadras-tectonic-history]].

**2. Sea'tua page created.** A new `sea-tua.md` page was authored from existing canon scattered across `peoples-of-eadras.md`, `merfolk.md`, `merrow.md`, `kuo-toa.md`, `elfen.md` etc. The Sea'tua were the third Elfen-engineered child race (alongside El'mer and Sidhe), created ~10M years after the Arathi Cataclysm to oversee oceanic balance, and the common progenitor of all seven modern sapient sea peoples (the Five Modern Oceanic Races plus the Kuo-toa and Sahuagin alien branches). The page covers Origin, Purpose, Inferred nature (reconstructed from descendant traits), Modern status (extinct as a distinct people, surviving only through descendants), Descendants table, and Open canon. Resolves the broken `[[sea-tua|Sea'tua]]` wikilink in `kuo-toa.md:71`. Added to `index.md` Engineered and Descendant Peoples section.

**3. Velrothi → Velrathi prose drift.** Canonical spelling is **Velrathi**. Prose drift fixed in: `velrathi.md:62` (apex society line), `gaia.md:73` (stranger arts line), `golems.md:31` (Velrothi labor cities), `orug.md:20` (engineered three crafted races), `veyr-keth.md:51` (princess display text), `index.md:95` (Great Betrayal entry), and `great-betrayal.md` lines 53, 65, and 144 (princess fiancée, alchemical arts, sequence summary). The flyting ballad on `great-betrayal.md:127` was preserved with the *Velrothi* spelling intact, since the lint flagged it as deliberate vernacular within a flyting context. The explanatory note on `velrathi.md:18` (which mentions the alternate spelling) was also preserved.

**4. Merfolk-as-single-race deprecation enforcement.** `elfen.md:49` (Sea'tua row of the engineered-children table) rewritten to use the five-race list plus the two alien branches with proper wikilinks; `elfen.md:51` (descendants line) rewritten to reference the Five Modern Oceanic Races collectively under the [[merfolk]] umbrella with explicit framing. `worldbuilding-needs.md:52` Merfolk row removed (the five sub-races each have their own pages and don't need the umbrella development item) and replaced with a single *Cross-oceanic politics* row asking what pan-oceanic structures exist across the five.

**5. `goliath.md` orphan resolved.** `peoples-of-eadras.md` Goliath table row converted from bold-only `**Goliath**` to wikilink `[[goliath\|Goliath]]`; `[[goliath]]` added to the page's Related pages list. Also added `[[sea-tua]]` to Related pages now that the page exists.

**6. Tag taxonomy migration sweep.** Per the documented edit-as-you-go migration policy (with full sweep no later than 2026-05-30), executed a comprehensive tag normalization pass. **53 pages updated.** Singular → plural: `race → races` (10 pages), `deity → deities` (16 pages, including the `archons.md` and `ixthal.md` pages the lint missed), `event → events` (5 pages), `myth → myths` (1 page), `place → places` or specific (11 pages — many converted to `settlement`/`building`/`geographic-feature` per the merge map's "use a more specific tag if it fits" guidance), `character → characters` (2 pages). Off-taxonomy drops: `pantheon`, `dragon`, `gray-matriarchy`, `gaia`, `nyxar`, `celestia`, `katharim`, `aetherin`, `black-hand`, `the-three`, `fate`, `death`, `spear`, `moon`, `exile`, `weapon`, `artifact`. Merge-map replacements: `artifact → item` (3 pages), `faction → organization` (2 pages, gray-matriarchy and kingdom-of-xanar). All affected frontmatter now uses Required Taxonomy + Modifier tags only.

### Verified clean

A post-sweep Grep confirmed:
- Zero singular `race`/`deity`/`event`/`myth`/`place`/`character`/`faction`/`artifact` tags remain in frontmatter.
- Zero off-taxonomy tags from the lint findings remain in frontmatter.
- Inbound wikilinks to `[[sea-tua]]` from `kuo-toa.md` now resolve.

### Items deferred

- **Lint item 7** ("Tarran" vs canonical "Taran" prose drift across ~45 files) — soft flag; the `taran.md` page itself documents both spellings as accepted variants. No sweep performed; future normalization may be done by edit-as-you-go.
- **Lint item 8** (Council of 99 / Compact of Horn and Flame as standalone pages) — judgment call; both currently work as section anchors and don't need promotion until they accumulate material that doesn't fit on parent pages.

### Memory implications

- No memory updates required; the lint sweep is normal maintenance.
- The Sea'tua page creation is worth noting since it materializes a previously-implicit canon node; the page is now the canonical home for Sea'tua-specific material going forward.

## 2026-05-10 — Race renames, Three-hands-off canon, four new pages, halflings retcon, and recovery from a sed-induced wiki-wide corruption

A long single-day session that mixed mechanical canon maintenance with a catastrophic mid-session corruption, full restore from backup, and a clean replay of the work. Documenting in roughly chronological order.

### Sources ingested

- `Notes for Changes for 5-10-26.txt` (canon clarifications: Three hands-off, gnomes pure Grugi, Demonic→Chaos suppression, page-creation routing)
- `Mitans.txt` (canonical Mitan page material)
- `Halfling Origin & the Change 5-10-26.txt` (halflings as Mitan subrace; Demon-War-trauma origin of The Change)
- `seraph-concept-2026-05-10.txt` (Seraphim canonical material)
- `devil-concept-2026-05-10.txt` (Devils canonical material)
- `devils-base-form-5-10-26.txt` (devils base-form canon: ordinary 5-foot red humanoid; uniforms produce the apparent variety)

### Race renames (canonical singular/plural distinctions enforced)

Five page renames with `aliases:` frontmatter so old wikilinks continue to resolve:

| Old | New | Title | Aliases added |
|---|---|---|---|
| `rathar.md` | `rathari.md` | Rathari | `[Rathar, rathar]` |
| `taran.md` | `tarans.md` | Tarans | `[Taran, taran, Tarran]` |
| `aetherin.md` | `aetherins.md` | Aetherins | `[Aetherin, aetherin]` |
| `grug.md` | `grugi.md` | Grugi | `[Grug, grug]` |
| `orug.md` | `orugi.md` | Orugi | `[Orug, orug]` |

Names kept invariant by user direction: `velrathi`, `katharim`, `arathi`, `elfen`.

### Wikilink sweep

A pure-`str.replace`-based Python sweep (`sweep_wikilinks.py`) updated wikilinks across the wiki: `[[<old><term>` → `[[<new><term>` for terminators `]`, `|`, `#`, and `\` (the table-cell escape form). 66 files changed; 360 replacements. A follow-up sweep (`sweep_padded_links.py`) caught 4 padded table-cell links in `peoples-of-eadras.md` that the main sweep missed (whitespace padding between slug and `|`). Total: **364 wikilink replacements**. `log.md` deliberately excluded — historical record stays intact; the new aliases handle resolution.

### Four canon retcons applied wiki-wide

**1. Gnomes are *pure Grugi*, not dual-progenitor.** The earlier "gnomes carry partial Mitan ancestry" framing has been retracted. Gnomes descend purely from Grugi stock; they are no longer "the only modern race with dual-progenitor lineage." Their craft tradition and resilience are now developments along the Grugi line itself, not Mitan-derived.

Edits:
- `gnomes.md` — frontmatter (drop `tarran` tag), summary, Origin section, Magical Inheritance paragraph
- `dwarves.md` — Relations bullet on Gnomes (no longer blood-kin; partnership is craft economy, not lineage)
- `peoples-of-eadras.md` — Mitans table row (drop "Gnomes (partially)")
- `the-three.md` — Melania-section Mitan ancestry list (drop "Gnomes (partially)")
- `aetherins.md` — Origin-section Mitans bullet
- `tarans.md` — Tarran-engineered-children table row
- `index.md` — gnomes one-line description

**2. The Three are universally hands-off on engineered races.** None of the Three directed, assisted, or oversaw the engineering of any child race. Once the Elfen, Velrathi, and Tarran existed, every subsequent engineered race was the progenitor race's own initiative. The Three made the eldest three; the eldest three made everything else.

Edits:
- `peoples-of-eadras.md` — added doctrinal paragraph after the canonical-creation paragraph
- `the-three.md` — added doctrinal-point blockquote after the engineering-mechanism paragraph; reworded Mark, Melania, and Rand sections to "the X did this themselves; <Three-name> did not direct, assist, or oversee the work"
- `elfen.md` — Engineered Child Races intro reworded (was "with Mark's direct shaping at key moments")
- `tarans.md` — Engineered Child Races intro reworded (was "with Melania's direct shaping at key moments")
- `aetherins.md` — Origin section reworded (was "with Melania providing direct shaping at key moments"); summary line dropped "(under Melania's direct shaping)"

**3. Aetherin "Demonic suppression" → "Chaos suppression".** Pre-Demon-War, the threat was raw Chaos and proto-demonic incursions; the term "demonic" properly belongs to the Demon-War era. Edit: `aetherins.md` Form-and-Role bullet rewritten.

**4. Mitans table-cell entries cleaned up across all referencing pages.** Where the Mitans appeared in summary tables previously listing "ancestors of Dwarves, Gnomes (partially), and Halflings," the lists now read "ancestors of Dwarves and Halflings."

### Four new pages created

- **`mitans.md`** — Canonical Mitan page. Tarran-engineered tunnel-fighters and miners; Rathari-derived architecture adapted toward stone-and-steel-and-precious-metal aesthetic; warrior culture inherited from Tarran; common ancestor of Dwarves (spiritual successors) and Halflings (surface-divergent subrace). The species took catastrophic Demon-War losses, came out genetically too narrow to recover, and has been in slow decline ever since; small remnant populations are believed to persist in the deepest, most isolated holds. The dwarven Shada'din maintain a *Mitan-hold protocol* — sealed deep complexes plausibly Mitan-inhabited are not opened.
- **`seraphim.md`** — Canonical Seraphim page. Native rank-and-file celestial spirits of Celestia; vast majority workforce of the Divine Bureaucracy; the setting's "angels" when dispatched on divine errands. Dedicated and dutiful; jaded by eons of paperwork. Plural is *Seraphim* (Hebrew); singular *Seraph* (older raw sources used *Seraph* invariantly; *Seraphim* is canonical going forward). Explicit "Not Archons" disambiguation: **Archons are Omniversal (cross-Mythos); Seraphim are Eadras-Mythos-local**.
- **`devils.md`** — Canonical Devils page. Native rank-and-file infernal spirits of Nyxar, primarily based in Dreadharrow; everyday staff of the Infernal Bureaucracy. **Base form is an ordinary medium-sized red-skinned humanoid (~5-5.5 ft, smooth crimson skin, small horn nubs, lean athletic build)**. The dramatic mortal-iconography forms (imps, barbed devils, horned devils, pit fiends, etc.) are produced by **magically-reshaping uniforms issued by the Bureaucracy**, mapped to rank and department. Out of uniform — in the locker rooms of Dreadharrow — devils look ordinary and gripe about their day. Field role: tempters and adversaries, dispatched from bureaucratic case-files in the traditional fiery uniform. Explicitly **not Demons**.
- **`infernal-bureaucracy.md`** — Canonical Infernal Bureaucracy page. Structural counterpart to the Divine Bureaucracy. **Terrifyingly efficient** where the Divine institution is dysfunctional. The horror of Hell in Eadras is precisely that the system works. No sinecures; competent performance management; soul-intake on schedule; torture quotas met. Distinct from the Divine Bureaucracy's *Bureau of Nyxar* (which is the Divine's external-management office, not Nyxar's internal admin). Did not start the Demon War; manages its consequences. Tone references (Death and Taxes, Disenchantment's Hell, TVA from Loki, Robot Hell from Futurama) housed in a `<details><summary>Author's tonal references (OOC)</summary>` block — a **new wiki-wide pattern for OOC tonal documentation** (see Memory implications).

### Halflings retcon

`halflings.md` rewritten in two key sections:

- **Origin reframed.** Halflings did not emerge as an independent race; they began as a *subrace within the Mitan*, formed by deliberate Mitan policy long before the Demon War. The Mitan wanted reliable surface agriculture; they sent a contingent to the surface as farmers; the surface-farmers liked it; they built hole-houses near their fields and established permanent surface communities; over generations they diverged from the deep-hold Mitan trunk into a recognizably distinct folk. By the time the Demon War broke, halflings had been a separate people for many thousands of years.
- **The Change reframed as Demon-War trauma adaptation.** The Change is not an ancient biological cycle. It manifested a few years after the Demon War as a racial psychological coping mechanism for two specific compound traumas: **open-sky terror** (refugees living unsheltered while demonic incursions descended from above) and **food-supply collapse** (loss of farms and storage). The Change is the racial body's lasting answer: never settle long enough to be unsettled; never store more than can be carried. **Modern halflings are not agoraphobic** — that acute body-memory has discharged; only the behavioural cycle persists.

The cyclical-Change practical material (caravans, hole-house wagons, twin births, semi-communal property exchange, cognomen system) all stays — those are present-day facts about how the cycle manifests, not contradictions of the new origin.

### Aliases convention

The five renamed race pages received `aliases: [...]` frontmatter so old `[[rathar]]` / `[[taran]]` etc. wikilinks continue to resolve. This is a consistent pattern with `divine-bureaucracy.md`'s existing aliases. Going forward, race renames should always include alias frontmatter for backwards compatibility.

### Index updates

`index.md` updated:
- Added `[[seraphim]]` line under Eadras Internal Planes (right after celestia)
- Added `[[devils]]` line under Eadras Internal Planes (right after nyxar)
- Added `[[infernal-bureaucracy]]` line under Divine Constructs & Doctrine (right after divine-bureaucracy)
- Added `[[mitans]]` line under Engineered and Descendant Peoples (between aetherins and katharim)
- Updated `[[gnomes]]` description (dropped "partial Mitan ancestry; the only dual-progenitor race")
- Updated `[[halflings]]` description (Mitan-subrace divergence; The Change as post-war adaptation)

### Catastrophic mid-session corruption and full recovery

A bash-and-sed wikilink sweep run in the background mid-session **destroyed every wiki page** with recursive `[[aetherins|<single-char>...]]` substitutions. Every file ballooned 50–500x — `log.md` reached 33MB, `aberrations.md` had a single line of 831,401 characters, `tarans.md` was 1.5MB on 154 lines. The corruption hit `wiki/` and `wiki/_sealed/` both; the `raw/` folder was untouched (per CLAUDE.md immutability policy, raw was never targeted).

Recovery steps (executed in this session under user authorization):

1. **Forensic preservation** — corrupted `wiki/` was moved to `wiki-corrupted-2026-05-10/` (still sitting on disk for any future inspection).
2. **Restore `wiki/` (218 files) from `wiki-export-2026-05-09.md`** (the May 9 evening export, clean UTF-8, no mojibake). A custom Python splitter (`split_export.py`) parsed the `=== / FILE: wiki/<name> / ===` blocks and wrote each page individually. Verified by file count and content sampling.
3. **Restore `wiki/_sealed/` (2 files) from `wiki-export.md`** (the May 7 export, the only backup that includes sealed). The May 7 export had double-encoded UTF-8 mojibake (`Kudur-eṭir` rendered as `Kudur-eá¹­ir`, etc.); the splitter's `--fix-mojibake` flag applied a `latin-1 → utf-8` round-trip that fully reversed the corruption. Note: `_sealed/` is now 3 days stale relative to today — anything sealed-related added between May 7 11:21 and today is permanently lost (none known to have been added; the sealed folder's only canon-evolution since May 7 is documented in MEMORY.md and that documentation survived).
4. **Replay of today's work** — executed cleanly with Edit/Write tools only, no `sed -i` regex sweeps. The renames + retcons + new pages + halflings retcon + index/log updates were re-applied from this conversation's working memory.

### Tooling produced (kept on disk for future reuse)

The following Python scripts now live at the repository root and can be reused for future similar work:

- `split_export.py` — split a concatenated wiki export into individual pages (with optional `--only-sealed` filter and `--fix-mojibake` flag)
- `sweep_wikilinks.py` — safe literal-`str.replace` wikilink sweep across the wiki (with `--dry-run` and `--include-log` flags); guaranteed not to recursively expand the way the failed bash/sed sweep did
- `sweep_padded_links.py` — companion sweep for table-cell wikilinks padded with whitespace before the `|` separator
- `find_padded_links.py` — diagnostic for locating padded wikilinks
- `verify_no_stale_slugs.py` — post-sweep verification

These tools should be the canonical mechanism for future wiki-wide renames. The CLAUDE.md project policy now (informally) is: **never use `sed -i` for cross-file edits on this wiki; use Edit-tool calls for one-offs and the Python scripts for sweeps.**

### Verification

- `verify_no_stale_slugs.py` reports **TOTAL stale wikilinks: 0**.
- `find_padded_links.py` reports zero remaining padded table-cell links.
- Grep for `Gnomes (partially)`, `partial Mitan`, `direct shaping at key moments`, `Melania providing direct shaping`, `Demonic suppression` outside `log.md` returns no contradicting hits.
- `mitans.md`, `seraphim.md`, `devils.md`, `infernal-bureaucracy.md` exist and have correct frontmatter.
- `halflings.md` retcon section is in place.

### Memory implications

## 2026-05-10 (later) — Canonical frontmatter schema established and applied wiki-wide

The frontmatter schema was promoted from informal/partial-adoption to fully canonical. The work touched CLAUDE.md, every wiki page, every Templater template, and the orden.md model page.

### CLAUDE.md additions

`CLAUDE.md` now carries a comprehensive schema section: required fields (`title`, `tags`, `canon_status`, `perspective`, `historical_horizon`, `knowledge_access`), optional fields (`aliases`, `cssclasses`, `axes_profile`), locked value enums for the four meta-fields, body conventions (show-properties toggle, axes-of-creation slider block, OOC tonal-references block, related-pages block), the renames-and-aliases rule, the schema carve-outs (log/index/sealed/rpg/reference), and the plugin requirements (Meta Bind, Dataview, Templater).

### Locked enums

- **canon_status**: `established` / `proposed` / `open-canon` / `pending` / `deprecated` / `sealed`
- **perspective**: `tome-neutral` / `tome-secret` / `tome-sealed` / `in-character` / `ooc` / `reference`
- **historical_horizon**: `primordial` / `nerathi-era` / `dragon-era` / `dragon-unicorn-era` / `progenitor-era` / `high-firethorn` / `demon-war` / `dimming` / `modern-era` / `all`
- **knowledge_access**: `common` / `general` / `scholarly` / `esoteric` / `meta` / `sealed`

### Narathi → Nerathi sweep

The Arathi endonym was renamed from *Narathi* to *Nerathi* (user direction; better fit for the Near-Eastern naming convention). 10 replacements across 5 files: `naming-conventions.md`, `arathi.md`, `deep-vaults.md`, `lost-primer.md`, `trolls.md`. `log.md` historical entries left untouched per existing convention.

### Templates rewritten

All 7 existing templates at `templates/*.txt` rewrote to schema-conformance (Race, Faction, Character, Location, Object, Magic, Lore Entry). One new template added: `templates/Page.txt` for pages that don't fit any specific category. Each template emits the canonical frontmatter, the show-properties toggle, the body skeleton, and (for agent-category templates: Race, Faction, Character) the axes-of-creation slider block with `axes-unset` cssclass. The legacy `type:` field and the `tags: <type>, created: <date>` string format are gone.

### orden.md cleanup

orden's `cssclasses: [hide-props, axes-unset]` was reduced to `[hide-props]` (the page already has filled axes_profile values; `axes-unset` was the in-between marker that should have been removed when values were saved). Frontmatter also normalized from YAML list form to compact array form to match the schema.

### Today's 10 pages: schema applied

The 10 pages I created or substantially edited earlier in this session got the full schema:
- 5 race renames: `rathari.md`, `tarans.md`, `aetherins.md`, `grugi.md`, `orugi.md`
- 4 new pages: `mitans.md`, `seraphim.md`, `devils.md`, `infernal-bureaucracy.md`
- 1 retconned: `halflings.md`

Each got the four meta-fields, `cssclasses: [hide-props, axes-unset]` (all are agent pages), `axes_profile:` dict with zero defaults (user fills via Meta Bind sliders), the show-properties toggle, and an axes-of-creation slider block before the Related pages block. Per-page `historical_horizon` set to `[all]` (these pages span multiple eras); `canon_status: [established]`; `perspective: [tome-neutral]`; `knowledge_access` varied by accessibility (`common` for widely-known peoples, `scholarly` for extinct or deep-lore subjects, `general` for the Mitans).

### Wiki-wide backfill

A Python `backfill_schema.py` script swept all 224 wiki pages, adding any missing meta-fields, cssclasses, and show-properties toggle. The carve-outs (`log.md`, `index.md`) were skipped per the schema rule. Sealed and rpg subfolders received their category-specific defaults (sealed → `[tome-sealed]/[sealed]`; rpg → `[ooc]/[meta]`). Reference pages (`tags.md`, `naming-conventions.md`, `axes-of-creation.md`, `eadras-timeline.md`, `open-questions.md`, `worldbuilding-needs.md`, `inspirations.md`) received `[reference]/[meta]`.

A bug in the parser (handled BOM after newline rather than before) was caught when 38 pages reported as "no-frontmatter" — they all had BOM + leading-blank-line + frontmatter and the parser missed them. Fixed and verified.

### List-form → compact-form conversion

41 pages had been written with YAML list form on their meta-fields (`field:\n  - value` style) before the schema locked compact form as canonical. A `compact_listform.py` script converted all of them in a single pass.

### Enum compliance fixes

8 pages had non-enum values in their categorical fields, mostly remnants of in-progress canon work that predated the locked enums:

- 6 pages with `canon_status: [rework-pending]` (from the 2026-05-09 magic-system rework) → mapped to `[pending]`
- 1 page (`magic-in-eadras.md`) with `[partial-rework-pending]` → mapped to `[pending]`
- 1 page (`lost-primer.md`) with `perspective: [tome-recovered]` → mapped to `[tome-secret]`

The rpg subfolder pages also had non-enum values (`canon_status: [splat-material]`, various `perspective` values, `historical_horizon: [crystalline-age]`); these were normalized to the rpg defaults (`[pending] / [ooc]` per the schema's rpg carve-out) and `crystalline-age` was mapped to `nerathi-era` (the era label that covers the pre-Cataclysm Nerathi civilization).

The `rework-pending` mapping is a soft loss — the value carried distinct semantics ("was established, now under rework") that `pending` doesn't fully capture. Whether to add `rework-pending` (and `tome-recovered`) back into the locked enums is open canon. Until then, the affected pages flag their rework status in body prose and via the relevant memory pointer (`project-magic-system-rework.md`).

### Verification

- `python backfill_schema.py wiki --dry-run` reports `change: 0, already-conforms: 222, skip-carveout: 2, no-frontmatter: 0`.
- `python compact_listform.py wiki --dry-run` reports `Compacted 0 pages`.
- The enum-violation scan reports `Violations: 0`.
- All 220 content pages have the canonical frontmatter, the show-properties toggle, and matching cssclasses.
- 11 pages have `axes_profile` filled (the 10 schema-applied pages today plus orden); the remaining ~110 agent-tagged pages still need axes-block addition and `axes-unset` cssclass — that's a follow-up sweep for a future session, since the question of which pages count as "agent pages" requires per-page judgment.

### Tooling produced (kept on disk)

- `backfill_schema.py` — wiki-wide schema backfill (idempotent; safe to re-run)
- `compact_listform.py` — convert YAML list form to compact array form
- (existing) `split_export.py`, `sweep_wikilinks.py`, `sweep_padded_links.py`, `verify_no_stale_slugs.py`, `find_padded_links.py`

### Memory implications

- New memory needed: **OOC tonal-references pattern** is already documented in `project-ooc-tonal-references-pattern.md`; the schema work today doesn't change it.
- The `feedback-no-sed-cross-file-edits.md` lesson holds firm — every cross-file sweep today used `str.replace` Python scripts with dry-run-first discipline.
- The `project-export-backup-recovery.md` pattern still applies; this session has added enough work that a fresh export is recommended before next session.

### Open canon (specific to this work)

- **Whether to add `rework-pending` and `tome-recovered`** back to the locked enums. Today's mapping to `pending` / `tome-secret` is canonical compliance but loses semantic distinction. User call.
- **Axes-of-Creation profile coverage.** Which pages count as agent-pages and should carry the slider block is a per-page judgment that hasn't been done wiki-wide yet. Today only 11 pages have axes; ~100+ candidates remain.
- **Templater integration.** The templates are now schema-conformant but use core-Templates `{{title}}` syntax rather than Templater `<% tp.file.title %>` syntax. If the user wants Templater-native templates, that's a future conversion.

## 2026-05-10 (closing addendum) — Enum expansion, fresh export, Templater conversion

User direction at session close: restore the rework-state values, generate a fresh export, and convert templates to Templater syntax (defer the axes sweep).

### Enum expansion (CLAUDE.md)

The locked enums in CLAUDE.md were expanded to restore the values the earlier mapping had collapsed:

- **`canon_status`** gained `rework-pending` (was-established, currently-being-revised) and `partial-rework-pending` (some sections reworked, others not).
- **`perspective`** gained `tome-recovered` (page content reconstructed from indirect evidence; the Tome did not directly observe).

The 8 pages mapped earlier in this session were restored to their original semantic values: `dashar.md`, `heart-of-the-goddess.md`, `order-sharanel.md`, `order-sworn-sorcerers.md`, `sorcerer-crusade.md`, `weavespinners.md` back to `[rework-pending]`; `magic-in-eadras.md` back to `[partial-rework-pending]`; `lost-primer.md` back to `[tome-recovered]`. Final enum-violation scan: zero violations across 224 files.

### Fresh export

`wiki-export-2026-05-10.md` generated at the repository root (224 pages, ~2.5 MB). Includes `wiki/`, `wiki/_sealed/`, and `wiki/rpg/` per the new CLAUDE.md export rule. Round-trip-verified by `split_export.py --dry-run` — parses cleanly back to 224 individual pages.

While generating the export, found that `wiki/_sealed/README.md` and `wiki/_sealed/fourth-hiding-place.md` still carried **double-encoded UTF-8 mojibake** that the May 10 recovery's `--fix-mojibake` flag (which used Latin-1 round-trip) had only partially reversed. The actual mojibake was Windows-1252-flavored, with characters like `€` (U+20AC) at byte `\x80` that Latin-1 doesn't define. Applied a Windows-1252 round-trip fix to both files; em-dashes and curly quotes now render correctly.

### CLAUDE.md export rule

A new "Backups and exports" section was added to CLAUDE.md mandating that fresh exports be generated:
- **After any large change session** that touched many pages or made schema-altering changes.
- **Before closing down a session** if any wiki content has been modified that day.

The rule explicitly states that the export must include `_sealed/` and `rpg/` for backup completeness; if the export is going to be shared publicly, strip `_sealed/` first rather than excluding it from the canonical backup. (The 2026-05-09 export's exclusion of `_sealed/` is exactly the failure mode the rule prevents.)

### Templater conversion

All 8 templates at `templates/*.txt` were converted from core-Templates syntax (`{{title}}`, `{{date:YYYY-MM-DD}}`) to Templater syntax (`<% tp.file.title %>`, `<% tp.date.now("YYYY-MM-DD") %>`). The four canonical-enum frontmatter fields now use **Templater suggesters** which prompt the user to choose from the locked enum values at template-instantiation time, guaranteeing schema compliance:

- `canon_status` — suggester with all 8 values
- `historical_horizon` — suggester with all 10 values
- `knowledge_access` — suggester with all 6 values
- `perspective` — hardcoded default (`[tome-neutral]`); user edits manually for non-default categories (sealed, rpg, in-character, reference, ooc, tome-recovered)

The agent-category templates (Race, Faction, Character) keep `cssclasses: [hide-props, axes-unset]` and the axes-of-creation slider block; the non-agent templates (Page, Location, Object, Magic, Lore Entry) keep `cssclasses: [hide-props]` only.

### Tooling produced

- `generate_export.py` — write a `wiki-export-YYYY-MM-DD.md` from current wiki content; refuses to overwrite without `--force`. Saved at repository root.

### Verification

- `python backfill_schema.py wiki --dry-run` → 222 conform / 2 carve-outs / 0 missed
- `python compact_listform.py wiki --dry-run` → 0 pages remain in list form
- Enum violations across 224 files → 0

## 2026-05-10 (evening) — `/five-whys` skill + Titans page + progenitor role doctrines

Smaller focused session that established the first Claude Code skill and used it to surface and fill a load-bearing canon gap.

### Infrastructure (new tier + first skill)

- **`.claude/skills/` directory** created. First skill: **`.claude/skills/five-whys/SKILL.md`** — probes one load-bearing element of a wiki page by asking *"why does this exist in-world?"* five times, tags each answer's provenance (established / implied / GAP), bottoms out at a foundational canon or surfaces a deep gap. Outputs analysis to `derived/five-whys/`; never modifies the wiki.
- **`derived/` tier** created — writable analysis-artifact area between `raw/` and `wiki/`. First inhabitant: `derived/five-whys/orcs-2026-05-10.md`.

### Tier 1: canon-shifting

- **Progenitor role doctrines established.** Each progenitor race has a defining societal role that determined what they engineered:
  - **[[tarans|Tarran]] = Protectors** → engineered the martial cluster ([[aetherins|Aetherin]] shock troops, [[titans|Titans]] heavy war engines, [[mitans|Mitans]] subterranean specialists).
  - **[[velrathi|Velrathi]] = Deep Learning** → engineered a self-sustaining scholarly civilization ([[rathari|Rathar]] scholars, [[grugi|Grug]] makers, [[orugi|Orug]] internal guardians).
  - **[[elfen|Elfen]] = Nature Guardians** → engineered preservation specialists ([[el-mer|El'mer]]).
  - **Orug non-aggression** is now understood as inter-progenitor lane-discipline: the Velrathi engineered their internal guardians NOT to encroach on Tarran's war-against-chaos jurisdiction. Pending Philosophy-of-Engineering paragraphs on [[velrathi]], [[tarans]], [[orugi]] to formalize this in prose.
- **Engineering register clarified.** "Engineering" of races in Eadras = spellcraft + Mendelian selective breeding across many generations. **NOT** in-vitro / viral / lab biotech. All future page work touching engineered races must use fantasy register (*wrought, shaped, bred, lineage-shaping, spellcraft of lineage*) and exclude biotech vocabulary (*gene, DNA, splice, vat, in-vitro*).

### Tier 2: pages

- **[[titans]] created** (`canon_status: proposed` — pending user review). 25–30m adult / 10m child; bred for war against chaos; eat near-constantly due to scale; civilized vs. uncivilized distinction; fully sapient brains but developmental disabilities common from childhood under-feeding; most died in Demon War with surviving population in genetic bottleneck decline; feral remnant roams Eadras (mobile, food-driven, not anchored to fixed ranges); Gray Matriarchy keeps a small stable civilized breeding population used as instruments of terror against commoners.
- **[[goliath]] corrected.** Pre-existing canon stated Titans were 3m and Goliath "returned to Titan dimensions" via devolution. Both wrong. Titans are 25–30m; devolution is ~order-of-magnitude size reduction across two stages; Goliath are recognizable kin in body-plan but only fragments of the progenitor stock's scale and capability. Added [[titans]] wikilink.

### Tier 3: derived analysis (1 new artifact)

- **`derived/five-whys/orcs-2026-05-10.md`** — five-whys probe on [[orcs]]. Probed *"Orc honor is rooted in self-mastery, not territorial conquest."* Bottomed out five levels deep at cosmological-foundational (the tiered intentional-creation cascade from The Three downward). Surfaced the role-doctrine gap that became the Tier 1 resolution above.

### Tier 4: raw session captures

- **`raw/titans-canon-2026-05-10.txt`** — role doctrines, Titan size/diet/civilized-uncivilized canon, engineering register rule.
- **`raw/titans-canon-additions-2026-05-10.txt`** — feral Titan range, genetic bottleneck, Gray Matriarchy terror-use, sapience baseline + developmental disability pattern.

### Pending follow-ups for next session

1. Philosophy-of-Engineering paragraphs in [[velrathi]], [[tarans]], [[orugi]] formalizing the role doctrines in prose.
2. File to [[open-questions]]: civilized-Titan language (Tarran or own tongue?); Titan participation in the unified charge of the [[three-who-stood|Three Who Stood]]; promotion of the Protection / Deep Learning / Nature Guardianship triad to a dedicated page; mapping of role-doctrines to The Three creator-gods.
3. Promote [[titans]] from `canon_status: proposed` to `established` after user review.
4. Build the next workflow skill — `/multi-pov` (parallel-subagent pattern; one event told from multiple race perspectives, fitting the Tome conceit).

## 2026-05-11 — Sarathim Empire revision merge + OOC block schema refinement

Morning session integrating an AI-generated Sarathim page rewrite Josh shared from another LLM. Major canon additions on imperial government and bureaucracy; a new OOC author-side worldbuilding annotations pattern adopted into the schema.

### Tier 1: canon-shifting (Sarathim Empire)

- **The Sarathim were a true Divine Imperial state** for approximately 5,000 years (post–[[demon-war|Demon War]] through the [[sorcerer-crusade|Sorcerer Crusade]]). Earlier canon framed the throne as "largely ceremonial" with merchant-princes holding real power; this is **reversed**. The Divine Emperor or Empress was the living bearer of a sacred imperial legacy and held real political authority — specifically over the professional Imperial military.
- **Strict hereditary succession** parent-to-direct-child only; lateral succession (siblings, cousins, collateral dynasties) forbidden. Dynastic termination is interpreted as divine judgment; houses then compete for the throne in such interregna; the winner formally severs all ties with their original house and becomes sacred, above the noble order.
- **Three-way political balance**: noble houses (wealth) / professional eunuch bureaucracy (administration) / Divine Throne (military). The empire's long endurance is attributed to this stability — none of the three could fully dominate the others.
- **Private armies capped at 1/10 of Imperial strength**; transgressions could dissolve a house entirely. **Nobles forbidden from Imperial military command at any rank** — officer, advisor, or logistician.
- **Eunuch bureaucracy** of commoner children purchased after imperial testing for exceptional intelligence/memory/discipline/loyalty; brutally educated across literacy, accounting, law, administration, diplomacy, logistics, political theory, and arcane regulation. The bureaucracy's institutional loyalty drifted from any individual Emperor or Empress toward "the continuity of the empire" itself.
- **The Divine Throne was lost in Sarathis's fall**; no formal succession has been recorded since. Whether any legitimate claimant lineage survives is open canon. (Resolves and replaces the earlier "current Sarathim ceremonial Emperor?" open question.)
- **Ottoman imperial administration added** as the fourth named cultural-fusion influence (now: Renaissance Italy + Ottoman + Ancient Egypt + Islamic Golden Age). The Ottoman influence accounts for the eunuch bureaucracy and the strict noble/military separation in the in-character framing.
- **[[orden|Orden]] and other modern trade leagues** trace precursor systems to Sarathim commercial law, accounting practices, and merchant-house structures.
- New canon sayings (in-character): *"A Sarathim smiles with the mouth and measures your coffin with the eyes."* / *"Empires drown. Houses endure."*

All preserved old content (Velrathi-heir manifesto, audience reactions, Magic and Scholarship section, Imperial Decree on charity, "great house" ideal, festivals, naming, original open-canon questions, complete wikilink set) was restored in the merged version per user direction; only directly contradicted material was removed.

### Tier 2: schema refinement

- **`CLAUDE.md`** — "OOC tonal references block" section replaced with **"OOC author-side worldbuilding annotations."** The new pattern uses three optional sub-headings — *Cultural shorthand* (bulleted), *Intended civilizational feel* (prose), *Visual motifs* (bulleted) — under the canonical `<details class="ooc-block">` collapsible. The Sarathim page is the first to adopt the fuller pattern. The simpler tonal-touchstones-only form remains valid for pages with narrower OOC content.

### Tier 3: schema corrections applied during the merge

The AI-drafted revision had three schema violations that the merge corrected:

- `historical_horizon: [post-demon-war, modern-era]` — multi-value array plus an invented enum entry. Corrected to **`historical_horizon: [all]`**, with the era refinement (see Tier 4) flagged in the page's Open Canon section.
- `tags: [civilization, empire, human, modern-era, eadras]` — three non-taxonomy tags plus an enum-value used as a tag. Corrected to **`tags: [country, culture, history, eadras]`** using canonical entries from [[tags]].
- OOC `<details>` block missing the `ooc-block` CSS class hook — class added.

### Tier 4: pending schema work (filed on the Sarathim page's Open Canon)

- The `historical_horizon` enum may need refinement to add a **`pre-modern`** era (10,000–5,000 ya, covering the Sarathim Empire and other long-lived post-Demon-War institutions) and to narrow `dimming` to 5,000–4,000 ya, with `modern` (4,000–now) potentially renamed from `modern-era`. This would require a wiki-wide migration sweep touching every page that uses `historical_horizon`. Deferred pending user decision.

### Tier 5: raw session capture

- **`raw/sarathim-revision-2026-05-11.txt`** — session capture documenting the canon decisions, the preserved content, the pending schema work, and the new OOC pattern. Cited by the merged Sarathim page.

## 2026-05-11 (later) — Spirits umbrella canon: universal true form, uniforms, back rooms

Substantial cosmological canon establishing a single mechanism that governs spirit appearance and behaviour across all four non-mortal realms of the Eadras Mythos. The "devils wear uniforms" canon already established on [[devils]] is generalised to [[seraphim]], fey, and shadowdark spirits; a new **back rooms** concept is added across all four realms.

### Tier 1: canon-shifting

- **Universal spirit true form.** All spirits — [[seraphim|Seraphim]], [[devils|Devils]], fey, dark spirits — share the same basic true form: a smooth, nearly featureless, androgynous humanoid figure of roughly mortal proportions, with minimal facial features and no hair, and a *glow* emanating from the body.
- **Glow colour = realm of origin.** Celestials glow bright golden-white; infernals glow deep crimson-red to orange; fey glow vibrant emerald green; shadowdark spirits glow blacklight ultraviolet-violet.
- **Glow brightness = raw spiritual power**, independent of role. A bright-glowing spirit in a low role is a visible institutional event.
- **Universal uniform mechanic.** The "types" of spirits mortals catalogue (imps, wraiths, dryads, seraphs, pit-fiends, sprites, banshees, ad infinitum) are *not* species — they are uniforms worn over the universal true form, calibrated to mortal expectations and bureaucratic role, and they carry the powers associated with the role. Each realm has its own uniform code maintained by its institutional order.
- **Back rooms.** All spirit realms — Upper, Middle, Lower — contain *back rooms*: private spaces where spirits can remove their uniforms and rest in true form. The cultural framing is universal: even spirits cannot remain on duty for eternity. The canonical example is the **locker rooms of [[dreadharrow|Dreadharrow]]** (Infernal Bureaucracy's back rooms); equivalents are the **celestial rest-halls** of Celestia, fey **glade-clearings** of the Feywild, and the **quiet rooms** of the Shadowdark.

### Tier 2: pages

- **[[spirits]] created** (`canon_status: established`) as the umbrella page documenting the universal canon: true form, glow colour table by realm, glow brightness mechanic, uniforms, back rooms, and distinctions from demons / gods / engineered races / archons.
- **[[devils]] updated** — Summary, Sources, Last updated, Base form section, table-of-mirror row, and "When a devil clocks out…" reverting-to-base-form line all updated to use the universal canon. The contradicted *"5-foot red-skinned humanoid with small horn nubs"* framing has been retired; the new base form is "featureless androgynous humanoid with crimson glow." Horns are now explicitly part of the uniform, not the true form. The locker rooms of Dreadharrow are now framed as "the canonical example of the *back rooms* every spirit realm maintains." [[spirits]] added to Related pages.
- **[[seraphim]] updated** — Sources, Last updated, and a new **True form** section added (between *What they are* and *Daily role*). The Seraph true form is the universal featureless androgynous humanoid with bright golden-white glow; the iconographic radiance, wings, halo, robes, and burning sword are now explicitly the field-dispatch uniform, not the underlying being. The **celestial rest-halls** are introduced as Celestia's back rooms (the equivalent of Dreadharrow's locker rooms), including the canonical Seraphim grousing-culture detail. [[spirits]] added to Related pages.
- **[[index]] updated** — `[[spirits]]` added to the *Eadras Internal Planes* section, immediately after [[eadras-cosmology]] and before the per-plane entries.

### Tier 3: raw session capture

- **`raw/spirits-canon-2026-05-11.txt`** — session capture documenting the universal canon, the resolved contradictions on the [[devils]] page, preserved canon that didn't change, and the new additions. Cited by [[spirits]], [[devils]], and [[seraphim]].

The new universal canon affects several pages that weren't updated this session. Each gains relevant detail from the universal canon but doesn't contradict its current content:

- **[[feywild]]** — should mention the universal true form + emerald glow for fey spirits, and the realm's back rooms (glade-clearings).

## 2026-05-11 (third) — Spirits canon refinement: shells terminology and bespoke-vs-standardised distinction

Refinement appended to the morning's spirits umbrella canon. The "uniform" mechanism is reframed as the deeper concept of **shells**, with a new distinction between standardised shells (bureaucratic realms) and bespoke shells (Feywild and Shadowdark).

### Canon refinement

- **`Shell` is the canonical term** for what the spirits umbrella canon had been calling a *uniform*. A shell is a physical and magical construct that **fundamentally changes what the spirit is** while worn — not merely changing appearance, but bundling appearance, powers, and **responsibilities** into a single role-and-identity package. The spirit placed into a new shell does not appear to be a different being; they functionally *are* one.
- The role assignment is literal: *"You are now a nymph."* / *"You are now a brownie."* / *"You are now the genius loci of this forest."*
- *Uniform* remains valid as shorthand, especially in the bureaucratic realms where standardised shells double as institutional rank markers.
- **Standardised shells** (bureaucratic realms — Celestia / Nyxar): issued from a code, organised by department and rank, mass-produced; the uniform-shorthand fits cleanly.
- **Bespoke shells** (Feywild / Shadowdark): bound to *specific* landscapes, hearths, streams, groves, or relationships. A nymph is the nymph of *this* stream; a brownie is the brownie of *this* household; a *genius loci* is by definition the spirit of one named place. The shell binds role, place, and relationship as a single unit; reassignment changes all three together.
- No previous canon is contradicted by this refinement; it deepens the mechanism with terminology and a finer distinction.

### Page updates

- **[[spirits]]** — the `## Uniforms` section is replaced with `## Shells`, with the new sub-section `### Standardised shells vs. bespoke shells`. The new section establishes *shell* as canonical, *uniform* as bureaucratic-context shorthand, includes the literal role-assignment phrasing, the appearance+powers+responsibilities bundle, and the bespoke/standardised distinction.
- **[[devils]]** — cross-reference parenthetical added at the start of the `## Uniforms` section pointing to [[spirits#Shells]]. Existing uniform-language preserved (bureaucratic context where the shorthand is idiomatic).
- **[[seraphim]]** — equivalent cross-reference parenthetical added in the *True form* section.
- **[[index]]** — Spirits umbrella entry updated from *"uniforms as the source"* to *"shells (uniforms in bureaucratic shorthand) as the source."*

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/spirits-shell-refinement-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the terminology, the role-assignment phrasing, the bundle-of-three, the standardised-vs-bespoke distinction, and the no-contradictions note.

## 2026-05-11 (fourth) — Spirits canon clarification: shells are still put-on/take-off; promotion is shell-upgrade

Clarification pass on today's spirits canon. The earlier shell-refinement said shells "fundamentally change what the spirit is while they are wearing them" — the WHILE qualifier was doing important work and the clarification makes that explicit.

### Refinement

- **Shells are still put-on / take-off**, like any uniform. The deeper-than-clothing aspect is what they carry *while worn* (appearance + powers + responsibilities). Outside the shell, in the back rooms, the spirit returns to the universal true form, free of the previous role's powers and duties.
- **Promotion is a shell upgrade, not a re-creation of the spirit.** A spirit promoted from Pixie to Brownie remains the same spirit; the pixie-shell goes back to the institutional channel, the brownie-shell is issued, and the spirit's career-history and reputation travel with them into the new role. The canonical fey-hierarchy promotion phrasing is now: *"Congratulations on your promotion, spirit. You have been promoted from Pixie to Brownie!"*
- The spirit is the unit of continuous identity; the shell is the variable. Career history, reputation, and institutional standing are spirit-attached, not shell-attached.

### Page updates

- **[[spirits]]** — `## Shells` section: a new paragraph between the role-assignment quotes and the bundle-list explicitly establishes put-on/take-off + the Pixie-to-Brownie promotion notice + spirit-continuity-across-shells. The line *"While the shell is on, the nymph **is** a nymph in every functional sense"* tightened to *"functions as a nymph in every operational sense — but it remains a shell that can be taken off at the end of the shift."* In the bespoke section, *"no longer the same kind of being in any functional sense"* tightened to *"functions as a different kind of being from the moment the new shell is donned, even though the underlying spirit is the same individual."*

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/spirits-shell-clarification-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the put-on/take-off framing, the promotion-as-shell-upgrade canon, the canonical Pixie-to-Brownie notice, and the spirit-attached vs shell-attached identity distinction.

## 2026-05-11 (fifth) — Spirits canon: cross-realm bureaucratic scope

The Feywild and Shadowdark do **not** maintain their own administrative orders. Shell-issuance, assignment, and promotion across all four spirit realms are handled by only two bureaucracies, each overseeing two realms apiece along the cosmological bright/dark axis.

### Canon

- **[[divine-bureaucracy|Divine Bureaucracy]] administers the bright realms**: [[celestia|Celestia]] (primary) and the [[feywild|Feywild]] (secondary). A fey-hierarchy promotion notice is a Divine document; the same institution that issues seraphic dispatch-uniforms also issues nymph-shells and *genii loci* bindings.
- **[[infernal-bureaucracy|Infernal Bureaucracy]] administers the dark realms**: [[nyxar|Nyxar]] (primary) and the [[shadowdark|Shadowdark]] (secondary). The same institution that issues pit-fiend uniforms also issues wraith-shells and shadow-stalker bindings.
- The standardised-vs-bespoke shell-mode distinction maps onto the primary-vs-secondary realm distinction inside each bureaucracy:
  - Primary realms (Celestia, Nyxar) → standardised shells (mass-produced, rank-coded)
  - Secondary realms (Feywild, Shadowdark) → bespoke shells (bound to specific places and relationships)
- Each bureaucracy must therefore maintain **two qualitatively different shell catalogues** — a standardised one for its primary realm, a bespoke one for its secondary.
- Shells are **bureaucracy-specific**, not strictly realm-specific. A Divine celestial-shell and a Divine fey-shell are both Divine Bureaucracy products drawn from a single administrative tradition; a Divine shell cannot fit an Infernal spirit.
- Back rooms across all four realms are infrastructure of the administering bureaucracy: celestial rest-halls and Feywild glade-clearings are Divine Bureaucracy infrastructure; Dreadharrow locker rooms and Shadowdark quiet rooms are Infernal Bureaucracy infrastructure.

### Resolved open canon

An earlier open-canon item — *"The structure of fey and shadowdark institutions. The Divine and Infernal Bureaucracies are documented; the equivalent institutional order in the Feywild and Shadowdark (whether also bureaucracies, or courtly hierarchies, or something else) is open canon"* — is now **answered**: there is no separate institutional order. The two main bureaucracies are the answer.

### New open canon (narrower)

- The internal organisation of each bureaucracy's secondary-realm division (Divine Bureaucracy's Feywild administration; Infernal Bureaucracy's Shadowdark administration) — whether a formal Department, sub-bureau, parallel column, or something else.
- Whether spirits rotate between primary and secondary realms within the same bureaucracy (a Seraph reassigned to a fey-shell? a Devil to a wraith-shell?) or whether shell modes are non-interchangeable even within a single bureaucracy's scope.

### Page updates

- **[[spirits]]** — Standardised-vs-bespoke section restructured into two sub-sections: a new **Administration: two bureaucracies, four realms** sub-section establishing the cross-realm scope, followed by the **Standardised shells vs. bespoke shells** sub-section now framed as the primary-vs-secondary realm distinction inside each bureaucracy. Back rooms section: "fey hierarchies" and "shadow hierarchies" updated to "Divine Bureaucracy's Feywild operations" and "Infernal Bureaucracy's Shadowdark operations" respectively. The open-canon item about fey/shadowdark institutions replaced with two narrower items.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/spirits-bureaucracy-scope-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the cross-realm scope canon, the primary/secondary realm mapping, the implications for shell catalogues and back rooms, and the new (narrower) open-canon items.

### Pending follow-up amendments (updated from earlier today)

The morning's pending-follow-up list for the spirits canon now includes:

- **[[divine-bureaucracy]]** — describe its cross-realm administrative scope: Celestia (primary) + Feywild (secondary). Two shell catalogues. Both kinds of back room.
- **[[infernal-bureaucracy]]** — describe its cross-realm administrative scope: Nyxar (primary) + Shadowdark (secondary). Two shell catalogues. Both kinds of back room.
- **[[feywild]]** — administered by the Divine Bureaucracy; no independent fey-court bureaucracy exists.
- **[[shadowdark]]** — administered by the Infernal Bureaucracy; no independent shadow-hierarchy bureaucracy exists.

## 2026-05-11 (sixth) — Spirits canon clarification: interior governance vs shell-administration

Clarification on the scope of the cross-realm Bureaucratic administration established in the (fifth) entry above. The Divine and Infernal Bureaucracies handle **shell-administration** (issuance, assignment, promotion) across their two realms apiece — but they do **not** run day-to-day governance in the Feywild or the Shadowdark. Each secondary realm maintains its own **interior governance**, local and regional rather than plane-wide.

### Canon

- The [[feywild|Feywild]] and [[shadowdark|Shadowdark]] each maintain their own interior governance: fey courts, shadow councils, regional fiefs, and place-by-place political arrangements. This is **distinct from** and **not handled by** the Divine or Infernal Bureaucracy.
- Interior governance is **local or regional, not plane-wide.** The secondary realms are not unified under any single internal authority the way [[celestia|Celestia]] and [[nyxar|Nyxar]] are under their respective Bureaucracies. *There is no fey-wide council; there is no shadow-wide throne.*
- The Bureaucratic scope is precisely: shell-issuance, shell-assignment, promotion processing, shell-catalogue maintenance, and back-room infrastructure. Everything else in the secondary realms is the secondary realm's own affair.
- A way to read the split: the Bureaucracies are the **employment and credentialing** layer; the local fey courts and shadow councils are the **political and social** layer. They cooperate at the shell-handoff (a promotion requires both a local sponsor and a new shell), but they are different institutions doing different work.

### Page updates

- **[[spirits]]** — *Administration: two bureaucracies, four realms* sub-section reworded throughout to clarify Bureaucratic scope = shell-administration only, with a new paragraph establishing the secondary realms' interior governance (local/regional, not plane-wide) and the employment-vs-political layer split. *Back rooms* section: "Divine/Infernal Bureaucracy's Feywild/Shadowdark operations" tightened to "Feywild/Shadowdark shell-administration." Open canon: the item about each bureaucracy's secondary-realm "administration" tightened to "shell-administration"; a new open-canon item added about the structure of interior governance.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/spirits-governance-clarification-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the bureaucratic-scope clarification, the interior-governance canon, the employment-vs-political-layer split, and the updated pending follow-ups.

### Pending follow-ups (updated)

- **[[divine-bureaucracy]]** / **[[infernal-bureaucracy]]** — scope should be described as shell-administration across two realms (not all-governance).
- **[[feywild]]** — should describe its interior governance (local/regional fey courts) AND its dual structure with the Divine Bureaucracy's shell-administration layer.
- **[[shadowdark]]** — same for the Shadowdark with the Infernal Bureaucracy.

## 2026-05-11 (seventh) — Spirits canon: gods as primary-realm non-Bureaucratic political layer

Parallel addition to the (sixth) entry's interior-governance canon. The primary realms ([[celestia|Celestia]], [[nyxar|Nyxar]]) also have a non-Bureaucratic political layer alongside their Bureaucracy: the **gods**, who are *outside* the Bureaucracy and have their own goals, desires, and power to create intrigue for it.

### Canon

- In Celestia and Nyxar, the [[gods-of-eadras|gods]] (Elder Gods, Ascended Mortal Gods, senior infernal powers) sit *outside the Bureaucracy* — above it and beside it. They are not part of the Bureaucratic apparatus; they are nominally served by it.
- The gods have personal goals, desires, alliances, grudges, and political projects, and the power to act on them. They can and routinely do create intrigue and problems for the Bureaucracy below them.
- This means the **non-Bureaucratic political layer is universal across all four realms**, with different shapes:
  - Primary realms (Celestia, Nyxar) → gods
  - Secondary realms (Feywild, Shadowdark) → local/regional courts and councils
- The Bureaucracy is the *constant* across all four realms; what differs is the kind of non-Bureaucratic actor that operates beside it.
- The "way to read the structure" framing updated: Bureaucracies are the **employment and credentialing** layer; the gods (in primary realms) and the local courts (in secondary realms) are the **political and social** layer.

### Correction noted

In a prior Claude Code session-reply I summarised the asymmetry by calling the primary realms "claustrophobic with paperwork" — under-stating their political life. The primary realms have their own non-Bureaucratic intrigue (gods scheming, alliances shifting, mandates handed down) just as the secondary realms have fey-court and shadow-council intrigue. The asymmetry between primary and secondary realms is about the **shape** of the non-Bureaucratic layer (centralised divine pantheon vs. distributed local courts), not its presence.

### Page updates

- **[[spirits]]** — *Administration: two bureaucracies, four realms* sub-section: the paragraphs about non-Bureaucratic political layers restructured into a four-paragraph block. New opening paragraph ("Every realm has another political layer..."). New paragraph on PRIMARY realms (gods as non-Bureaucratic layer). The existing paragraph on secondary realms preserved but tightened (dropped a comparison phrasing that implied primary realms were Bureaucracy-only). The "way to read the structure" framing updated to include both gods AND local courts in the political-and-social layer.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/spirits-gods-clarification-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the parallel-political-layer canon, the universal-pattern table across all four realms, the correction of the prior under-statement, and the unchanged pending follow-ups.

## 2026-05-11 (eighth) — Gods hate demons: petty grudge canon

The gods' loathing of [[demons|demons]] is canonically **petty**, not noble. Demons disrupted the [[gods-of-eadras#The Game of the Gods|Game of the Gods]] and forced the gods to leave the Game to intervene in the [[demon-war|Demon War]], further disrupting it. Mortal-facing doctrine frames godly opposition to demons as cosmic righteousness; the underlying motive is grudge.

### Canon

- The gods hate demons for personal reasons, not cosmic ones.
- The specific grievance: demons disrupted the **[[gods-of-eadras#The Game of the Gods|Game of the Gods]]**. When the [[demon-war|Demon War]] began and the [[demon-prince-of-the-open-wound|Demon Prince]] tore into Eadras through [[xarvion|Xar'vion]]'s summons, important mortals (Game pieces) died in volumes the Game's rules had never been built to handle; whole regions cleared off the board; carefully-balanced narrative cycles built over millennia were torn up in months.
- **Worse**, the demons forced the gods to *leave the Game* and intervene directly in the war. Intervention itself disrupts the Game — moving a god's own pieces, breaking turn-by-turn discipline. The gods entered the war reluctantly, knowing each direct action further degraded the Game they were trying to defend.
- Most of the divine pantheon's loathing of demons is rooted in this grudge, not moral horror. A god unmoved by mortal suffering on a scale that would shatter mortal minds is *furious* about their interrupted entertainment.
- The [[divine-bureaucracy|Divine Bureaucracy]] has spent millennia **routing around the grudge** — fielding divine demands that demons be hunted, ritualised, anathematised, and framed in mortal-facing doctrine as cosmic evils when the underlying motive was always *they broke our game*. Lirran clergy maintain a quiet tradition of asking awkward questions about divine motivation but few openly note the gap.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *The Game of the Gods* section extended with a new sub-section **"Why the gods hate demons"** covering the petty-grudge canon, the Demon Prince's disruption of the board, the forced direct-intervention double-disruption, the gods' reluctance, and the Divine Bureaucracy's doctrinal-cover work. Sources and Last updated refreshed.
- **[[demons]]** — new section **"Why the gods hate them"** added before *Open canon*, cross-referencing the gods-of-eadras primary canon and noting the mortal-facing doctrine vs underlying motive gap. Sources and Last updated refreshed.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/gods-hate-demons-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the petty-grudge canon, the Game-disruption mechanism, the forced-intervention double disruption, the Divine Bureaucracy's doctrinal management, and the pending follow-up on [[demon-war]].

### Pending follow-up

- **[[demon-war]]** — could optionally note that godly intervention in the war was driven by the petty Game-disruption grudge, not noble cosmic motivation. Existing canon describes the intervention; the new canon adds godly motive. Not urgent; can land next time the demon-war page is touched.

## 2026-05-11 (ninth) — Game of the Gods: nature and causation canon

Extension of the *Game of the Gods* canon with three additions: the Game's structural nature as a miniature of Eadras, the godly complexity of its rules, and the unresolved causation question that mortal philosophers debate.

### Canon

- **The Game is a perfect recreation of the Eadras Mythos in miniature, gamified.** The board is an exact-scale model of the world below, with all important mortals as pieces. Not an abstract gameboard — the actual Eadras Mythos rendered in playable form.
- **The rules are intricate, layered, and *godly*** — appropriate to immortal players, beyond any mortal mind to hold in full. Mechanics resemble D&D in surface form (turn-based, piece-moving) but operate at a different order of strategic depth.
- **The Game seemingly produces outcomes on Eadras.** A god moves a piece, the mortal-world correlate moves: armies march, lovers change their minds, cities' fortunes turn. The correspondence is reliable enough that the gods plainly believe they are playing reality.
- **The direction of causation is one of the great philosophical questions of Eadras**, and from the mortal side it cannot be resolved. Mortal schools have lined up on every position; the gods themselves do not always agree; dispatched divine agents asked about it have given different answers depending on the god. The debate is approximately as old as recorded scholarship.
- **Four canonical positions in the debate**:
  - **Game-causes-Eadras** (no free will; divine moves directly enforce mortal events)
  - **Eadras-causes-Game** (the reflective reading; board mirrors mortal choices; [[lirra|Lirran]] clergy favour this for moral-responsibility reasons)
  - **Isomorphism without direction** (the question is ill-formed; some Tarran philosophers)
  - **Principled refusal to speculate** (mortals can't resolve from inside; [[doctrine-of-unheld-hand|Doctrine of the Unheld Hand]])

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *The Game of the Gods* section: opening paragraph rewritten to incorporate the miniature-of-Eadras canon and the godly-complexity-of-rules canon. New sub-section **"Causation and reality"** added between the opening paragraph and the *Why the gods hate demons* sub-section (added earlier today), covering the causation question, the philosophical debate, and the four positions. Sources line updated.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/game-of-gods-causation-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the four canon points, the four debate positions, the connection to free will / divine intervention / prayer efficacy (largely unexplored this session), and the open-canon hooks.

### Thematic note

The unresolved causation question fits the Eadras tonal register precisely: mortals live with deep cosmic uncertainty about whether their choices are their own, and the divine pantheon — which *could* answer the question — does not even agree among itself. The Doctrine of the Unheld Hand's "asking is not piety" stance reads less as cosmic wisdom and more as the practical theology of a tradition that has noticed the gods are not reliable witnesses on their own causation.

---

## 2026-05-11 (tenth) — Game of the Gods: board nature and subtle play

Extension of the Game of the Gods canon with five additional structural and strategic facts.

### Canon

- The **board updates in real time** — continuously reflecting the state of Eadras-below as it changes. The board IS a divine-realm view of the same world below, not a separate representation.
- All data is shown in **pictographic form** — symbols and shifting iconography that the gods read fluently.
- **Mortals cannot comprehend the board.** A scholar shown it would see an unintelligible mass of moving signs. The pictographic form is what permits immortal players to take in the whole board at once; the information density of Eadras-at-any-instant exceeds mortal capacity.
- Gods can make **subtle moves** — using the Game's rules, an immediate board-effect too subtle for any mortal to register.
- Subtle moves can **produce major results turns later**. Divine plans operating across centuries is, in the Game, mechanical truth — playing the rules *as designed*, not bending them.

### Implications

- **The causation question is deepened.** Even if a mortal accepted "Game-causes-Eadras," they could not trace any particular mortal event back to its originating divine move. Causation, if it exists, is *real but unrecoverable*.
- **Divine plans in Eadras are quiet, layered, and long-term**, not theatrical announcements followed by visible miracles. A god who suddenly intervenes openly is doing something *outside* their usual play.
- **The grudge canon sharpens.** Demons didn't just disrupt casual entertainment — they disrupted plays that had been set up across many turns, possibly across millennia. Setups that would have landed beautifully became unrecoverable in days. From the gods' internal frame, the loss is far more catastrophic than mortals appreciate.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *The Game of the Gods* section: new sub-section **"The board and the play"** inserted between the opening paragraph and the *Causation and reality* sub-section. Covers the five canon points plus the implications for causation and the aesthetics of divine plans. Sources line updated.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/game-of-gods-board-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the five canon points, the implications, the connection to the gods-hate-demons grudge canon (which now reads as a much larger loss from the gods' frame), and the edit notes.

---

## 2026-05-11 (eleventh) — Game of the Gods: evidence in the causation debate

The causation question is now empirically grounded. Canonical examples exist on both sides of the *Game-causes-Eadras* vs *Eadras-causes-Game* debate; the evidence weakens pure versions of both positions and is producing a hybrid asymmetric reading among modern scholars.

### Canon

- **Evidence for the Game causing Eadras**: **direct-effect actions**, especially the moving of **Heroes** (the Game's term for the rare mortal pieces with personal divine attention). When a god moves a Hero, the corresponding mortal Hero in Eadras acts accordingly — sets out, confronts an enemy, makes a choice — and often retrospectively acknowledges *not knowing why* they did so.
- **Evidence against the Game causing Eadras**: **emergent events with no deific cause**. The canonical example is the [[demon-war|Demon War]]: the [[demon-prince-of-the-open-wound|Demon Prince]] was summoned by [[xarvion|Xar'vion]] through ritual operating *outside* the Game's mechanics, not through a Game move. The board *updated* to reflect the catastrophe, but no god initiated it. If the Game caused Eadras purely, no such emergent event should have been possible.
- **Implication**: pure versions of *Game-causes-Eadras* and *Eadras-causes-Game* are both weakened. The *isomorphism* and *principled-refusal* positions remain consistent with the evidence.
- **Emerging hybrid asymmetric reading**: divine moves cause downward for actively-played pieces (Heroes etc.); emergent Eadras-events update the board reflectively. Not yet a canonical fifth school, but increasingly common in [[lirra|Lirran]] and Tarran philosophical circles.

### New Game terminology

- **Hero** — a Game-specific category of mortal piece, marked by personal divine attention. Heroes are the rare pieces gods actively play turn-by-turn. The mechanical and social distinction between Heroes and ordinary mortal-pieces is open canon.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *Causation and reality* sub-section: new paragraphs inserted between *"The Game's nature is, from any single vantage, opaque."* and the four-position list. Cover evidence for / evidence against / weakening of pure positions / emerging asymmetric reading / Hero terminology. Sources line updated.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/game-of-gods-evidence-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the evidence on both sides, the implications, the emerging hybrid position, and the new "Hero" terminology.

---

## 2026-05-11 (twelfth) — Game of the Gods: divine ignorance via Dao's secret-making

Final addition to today's Game canon: even the gods do not know the answer to the causation question. The mechanism is the existing canon ([[dao]] made the Game *in secret*, and the Game "simply appeared one day in Solarion"); the canon clarifies that Dao did not explain the Game and has not been interrogable since. The pantheon plays competently after millennia of practice but never received instruction.

### Canon

- The gods of Eadras **do not know** whether the Game causes Eadras or Eadras causes the Game (or any other position in the causation debate). This is not coyness or secret-keeping; it is genuine ignorance.
- The Game was created by [[dao]] in secret. Dao did not explain it. It simply appeared one day in [[solarion|Solarion]], complete and already playing.
- The current pantheon has learned the Game's rules through millennia of play — by trial, observation, and practice, not by instruction. They cannot interrogate the designer.
- The gods who give different answers when asked about causation are reporting **private theories formed during long play**, not authoritative knowledge. Their disagreements are not serious among themselves because none of them claim authority on the question.
- The principled-refusal position (the [[doctrine-of-unheld-hand|Doctrine of the Unheld Hand]]) reads, in light of this canon, as particularly mature — it acknowledges what the pantheon also acknowledges: the answer is not accessible to anyone currently inside the system.

### Story-rationale note

A still-existing secret-maker (Dao, who continues to exist somewhere in the cosmological frame and continues not to explain) is a better story than a dissolved-designer team (a reading briefly considered earlier this turn — *the Primordial Duo as last-act creators before dissolution* — and discarded as making weaker story). The mystery is **live**, not historical. The "Created by Dao in secret" canon is preserved across [[gods-of-eadras]] and [[solarion]]; this addition deepens it rather than retcons it.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *Causation and reality* sub-section: the *"Philosophers argue"* paragraph updated to add the gods-do-not-know canon and to explain that divine ignorance traces to Dao's secret-making. The "Created by Dao in secret" opening of the section is preserved unchanged. Sources line updated.

### Raw session capture

### Pending follow-up

- **[[solarion]]** not updated this session — its "Created by Dao in secret" line is preserved as-is. If anything needs to be added there later, it would be a brief cross-reference to the divine-ignorance canon on [[gods-of-eadras#Causation and reality]]. Not urgent.

## 2026-05-11 (thirteenth) — Dao: monitor not overseer, triple role canon

Unified role-framing for [[dao|Dao]]'s function within Eadras. The existing dao.md page documents many acts in detail; this canon provides the *frame* under which those acts make a single coherent purpose. The "Dao is invisible to the Gods" element of today's earlier turn is already established on dao.md (*"completely hidden from the Elder Gods of Eadras"*); no new edit needed for that.

### Canon

- Dao is a **monitor, not an overseer.** He watches; he does not govern.
- His function has **three distinct components**:
  1. **Ensure things run smoothly** — operational-level intervention only where systems would otherwise fail.
  2. **Keep the macro balance** — cosmological-scale equilibrium (the *Necessary Shadow* doctrine is its articulation).
  3. **Experience life as an individual semi-mortal, and transmit the experience back to the [[omniversal-creator|Omniversal Creator]]** — the genuinely new addition. Dao's humble guises (farmer, tinker, village elder) are not just concealment; they are *lived experience* gathered as the Creator's reading lens for what mortal life is *like*.
- The three components run in parallel across eons, all the time. They are facets of one constant monitor-job.

### Implications

- The existing "humble guises" section on dao.md gains depth: it's part of the Creator's mortal-experience pipeline, not just a concealment technique.
- The patience-based method is the monitor's natural disposition.
- The Necessary Shadow doctrine fits role 2.
- **Possible extrapolation (not stated by Josh, not committed to canon):** the Game of the Gods may serve role 1 — keeping the gods busy and preventing overly-direct intervention in mortal affairs, which would disrupt the smooth running of the Mythos. The gods-don't-know-the-rules canon (the gods learned through millennia of play, never from instruction) is consistent with Dao's monitor stance — he didn't sit them down for a rules seminar; he just gave them the Game and watched.

### Page updates

- **[[dao]]** — new section **"Role"** inserted between *Nature* and *Manifestation in Eadras*, capturing the monitor-not-overseer framing and the triple-role structure. Sources line updated. Last updated bumped to 2026-05-11.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/dao-monitor-role-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the canon, the implications, the connection to today's earlier Game canon, and the pending follow-ups.

### Pending follow-up

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — could note that the Game plausibly serves Dao's role 1 (extrapolation; awaits user confirmation).
- **[[omniversal-creator]]** — could note that the Creator monitors mortal experience through Dao's semi-mortal incarnations (awaits user read on whether this is too disclosive of Creator-side mechanics).
