## 2026-05-11 (fourteenth) — Eadras pantheon: multiverse position and the Game as benign containment

Major addition setting cosmic context for the Eadras pantheon and resolving the speculation flagged in the (thirteenth) entry about the Game serving Dao's Role 1. It serves *both* Role 1 *and* Role 2 — the Game is benign multi-purpose containment against what would otherwise be an Omniversal expansion problem.

### Canon

- **Eadras is one of the most magically rich Mythoi in the Omniverse.** Magical richness is the source of deity power.
- **The Eadras pantheon are among the most powerful deities in the multiverse**, positionally rather than intrinsically — a similar god in a thinner Mythos would be a far smaller being.
- **Standard high-tier deity pattern across the Omniverse is expansionist** — pushing worship outward into neighbouring Mythoi, contesting other pantheons, accruing influence beyond the home plane.
- **The Eadras pantheon does not do this.** They are turned almost entirely inward, absorbed in the [[gods-of-eadras#The Game of the Gods|Game of the Gods]].
- **The Game is the containment mechanism.** It keeps the pantheon busy *without harming them* — not a chain, not a binding. The gods remain at full power and simply spend it inward, because the Game is more interesting than anything outside Eadras would be.
- From [[dao|Dao's]] [[dao#Role|monitor frame]], the Game serves **both Role 1 (smooth running of Eadras) and Role 2 (macro balance of the Omniverse)**. This resolves the extrapolation flagged in the (thirteenth) entry.
- **The pantheon does not experience the Game as containment.** From inside it, it is the most interesting thing in existence — which it largely is, for them. The system is stable because it is genuinely satisfying to the contained.

### Implications

- The "deeply addictive" descriptor of the Game (existing canon) now reads as *design intent* (or at minimum, a feature Dao did not mitigate) rather than as accident.
- The grudge canon (gods hate demons because demons disrupted the Game) sharpens further: demons didn't just disrupt entertainment, they threatened to break the containment that maintains macro balance. From Dao's frame the Demon War was a near-disaster at the Omniversal scale, not just a Mythos-internal disturbance.
- The pantheon's exceptional power is a *structural consequence* of Eadras's magical richness, not a virtue of the gods themselves.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — new section **"Position in the multiverse"** inserted between the worship paragraph and *The Game of the Gods*. Covers the pantheon's exceptional power, the standard expansionist pattern, the Eadras pantheon's exceptional inward orientation, the Game as benign containment, and the dual-role framing from Dao's monitor frame. Sources line updated.
- **[[dao]]** — *Role* section: final paragraph added after the three-component list, citing the Game as a worked example of Roles 1 and 2 in action. Cross-references [[gods-of-eadras#Position in the multiverse]].

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/pantheon-multiverse-position-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the canon, the Game-as-multi-purpose-containment framing, the connection to today's earlier canon (grudge sharpened, divine ignorance contextualised), the design-intent reading of the Game's addictiveness, and pending follow-ups.

### Pending follow-ups

- **[[omniverse]]** / **[[mythos]]** / **[[eadras-cosmology]]** — could note that Eadras is one of the most magically rich Mythoi and that this has cosmic implications. Not urgent.

## 2026-05-11 (fifteenth) — Godpower and the Well of Creation: the universal mechanism

Foundational canon: every god in every Mythos draws power from the same kind of source. The mechanism explains and underlies today's earlier "Eadras pantheon is positionally powerful" canon.

### Canon

- **Godpower (in all Mythoi) taps the leftover primordial power in the Well of Creation that exists in every Mythos.**
- The [[omniversal-creator|Omniversal Creator]] puts **Creative Power** into every Mythos at its making.
- Most of that Creative Power is spent on creation (planes, laws, substance). What remains is **leftover**, sitting in the **Well of Creation** of that Mythos.
- A deity's power, anywhere in the Omniverse, is **a tap on the local leftover Creative Power**.
- Variation between Mythoi (magic-rich vs thin, mighty pantheons vs marginal) is variation in *how much* leftover Creative Power each Well holds.
- Eadras's exceptional pantheon power is now mechanically explained: Eadras has one of the largest Wells, so its leftover Creative Power is vast, so its gods are mighty.
- **Theological consequence:** gods are not the source of their own power. Whatever they do is ultimately a borrowing from the OC's prior creative act.

### New terminology

- **Godpower** — cross-Mythos theological term for the power gods exercise.
- **Well of Creation** — the reservoir in every Mythos containing the OC's leftover Creative Power.
- **Creative Power** — what the OC pours into each Mythos at its making.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — new section **"Source of godly power"** inserted between the worship paragraph and *Position in the multiverse*. Covers the universal architecture, the Godpower term, the Well, the positional variation, and the theological consequence. Sources line updated.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/godpower-well-of-creation-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the canon, the implications, the open questions (Well refillable or finite, mortal magic relationship, Primordial Duo's sacrifice contribution to Eadras's Well, etc.), and pending page follow-ups.

### Pending follow-ups (added by this canon)

- **[[omniversal-creator]]** — should note the OC's role in putting Creative Power into every Mythos at making, with the leftover constituting the Well.
- **[[mythos]]** — Wells of Creation are structural canon about what a Mythos is; should be referenced.
- **[[magic-in-eadras]]** — open canon on whether Eadras's magical mechanisms (Weave / Pillar Magic / Netharim / Lexanari / true language) are Well-derived. Worth checking when the magic-system rework is next touched.
- A dedicated **`well-of-creation.md`** page is a candidate if the concept accumulates more detail.

## 2026-05-11 (sixteenth) — Godpower: direct link, Spear's link, and Eadras Well retcon

Two canon additions plus one major retcon to the (fourteenth) entry's "Eadras has a large Well" framing.

### Canon: direct link

- **All gods hold a direct link to their Mythos's Well of Creation.** The connection is unmediated — no priestly conduit, no intermediary, no permission required beyond divinity itself. A god is, by definition, *something that holds a direct link to its local Well*.
- **The [[spear-of-crystallized-entropy|Spear of Crystallized Entropy]] also holds a direct link.** It is the canonical non-deity exception. This explains why the Spear operates at god-tier power and is so catastrophic when wielded — it has the same unmediated tap a god has. In a very specific sense the Spear *is* a god, though a thing rather than a person. The Spear is the reason a mortal can, briefly and disastrously, exercise something resembling divine power. ([[dao]]'s curse on the Spear is what keeps that touch from being merely beneficial.)

### Retcon: Eadras has the smallest Well, not a large one

The (fourteenth) entry stated Eadras has one of the largest Wells in the Omniverse. **That extrapolation was wrong.** Corrected canon:

- Eadras has the **smallest Well in the multiverse** by raw allotment. The OC put very little Creative Power into Eadras at its making, and what little was there was largely spent during creation.
- By raw-allotment measure, the Eadras pantheon should be *thin*, not mighty.
- The exception is **location**: Eadras sits immediately adjacent to the [[concordance|Concordance]], and the [[bastion-of-light|Bastion of Light]] continuously feeds Eadras's Well through Concordance-proximity. The Bastion radiates Creative Power; the nearest Mythos receives the seep; Eadras is the nearest Mythos.
- The Eadras pantheon is therefore powerful by **rate of replenishment**, not by depth of Well. *A gift of geography.*

### Implications

- Eadras's exceptional pantheon strength is conditional on continued Bastion feed. The pantheon's existence is structurally dependent on cosmic geography rather than intrinsic Mythos wealth.
- The Demon War threatened more than the Game's containment — demons potentially disrupting the closest seep-point from the Bastion to the rest of the Omniverse is a *broader* cosmic threat than mere Mythos-internal disruption.
- The Eadras pantheon, properly understood, is a **fed** pantheon, not an endowed one. Their power is a continuous gift, not a possession.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *Source of godly power* section: two new paragraphs added on the direct-link canon and the Spear's exceptional link. *Position in the multiverse* section: opening paragraph **rewritten** to retcon the "large Well" framing, establishing the Bastion-feed mechanism (smallest Well + continuous replenishment = positionally powerful). Sources line updated.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/godpower-direct-link-and-eadras-feed-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the direct-link canon, the Spear's link, the Eadras Well retcon, the Bastion feed mechanism, implications (cosmic dependency, demon-war scale), and open canon hooks.

### Pending follow-ups (added by this canon)

- **[[spear-of-crystallized-entropy]]** — should note the direct-link canon as the underlying reason for the Spear's god-tier power; Dao's curse takes on additional significance.
- **[[bastion-of-light]]** — should describe the radiation-into-Concordance mechanism and Eadras's privileged feed position.
- **[[concordance]]** — as the conduit plane through which Bastion radiation passes to Eadras.
- **[[omniversal-creator]]** — feed canon could be noted here (still flagged from earlier).

Previous pending follow-ups remain queued.

## 2026-05-11 (seventeenth) — Eadras's Well: corrected history (intrinsically rich → mostly expended → small remainder + Bastion feed)

Third retcon of Eadras's Well today, this time correctly. The (fourteenth) entry said the Well was *large*; the (sixteenth) entry over-corrected to *smallest in multiverse by raw allotment*. Both were wrong. The actual canon is a story over time, with two separate truths that don't conflict once put in order.

### Canon (final state)

- **Eadras is intrinsically rich.** The Omniversal Creator put a substantial allotment of Creative Power into Eadras at its making — Eadras was not made poor.
- The **[[primordial-duo|Primordial Duo]]'s sacrificed essence was added to the Well**, deepening it further. Eadras began with one of the deepest reservoirs in the Omniverse.
- **Most of that combined essence was expended in creation.** *Most of the Primordial Duo's essence, and most of the Well*, went into producing the planes, the laws, the substance, and the conditions of life that make Eadras the place it is.
- What remains in the Well today is **a small remainder of what was once a deep reservoir**.
- The small remainder **never empties** because the [[bastion-of-light|Bastion of Light]] continuously feeds it through [[concordance|Concordance]]-proximity (canon from the sixteenth entry; preserved).
- Result: Eadras is magic-rich by **rate of replenishment** flowing into a small Well, not by current depth and not by original allotment (most of that was poured outward into the creation that *is* Eadras).
- The pantheon's strength is a "gift of geography compounding what remains of an originally rich allotment that was poured out into the Mythos itself."

### Resolution of two earlier open-canon items

- *Did the Primordial Duo's sacrifice contribute to Eadras's Well?* **Yes** — their essence was added; subsequently most was consumed in creation along with most of the OC's original allotment.
- *Is Eadras's exceptional richness OC-baseline-plus-Primordial or just OC-baseline?* **Both** — substantial OC allotment plus added Primordial Duo essence; together they constituted an unusually deep starting Well.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *Position in the multiverse* section: opening paragraphs rewritten (third time today, this time correctly). Captures the intrinsic richness, the Primordial Duo contribution, the mass expenditure in creation, the small remainder, the Bastion feed, and the integrated result. Sources line updated.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/eadras-well-corrected-history-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures both earlier retcons, the canonical final state, the five-stage history of Eadras's Well (allotment → Primordial contribution → expenditure in creation → small remainder → Bastion feed), and pending follow-ups.

### Pending follow-ups (added)

- **[[primordial-duo]]** — should note the Duo's sacrificed essence went into Eadras's Well, and that most was consumed in creating the Mythos.
- **[[creation-myth]]** — if it exists, similar update.

Previous follow-ups remain queued.

## 2026-05-11 (eighteenth) — Eadras's position: untangling intrinsic richness from Well size, and the Primordial sacrifice as unique circumstance

Fourth and (intended) final pass on the Eadras-position canon today. The error that ran across the three earlier retcons was conflating two genuinely distinct properties: **intrinsic magical richness of the Mythos** vs. **size of the Well of Creation**. They vary independently. Additionally, the **Primordial sacrifice is unique to Eadras** in the Omniverse — other Mythoi's primordials still rule.

### Canon (corrected, properly disentangled)

- **Intrinsic magical richness** is a property of the **Mythos itself** — its substance, laws, architecture. Eadras IS intrinsically magically rich. This is independent of Well size.
- **Well size** regulates total Godpower available to the local pantheon — a power-budget. Eadras's current Well is small.
- **The two properties are independent** and should not be conflated. A Mythos can be intrinsically rich with a small Well, or thin with a large one.
- **The Well size only acts as a cap when not refilled.** Eadras's Well is always full (Bastion feed), so size-as-cap doesn't apply; the pantheon has effectively unlimited Godpower access.
- **The Primordial sacrifice is unique to Eadras.** Evye and Fryr sacrificed themselves; their essence went into the Well and the world's substance; most was consumed creating Eadras's intrinsic magical richness. No other Mythos has had this happen.
- **Other Mythoi**: primordials are still present and still rule as the top tier of divinity; Wells are not depleted in this way; intrinsic richness varies (often less than Eadras's, since no comparable expenditure).
- **The Eadras pantheon is exceptional because three rare conditions align**: (1) intrinsically rich Mythos, (2) always-full Well (Bastion feed), (3) no primordial-tier active divinity above them (sacrifice left a vacancy). No other pantheon has all three.

### My earlier confusions, recorded for posterity

| Entry | What I said | Why it was wrong |
|---|---|---|
| (fourteenth) | Eadras has one of the largest Wells | Conflated intrinsic richness with Well size |
| (sixteenth) | Eadras has the smallest Well by raw allotment | Over-corrected; original allotment was substantial |
| (seventeenth) | Intrinsic richness lives in the Well's depth/history | Still conflating; richness is a Mythos property |
| (eighteenth, this) | Two distinct properties; Primordial sacrifice is unique | Should be correct |

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *Position in the multiverse* section: **fourth rewrite today**, using three explicit sub-sections (*Eadras is intrinsically magically rich* / *The Primordial sacrifice — Eadras's unique circumstance* / *Why the pantheon is still powerful*) to disentangle the two properties and make the Primordial-sacrifice uniqueness explicit. Sources updated.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/eadras-position-final-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the disentangled-properties canon, the Primordial-sacrifice uniqueness, the three-aligned-conditions structure, the corrections to all three earlier retcons, and pending follow-ups.

### Pending follow-ups (added)

- **[[primordial-duo]]** — should note the sacrifice is *unique in the Omniverse*. Other Mythoi's primordials still rule. The Eadras sacrifice is one-of-a-kind.
- **Open canon worth exploring later:** why did the Primordial Duo choose to sacrifice when no other primordial creators did? Was it required to produce a Mythos with Eadras's intrinsic richness, or was it a choice made under different constraints?

Previous follow-ups remain queued.

## 2026-05-11 (nineteenth) — Primordial sacrifice: rare-but-not-unique correction; motivation canon

Two corrections to the (eighteenth) entry: the sacrifice is **not unique** to Eadras (existing canon on [[primordial-duo]] already established the *seven closest Mythoi* framing — I missed it); and the **motivation** for the Primordials' sacrifice is now canonical.

### Canon

- The Primordial sacrifice has happened in only a small handful of Mythoi: **the seven Mythoi closest to the [[bastion-of-light|Bastion of Light]]** (Eadras among them), and possibly some Mythoi of the **second cosmographical ring** outward (open canon).
- Across the rest of the infinite Omniverse, primordial creators are still present, still ruling, and have not consumed their Wells. The sacrificial pattern is *extraordinarily rare* — restricted to a small inner cluster around the Bastion.
- **Motivation of Eadras's Primordial Duo**:
  - They had **no desire to rule** what they made.
  - They wanted to create the **most bountiful, diverse, magically rich Mythos possible**.
  - They **trusted the Elder Gods** (whom they themselves had made) to **shape creation alongside them during the creative act, and to rule after their departure**.
  - The Elder Gods are therefore **co-creators by design and successors by deliberate handoff**, not just inheritors.

### Existing canon I missed earlier today

The [[primordial-duo]] page already stated: *"This also placed Eadras among the seven Mythoi closest to the core of the Omniverse."* I should have read that page before claiming the sacrifice was "unique to Eadras in the Omniverse" in the (eighteenth) entry. The error cascaded from not checking adjacent canon — a recurring problem across today's session.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *Position in the multiverse*: the Primordial-sacrifice sub-section retitled and rewritten to use the *rare-but-not-unique* / *seven closest* framing and cross-reference the motivation canon now on [[primordial-duo]]. The *Why the pantheon is still powerful* sub-section softened from "what no other pantheon has" to "what only the seven closest Mythoi possess," and the closing line about "three rare circumstances aligned in one place" updated to acknowledge the close cosmic neighbours.
- **[[primordial-duo]]** — new section **"Why they sacrificed"** inserted between *Creation* and *The Exchange*. Covers the no-desire-to-rule motivation, the most-bountiful-creation ambition, the trust-Elder-Gods handoff, and the rare-not-unique seven-closest framing. Sources line + Last updated refreshed.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/eadras-sacrifice-context-and-motivation-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the corrections, the motivation canon, the seven-closest cosmographical structure, the open question about whether proximity to the Bastion *causes* sacrifice or vice versa, and an acknowledgment that this is the fifth retcon on the Eadras-position section today.

### Pending follow-ups (added)

- **[[bastion-of-light]]** — should mention the seven-closest-Mythoi pattern and the proximity-via-sacrifice mechanism (open canon).
- **[[omniverse]]** — cosmographical structure (concentric rings around the Bastion) is structural canon.
- **Open canon**: why does proximity correlate with primordial sacrifice? Existing primordial-duo.md canon implies sacrifice → proximity (*"This also placed Eadras among the seven Mythoi closest"*) — pouring divine essence into a Mythos's substance plausibly draws the Mythos closer to the OC's home. Worth fleshing out later.

Previous follow-ups remain queued.

## 2026-05-11 (twentieth) — Primordial sacrifice method + Eadras planewalker strength

Two additions: sharpening the *method* of the Primordial sacrifice (most Primordials use Well-energy only; Evye and Fryr did **both** — Well and essence), and introducing new canon about **planewalkers from Eadras being 2–4x stronger** than planewalkers from other Mythoi. Plus confirmation from Josh that sacrifice → proximity is canonical (pouring divine essence into a Mythos's substance draws it closer to the Bastion of Light).

### Canon: sacrifice method

- Most Primordial creators across the Omniverse **use only the Well of Creation's energy** to create — the Creative Power the OC put into the Mythos at its making. Their own essence stays intact. They remain to rule.
- Evye and Fryr **did both**: spent down the Well extensively *and* poured out their own essence on top. The result: a severely depleted Well plus complete dissolution of both creators.
- This double-pour method is unusual even among the seven closest Mythoi where primordial sacrifice happens at all. It is what makes Eadras exceptional even within the rare-sacrifice cluster.
- **Confirmed**: sacrifice → proximity. Pouring divine essence into a Mythos's substance draws that Mythos closer to the [[bastion-of-light|Bastion of Light]]. The seven closest Mythoi are close *because* their primordials sacrificed, not the inverse.

### Canon: Eadras planewalker strength

- **Planewalkers from Eadras are fundamentally 2–4× stronger than planewalkers from other Mythoi.** The multiplier covers strength, magical capacity, endurance, and the depth/quality of exercised powers.
- "Fundamentally" — the advantage is *structural*, not situational. It is a property of being-from-Eadras.
- Applies to *all* planewalkers from Eadras, regardless of whether they are divine, mortal, ascended, or artifact-bound.
- Mechanism: Eadras's intrinsic magical richness — saturated into the Mythos's substance by the Primordial Duo's double-pour sacrifice — infuses every being born or made within Eadras. They carry the saturation with them across boundaries.
- The advantage is **enduring rather than transient**: it does not fade with time away from Eadras. (Whether sufficiently long absence eventually erodes it is open canon.)
- **Cross-Mythos contact involving Eadras is structurally asymmetric.** Eadras beings visiting other Mythoi arrive overpowered; visitors *to* Eadras do not get the inverse boost. The advantage is bound to origin, not to location.

### Page updates

- **[[planewalkers]]** — **new page created**, `canon_status: established`. Covers what planewalkers are, the 2–4× Eadras advantage, persistence and asymmetry, practical implications, open canon.
- **[[primordial-duo]]** — *The Exchange* section: the existing line "No other creator deities sacrificed themselves so completely" is replaced with the proper canon. Most Primordials use Well-only; Evye and Fryr did both; severely depleted Well + complete dissolution; double-pour also explains why Eadras was placed among the seven Bastion-closest Mythoi.
- **[[index]]** — `[[planewalkers]]` added to the *Eadras Internal Planes* section under [[spirits]].

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/eadras-planewalker-strength-and-sacrifice-method-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures both canon additions, the confirmed sacrifice→proximity mechanism, the structural asymmetry of cross-Mythos contact, and a meta-note on today's session's pattern of over-extrapolation followed by correction.

### Pending follow-ups (added)

- **[[bastion-of-light]]** — seven-closest pattern and confirmed sacrifice → proximity mechanism.
- **[[magic-in-eadras]]** — the "thick and alive" magic comes from *both* Well-allotment and Primordial essence (double-pour).
- **Specific named planewalkers** from Eadras-canon — currently undocumented; could be developed.

Previous follow-ups remain queued.

- **`.claude/skills/negative-space/SKILL.md`** — full vault scan for (era × race × tag) under-covered cells. Uses parallel Explore subagent for the actual enumeration. Read-only over wiki; outputs to `derived/negative-space/`.

### First scan output

- **`derived/negative-space/scan-2026-05-11.md`** — full report. Headline finding: 220 non-meta canon pages, 206 of them (93.6%) tagged `historical_horizon: [all]`. Only 12 pages target specific eras. Demon War / Dragon-Unicorn / Dimming / Dragon eras all have zero pages tagged despite rich content existing.

### Era-tagging sweep (this session)

Six event-page tagging fixes applied directly. Each was `historical_horizon: [all]` → era-specific:

- `demon-war.md` → `[demon-war]`
- `battle-of-the-broken-conclaves.md` → `[demon-war]`
- `three-who-stood.md` → `[demon-war]`
- `great-betrayal.md` → `[demon-war]`
- `great-banishment.md` → `[demon-war]`
- `sorcerer-crusade.md` → `[dimming]` (the Crusade is a Dimming-era event, ~5000ya, not Demon War-era)

Pure tagging changes; no body content modified. Last-updated lines preserved per CLAUDE.md (body content unchanged → Last-updated stays).

### Held for user judgment

These race / multi-era pages were *not* re-tagged this turn — they span multiple eras and the single-value `historical_horizon` schema doesn't accommodate spans:

- `orugi.md`, `el-mer.md`, `aetherins.md`, `titans.md` — extinct-at-Final-Wall races whose pages cover origin → engineering → war → modern descendants
- `three-thirds-of-the-rathar.md` — fragmentation that happened during the war but persists today

Default stance per the scan: leave at `[all]`. The user can override.

## 2026-05-11 (twenty-second) — `/adversarial` skill installed + first probe on Eadras-position canon

Second new skill of the session. Uses parallel subagents (Skeptic + Advocate) to stress-test canon before commit, or audit canon after major revision.

### Skill installed

- **`.claude/skills/adversarial/SKILL.md`** — spawns two parallel general-purpose subagents under different mandates. Skeptic finds contradictions, over-claims, weak assumptions, missing implications, schema issues, pressure points. Advocate defends load-bearing claims, structural strengths, supporting evidence, design rationale, what would be lost. Aggregator combines both into a single artifact at `derived/adversarial/`. Read-only over wiki.

### First probe run

- **Target:** `gods-of-eadras § Position in the multiverse` (the heavily-retconned section from today; chosen specifically because it had five rewrites and is the hardest test case).
- **Output:** `derived/adversarial/eadras-position-2026-05-11.md` — both reports in full plus six areas of agreement, seven areas of disagreement, and twelve suggested actions ranked by effort.

### Key findings

**Agreements (high confidence canon):** the two-properties disentanglement is the section's strongest contribution; the seven-closest framing is cross-page consistent; the Primordial-sacrifice motivation canon is well-grounded; planewalkers is structurally downstream of this section; the positional-not-intrinsic framing is thematically successful.

**Disagreements (user judgment needed):**
1. Is intrinsic richness *genuinely independent* of Well size, or causally linked in practice?
2. Is Godpower unbounded or "effectively unbounded subject to per-god capacity"?
3. Does Dao count as primordial-tier active divinity?
4. Is "expansionist gods" actually the universal default?
5. Is the Bastion-radiation mechanism canonically established or speculative?
6. Is the "seven closest" count precisely known, or speculative?
7. Is the Game's "design intent" framing fact or interpretation?

### Suggested actions (by effort)

- **Small cleanup**: fix the anchor-link style inconsistency (`[Well](#source-of-godly-power)` → `[[#Source of godly power|Well]]`); trim or restructure the bloated Sources line; add a clarifying parenthetical for Dao in the "no primordial-tier active divinity" sentence.
- **Medium**: reword the independence claim to acknowledge it's conceptual-but-coincident-in-canon; clarify "effectively unlimited" as referring to Well availability not per-god capacity; hedge or canonise the Bastion-radiation mechanism; reframe Game's function as observable rather than designed.
- **Larger**: bump knowledge_access for scholarly claims; establish in-universe attestation for the "seven closest" count; bridge the Demon War tension within the page.

### Notes

The probe found that even after five retcons, the section still has 7 substantive disagreement points and ~15 specific Skeptic findings, several of which are actionable cleanup. **The skill is working.** It would have caught most of these issues if run *before* committing the retcons rather than after — which is the canonical use-case suggested in the SKILL.md.

The parallel-subagent pattern (two general-purpose agents launched in a single message) executed cleanly. Each agent independently read ~8–10 pages and produced ~1500–2500 words of analysis; aggregation happened in the main session.

### Pending follow-up

- **User to decide which (if any) of the disagreement-points to resolve.** The seven areas of disagreement are real canon decisions waiting for the user. None are urgent; all are listed in `derived/adversarial/eadras-position-2026-05-11.md` with proposed resolutions.

## 2026-05-11 (twenty-third) — Adversarial-probe resolutions: 3 canon decisions committed

User responded to the seven disagreement points from the (twenty-second) probe. Three are committed as canon updates; four remain open user-judgment items.

### Canon committed

**1. Independence of intrinsic richness vs Well size — reframed.**
The two properties are *conceptually* independent variables. In sacrifice-Mythoi (the seven closest) they co-vary by shared cause — pouring out both Well-allotment and Primordial essence into substance produces intrinsic richness at the cost of the Well that remains. The typical consequence (small Well → modest pantheon) follows in most sacrifice-Mythoi. Eadras's exception is the Bastion feed, which decouples the consequence from the cause.

**2. Godpower is unbounded only on the Well axis; two other axes still constrain.**
Three-axis model now explicit:
- *Well size* — effectively unlimited in Eadras, finite elsewhere
- *Per-god draw capacity* — bounded everywhere; [[doctrine-of-unheld-hand|Auralis and Thamior]] is the canonical precedent (used full draw + personal life-force, dwindled to faint avatars; did *not* drain the Well — that mechanism doesn't apply at the individual-action scale)
- *Bureaucratic channeling* — the [[divine-bureaucracy|Divine Bureaucracy]] operates on rules (doctrine, Favor, procedure), not on power scarcity; miracle denials are doctrinal/procedural

The Eadras pantheon is unbounded on axis 1 and bounded on axes 2 and 3.

**3. Dao does NOT count as primordial-tier active divinity.**
Categorical: Dao is not a Mythos divinity, holds no Mythos portfolio, doesn't regulate the Mythos. His function is as an [[omniversal-creator|OC]] Avatar — a tier-prior cosmic layer that doesn't enter the Mythos's internal divinity ordering. "No primordial-tier active divinity in Eadras's pantheon" is therefore correct without retraction; the page now adds a parenthetical noting Dao as the cosmic-prior exception outside the local order.

### Non-issues (Skeptic findings explicitly rejected)

- **Unbounded vs Bureau:** the Bureau operates on rules, not on scarcity. Auralis/Thamior is a per-god draw-capacity precedent, not a Well-drain precedent. No contradiction.
- **No primordial-tier vs Dao:** Dao is outside the Mythos's divinity; doesn't participate in the ordering. No contradiction.
- **Expansionist gods unsupported:** Primary focus of the wiki is Eadras; Omniverse descriptions are useful background. Acceptable as background context without requiring full mechanical grounding.
- **Cross-Mythos divine business:** gods from different Mythoi conduct business in the Outer Realms (around Concordance) and in Nexus itself. Existing canon, confirmed.

### Still open (user judgment, deferred)

- Bastion-radiation mechanism (over-claim or canon-quality?)
- "Seven closest" count precision
- Game's "design intent" framing (fact or interpretation?)
- Schema cleanup (anchor-link style, bloated Sources line, knowledge_access mismatch, perspective register wobble)

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *Position in the multiverse*: three precise edits applied per the resolutions above.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/adversarial-resolutions-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the three resolutions, the four rejected Skeptic findings, the four still-open items, and the edits applied.

### Pending follow-ups (added)

- **[[divine-bureaucracy]]** — explicitly note Bureau operates on rules, not power scarcity. Surfaced as an implicit issue by the probe.
- **[[dao]]** — add "no Mythos portfolio" clarification (sharpens the "outside the Mythos's divinity" framing already on the page).

### Workflow note

This is the canonical use-case the `/adversarial` skill was designed for: probe → user resolves → commit. Worked cleanly. The probe surfaced seven real items, three of which produced canon updates and four of which were correctly rejected because they assumed a stricter mechanism than the canon actually requires. The skill earned its keep on its first run.

Previous follow-ups queued.

## 2026-05-11 (twenty-fourth) — Worship as a secondary source of godpower + remaining Skeptic findings

User responded to the four still-open items from the adversarial probe. **One major new canon (worship-as-power)** plus confirmations on Bastion-radiation and seven-closest as canonical; item 7 (Game design intent) deferred for user direction.

### Canon committed

**Worship as a secondary power source.** Gods across the Omniverse derive a secondary stream of power from worshippers. More worshippers = more godpower; loss of worshippers shrinks effective capacity. In typical Mythoi (finite, slowly-draining Wells) worship-power is **load-bearing** — this is the structural reason most pantheons are *expansionist*. Cross-Mythos competition for worshippers happens in the **Outer Realms** (encircling the Concordance) and in **Nexus** (megacity where gods of every Mythos can meet); gods don't invade other Mythoi directly — they contest in these shared venues.

The Eadras pantheon is the canonical exception. Bastion-fed Well makes Well-power unlimited, so worship-power is not load-bearing for them. Worship still flows (priesthoods exist, Bureau of Prayer and Bureau of Favor still process it institutionally), but it isn't the substrate of their existence. This is part of why they can afford to be inward-turned and Game-absorbed instead of expansionist.

### Canon confirmed (already on the page)

- **Bastion-radiation mechanism** is canon. No hedging needed.
- **"Seven closest"** is precisely seven, canon. No hedging needed.

### Page updates

- **[[gods-of-eadras]]** — *Source of godly power*: new sub-section **"Worship as a secondary source of godpower"** added after the Spear paragraph. Explains the mechanism for expansionism, the cross-Mythos venues (Outer Realms, Nexus), and Eadras's exception. *Position in the multiverse*: the expansionist paragraph updated to reference the worship-power mechanism and the cross-Mythos venues. Sources line not updated this turn (will batch with item-7 resolution if needed).

### Item 7 deferred (Game design intent)

The Skeptic flagged that the Position section attributes design *intent* to the Game ("the mechanism that maintains" / "benign containment") while the Causation section honestly admits Dao made the Game in secret and didn't explain. Two possible readings:

- **Function reading** (Advocate): the page describes the Game's observable effect, not Dao's intent. Fine as written.
- **Intent reading** (Skeptic): the page calls the effect "not coincidence," "benign containment," and attributes purpose — which goes beyond observable function to a claim about Dao's design intent that canon does not establish.

User direction needed: (a) canonize Dao's design intent (the page keeps its current confidence), (b) hedge the page to describe function only, or (c) preserve current language under the position that observers can infer purpose from consistent function.

### Pending follow-ups (added)

- Item 7 awaits user direction.
- **[[divine-bureaucracy]]** — explicit note that Bureau operates on rules, not scarcity (from previous resolution).
- **[[dao]]** — "no Mythos portfolio" clarification.
- **[[nexus]]** / Outer Realms — venues for cross-Mythos divine business. Worth confirming these pages exist and capture the venue canon.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/worship-as-power-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the worship-as-power canon, the Outer Realms/Nexus venue canon, the Eadras-pantheon exception, and the deferred item 7 explanation.

Previous follow-ups queued.

## 2026-05-11 (twenty-fifth) — `/multi-pov` skill installed + first run on the Final Wall

Third and last of the skills Josh queued for this session. Like `/adversarial`, uses parallel subagents — but multiple of them (N=3 in this run), each rendering the same event in a different in-universe voice and tradition.

### Skill installed

- **`.claude/skills/multi-pov/SKILL.md`** — spawns one subagent per perspective in parallel, each writing the event in that perspective's voice. Aggregates accounts plus a comparison analysis to `derived/multi-pov/`. Read-only over wiki. Fits the Tome-of-Baldaran conceit precisely.

### First run

- **Event:** the Battle of the Broken Conclaves (Final Wall).
- **Perspectives:** Katharim memorial / Modern Orc honor recitation / exiled Tarran (Gray Matriarchy) Ledger.
- **Output:** `derived/multi-pov/battle-of-the-broken-conclaves-2026-05-11.md`. All three accounts in full, plus structured comparison.

### What the run produced

Three substantially distinct accounts that converge on facts and diverge on framing:

- **Katharim** — institutional memorial. Reverent, names-focused, refuses to assign cause for the failure ("the judgement of that failure belongs to others"). Equal honor to all three races.
- **Modern Orc** — Night-of-the-Gray-Wall ritual recitation. Bitter, oath-bound, draws practical law from the wound. The Wall as a *living rule of conduct*. Centers the Orug.
- **Tarran** — Ledger Wall record at Firethorn Hold. Self-accusing, militarily-informed, the only voice with the *why*: drafted-but-unsigned orders, seven theatres, an Emperor's hesitation. Claims the Aetherin as *theirs*.

All three independently name the failure-of-reinforcement. That convergence is the strongest possible canon signal — three voices including the responsible party itself agree on the fact.

### Tarran-account extrapolations (candidates for canon promotion)

The Tarran agent introduced internally-consistent specifics not yet in canon: the **Ledger Wall** (opposite the Boast Wall) at Firethorn Hold, the **Thorn-Daughter of Memory**, the **Empty Claim** ritual, the **Twelfth and Fifteenth Legions** at the **Citadel of Vethal**, the **Door of the Eleven**, and the Emperor's three documented possible reasons for not signing the reinforcement orders. These are extrapolations from existing Tarran/Gray Matriarchy canon and could be promoted to actual canon on [[firethorn-hold]] / [[gray-matriarchy]] if the user wants.

### Workflow note

This is the canonical use-case for `/multi-pov`: take an event the wiki documents and render it through multiple traditions to see how it's *remembered* differently. The output is **not canon** but is **canon-shaped raw material** — exactly the kind of thing a Tome would collect across centuries. Three artifacts of distinct voice, in parallel, in roughly the time it would take to write one in sequence.

The three skills installed this session (`/five-whys`, `/negative-space`, `/adversarial`, `/multi-pov`) form a coherent workflow toolkit:

- `/five-whys` — probe one element of canon for foundations
- `/negative-space` — find what's missing across the vault
- `/adversarial` — stress-test canon before commit
- `/multi-pov` — render an event across traditions

Pair them sensibly: negative-space → identifies thin events worth developing → multi-pov → renders perspectives → adversarial → tests the canon under those tellings.

### Pending follow-ups

- Item 7 (Game design intent) still awaits user direction.
- **[[divine-bureaucracy]]** / **[[dao]]** clarifications still queued from earlier today.
- **Tarran-account extrapolations** — user decides whether to canonize.
- **Human perspective on the Final Wall** — worth a future `/multi-pov` run; predicted asymmetry (Orcs know, Humans mostly don't) would be dramatic.

## 2026-05-11 (twenty-sixth) — Game design intent canonized (resolves item 7)

User picked option 1 from the three options offered: **canonize Dao's design intent for the Game**. This resolves the last open item from the /adversarial probe.

### Canon

The Game of the Gods is **designed by Dao for containment**, serving Roles 1 and 2 of his monitor function:
- Role 1 — ensure things run smoothly (gods absorbed in the Game don't over-intervene in mortal affairs)
- Role 2 — keep the macro balance (the most powerful pantheon in a magic-rich Mythos doesn't push outward into other Mythoi)

Canon at the **Tome-narrator level**, not at the in-Eadras-mortal-scholar level. Eadras inhabitants don't know this; the Tome does.

### Two-epistemic-level resolution

The apparent tension between Position-section confidence and Causation-section humility is resolved by recognising that the page operates at two epistemic levels:

- **Position section** speaks at Tome-narrator level (knows the Game's design intent canonically).
- **Causation section** speaks at Eadras-internal level (correctly notes that the gods don't know the answer, can't ask Dao, etc.).

Both are correct simultaneously. The Tome knows what its readers know; the in-Eadras characters do not.

### No page edits required

All relevant pages are already correctly framed:
- [[gods-of-eadras]] Position section — confident, now canon-correct.
- [[gods-of-eadras]] Causation section — epistemically humble about what's inside-Eadras-knowable.
- [[dao]] Role section — already states the Game serves Roles 1 and 2.

### All seven adversarial-probe items now resolved

| # | Issue | Disposition |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Independence of richness vs Well size | Committed canon update (twenty-third) |
| 2 | Unbounded vs bounded Godpower | Committed canon update (twenty-third) |
| 3 | Dao as primordial-tier? | Confirmed *no*; clarification added (twenty-third) |
| 4 | Expansionist gods default | Canonized via worship-as-power (twenty-fourth) |
| 5 | Bastion-radiation mechanism | Confirmed canon (twenty-fourth) |
| 6 | "Seven closest" count precision | Confirmed canon (twenty-fourth) |
| 7 | Game's design intent | Canonized as Dao's design (this entry) |

The Position section is now in stable canon form. The full *probe → user resolves → commit* loop is complete.

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/game-design-intent-canon-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures the canon decision, the two-epistemic-level resolution, the no-edits-needed disposition, and the full adversarial-probe item ledger.

## 2026-05-11 (twenty-seventh) — Ledger Wall canonized + Demon War timeline locked

User canonized the Ledger Wall (originally invented in the Tarran /multi-pov account) and locked precise Demon War timeline. The full *probe → multi-pov → user promotes elements to canon* loop is now demonstrated end to end.

### Canon — Ledger Wall

The Ledger Wall is the **Tarran institutional record of failures, debts, and unkept commitments** — the counterpart to the existing canonical Boast Wall.

- **Two locations**:
  1. **Original** — at the imperial capital of the [[firethorn-empire|Firethorn Empire]] on Eadras (pre-Banishment).
  2. **Surviving** — at [[firethorn-hold|Firethorn Hold]] on [[gaia|Prime-like Gaia]] (exile equivalent).
- **Animating doctrine**: *the office is the act* — a Tarran who claims an office (Protector, Steward, Emperor, Mother) and does not perform the act has failed both the office and its witnesses.
- **Central entry**: the failure to reinforce the [[battle-of-the-broken-conclaves|Final Wall]].
- **Custodian** (exile Wall): one of the [[thorn-sanctum|Seven Thorn-Daughters]] under the High Priestess-Mother. Specific title proposed in the multi-POV ("Thorn-Daughter of Memory") remains a candidate for explicit canon promotion.

### Canon — Demon War timeline

- **Duration**: **twenty years** total (precise, replacing the prior "at least five full years" framing).
- **Xar'vion's turn**: year 5 (existing canon preserved).
- **Battle of the Broken Conclaves (Final Wall)**: **year 15 of the twenty-year war**.
- **War's end**: approximately year 20 (sealing of the Demon Prince and closure of the major incursion).

### Page updates

- **`wiki/ledger-wall.md`** — new page (`canon_status: established`). Function, two locations, the Final Wall entry, cultural function, other entries, open-canon hooks.
- **[[firethorn-hold]]** — Sources + Last updated refreshed. New section *"The Ledger Wall and the Boast Wall"* added between *The Door of the Eleven* and *The Thorn Sanctum*. *What the Hold Contains* list updated to include Ledger Wall paired with the Boast Wall.
- **[[demon-war]]** — Sources + Last updated refreshed. Duration line updated from "at least five full years" to "twenty years"; Final Wall named as year 15.
- **[[battle-of-the-broken-conclaves]]** — Sources + Last updated refreshed. Context section opening updated to *"year 15 of the twenty-year war."*

### Raw session capture

- **`raw/ledger-wall-canon-2026-05-11.txt`** — captures both canon decisions, the workflow note about /multi-pov → canon promotion, the timeline reconciliation with Xar'vion's year-5 turn, and pending follow-ups.

### Workflow note

This canon decision is the direct downstream of running `/multi-pov` earlier today. The Tarran agent invented institutional apparatus (the Ledger Wall) that the user reviewed and selectively promoted to canon. Other multi-POV elements (the Thorn-Daughter of Memory title specifically, the 15th-year recitation ritual, the Twelfth and Fifteenth Legions at the Citadel of Vethal) remain as candidates for promotion but were not directly canonized this turn.

**The full skill-toolkit loop is now demonstrated end to end:** `/five-whys` (probe) → canon emerges → `/negative-space` (find thin areas) → `/multi-pov` (render across traditions) → user reviews → user promotes selected material to canon → wiki updated. The skills earn their keep across the full lifecycle.

### Pending follow-ups (added)

- **Imperial capital of the Firethorn Empire on Eadras** — no dedicated page yet; the original Ledger Wall's location-specific records depend on it.
- **Boast Wall** — canon at [[firethorn-hold]] but no dedicated page; worth one for cross-references from [[ledger-wall]].
- **Thorn-Daughter of Memory** — possible specific title for the Thorn-Daughter who keeps the Ledger Wall.
- **15th-year Maternal-Line reading ritual** — multi-POV-suggested; not yet formally canonized.
